Hiring Dwellings: Implicit Permissibility and Restrictions
Explains ruling on hiring dwellings with implicit permission for normal use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on hiring houses and shops for residence without specifying the use, and identify which trades are excluded due to structural harm.

Core Idea
Custom validates hiring dwellings for residence without specification, but trades that cause structural damage are implicitly prohibited.

This lesson from Al-Hidayah examines a practical scenario: hiring a house or shop without specifying the exact use. While strict analogy (qiyas) would require specification to avoid uncertainty, the Hanafi school adopts juristic preference (istihsan) based on custom. You will learn the ruling and its important restriction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is hiring (istījār) a house or shop for residence. The ruling is that the contract is valid (sahih) even without specifying the use.
The ruling is based on istihsan, overriding qiyas.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is istihsan (juristic preference) grounded in custom (urf). Custom indicates that the primary purpose of such premises is residence, which does not vary in its effect.
Istihsan is a secondary source in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Custom acts as an implied condition (mashrut dalālah). Because residence does not cause differential harm, the contract is valid without specification. Uncertainty (jahalah) is tolerated due to custom.
4
Note the restriction
The contract is implicitly restricted to non-damaging uses. Specific trades—blacksmith (haddād), washerman (qassār), and miller (tahhān)—are excluded because they cause apparent harm (darar zāhir) by weakening the building.
These trades involve heavy impact, water, or vibration.
5
Understand the ihtiyat
The Hanafi school adopts istihsan for practical ease, recognizing that specifying every use is burdensome. The restriction balances the hirer's freedom and the owner's right to protect the property.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجوز استيجار الدور والحوانيت للسكنى وان لم يبين ما يعمل فيها لان العمل المتعارف فيها السكني فينصرف اليه وانه لا يتفاوت فصح العقد وله ان يعمل كل شيء للاطلاق الا انه لا يُسكن حدادا ولا قصار اولا طحانا لان فيه ضررا ظاهرا لانه يوهن البناء فيتقيد العقد بما ورائها دلالة
He said: It is permissible to hire houses and shops for residence, even if he does not specify what he will do in them, because the customary use in them is residence, so it is directed to that, and it does not vary. So the contract is valid. And he may do everything due to the absolute nature (of the contract), except that he may not house a blacksmith, a washerman, or a miller, because in that there is apparent harm, as it weakens the building. So the contract is restricted to other than them by indication.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of Al-Hidayah on hiring houses and shops. The default ruling is permissibility (jawaz) for any normal residential purpose, without needing to specify the exact use. The proof is istihsan (juristic preference) based on custom (urf): people ordinarily use such premises for residence, and residence does not vary significantly in its impact. By contrast, qiyas (analogy) would require specification to avoid uncertainty (jahalah) in the subject matter. The hirer may engage in any activity that does not structurally damage the building. However, specific trades—blacksmithing, laundering, and milling—are prohibited because they cause visible harm (darar zahir) by weakening the structure. The contract is therefore implicitly restricted to non-damaging uses. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi.

Key Terms
استيجار (istījār): Taking property on rent; hiring for a benefit.
حداد (haddād): Blacksmith; one who works with fire and heavy tools, causing structural damage.
قصار (qassār): Washerman; one who launders clothes, which involves water and heavy pounding.
طحان (tahhān): Miller; one who grinds grain, causing vibrations and dust.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires a shop without specifying the use, which of the following activities is impermissible?
A) Using it as a residence for his family
B) Storing household goods
C) Housing a blacksmith
D) Setting up a small tailor shop

Key Takeaway
A hire contract for a dwelling is valid without specifying use, but trades that cause structural damage (e.g., blacksmith, washerman, miller) are implicitly prohibited.

Hiring Land for Agriculture: Implicit Rights and Crop Specification
Explains ruling on hiring land for farming with implicit water/path rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissibility of hiring land for agriculture, identify the implied water and path rights, and apply the requirement of crop specification or delegation of choice.

Core Idea
In hire for agriculture, water and path rights are automatic; crop must be specified or choice delegated to avoid disputes.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common transaction: hiring land for farming. It clarifies two crucial points: what rights are automatically included, and what must be stipulated to make the contract valid. Understanding these ensures both parties avoid litigation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type and its purpose
Recognize that the contract is ijarah (hire) of land for agriculture. The purpose is utilization (intifa') of the land for cultivation.
Hire is for benefit, not ownership of the land itself.
2
Recognize the implicit rights
The hirer automatically has the right to water (shurb) for irrigation and a path (tariq) to access the land. These are implied because utilization is impossible without them.
No stipulation needed; they enter the contract by default.
3
Contrast with sale contract
In a sale, these rights are not implied because the purpose is ownership of the corpus (tamlik al-raqabah), not immediate use. The text gives examples of selling a foal or marshy land.
Sale transfers ownership even if the thing cannot be used immediately.
4
Determine the crop specification requirement
The contract is not valid unless the specific crop to be grown is named. Different crops affect the land differently, so specification prevents disputes.
If not specified, uncertainty (jahalah) renders the contract fasid.
5
Understand the delegation exception
If the owner says 'cultivate whatever you wish,' the choice is delegated to the hirer. This removes uncertainty, so the contract becomes valid.
Delegation (khiyara) is an alternative to specification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجوز استيجار الاراضى للزراعة لانها منفعة مقصودة معهودة فيها وللمستاجر الشرب والطريق وان لم يشترط لان الاجارة تُعقد للانتفاع ولا انتفاع الا بهما فيدخلان في مطلق العقد بخلاف البيع لان المقصود منه ملک الرقبة لا الانتفاع فى الحال حتى يجوز بيع الجحش والارض السبخة دون الاجارة فلا يدخلان فيه من غير ذكر الحقوق وقد مر فى البيوع. ولا يصح العقد حتى يسمى ما يزرع فيها لانها قد تُستاجر للزراعة ولغيرها وما يُزرع فيها متفاوت فلابد من التعيين كيلا يقع المنازعة او يقول على ان يزرع فيها ما شاء لانه لما فوّض الخِيرة اليه ارتفعت الجهالة المفضية الى المنازعة
He said: It is permissible to hire lands for cultivation, because it is an intended and customary benefit therein. And the hirer has the right to water and path even if he did not stipulate, because the contract of hire is concluded for utilization, and utilization is not possible without them, so they are included in the absolute contract. This is contrary to sale, because the purpose of sale is ownership of the corpus, not immediate utilization. Thus, it is permissible to sell a foal or marshy land, but not to hire them. So they are not included in sale without mention of rights, and this has passed in the Book of Sales. And the contract is not valid until he specifies what he will cultivate in it, because lands may be hired for cultivation or for other purposes, and what is cultivated varies. So specification is necessary to prevent dispute. Or he says on condition that he cultivates whatever he wishes, because when he delegated the choice to him, the uncertainty leading to dispute is removed.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage covers two aspects of hiring land for agriculture. First, the contract is permissible because cultivation is a customary and intended benefit. The hirer automatically obtains rights to water (shurb) and path (tariq) without stipulation, since the purpose of the contract (intifa') cannot be realized without them. This differs from a sale, where the purpose is ownership of the corpus (tamlik al-raqabah), not immediate use—so such rights are not implied. The text gives the example of selling a foal or marshy land, which is permissible despite inability to use immediately, but hiring them would be invalid. Second, the contract is not valid unless the specific crop to be grown is named (e.g., wheat, barley) because different crops have different effects on the land; otherwise, disputes arise. However, if the owner says 'on condition that you cultivate whatever you wish,' the delegation of choice removes uncertainty (jahalah) and validates the contract. The last line from Sharih supports this requirement. The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
شرب (shurb): Right to water for irrigation of the hired land.
طريق (tariq): Right of way/path to access the hired land.
جحش (jahsh): Young donkey or horse; a foal that cannot be used immediately.
سبخة (sabkha): Marshy or saline land unsuitable for immediate cultivation or construction.
خيرة (khiyara): Choice; delegation of decision to the hirer regarding which crop to cultivate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When hiring land for agriculture, which of the following is necessary for the contract's validity?
A) Stipulating water rights in the contract
B) Specifying the crop to be grown
C) Both A and B
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Hiring land for agriculture is valid with automatic water and path rights, but the crop must be specified or the choice delegated to prevent disputes.

Ruling and Definition of Kitaba
Ruling and definition of kitaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of kitaba, explain the legal definition of a mukatab, and analyse the Hanafi argument for placing kitaba after ijara.

Core Idea
Kitaba frees the slave's hand immediately but his neck only upon payment.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, Imam al-Marghinani presents the ruling on the contract of kitaba – a unique contract where a slave is granted immediate permission to earn and will become fully free upon payment of a stipulated amount. The commentary then explores why this chapter follows ijara, defending the placement through structural analogy. You will also learn the linguistic and technical definitions of mukatab and kitaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
Read the matn: when the master makes his slave a mukatab for a specified property and the slave accepts, the slave becomes a mukatab. Note that the contract is valid (sahih) and produces immediate effects.
The conditions are: (1) offer from the master, (2) acceptance from the slave, (3) specification of the property (al-mal al-mashrut).
2
Understand the legal definition
The passage defines kitaba as 'freeing the hand immediately and the neck upon payment'. This means the slave acquires the right to earn and dispose of property immediately, but remains a slave in person until the payment is completed.
This is a key Hanafi distinction: partial freedom (hand) vs full freedom (neck).
3
Analyze the argument for chapter placement
The author justifies placing kitaba after ijara (lease) by qiyas: both contracts involve obtaining property (the slave's earnings) in exchange for something other than property (usufruct), requiring offer, acceptance, and mention of the exchange. Atqani's objection (that kitaba should follow itq because of wala') is refuted.
Focus on the illa: the transfer of usufruct while ownership of the person remains is common to ijara and kitaba.
4
Appreciate the linguistic derivation
The term 'mukatab' is derived from 'kitaba' meaning 'to gather'; it is a passive participle meaning 'one freed on condition of payment'. The concept is an Islamic innovation, first applied to Abu Maysara, slave of Umar (RA).
This shows the term's technical evolution and its basis in the Arabic language.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المكاتب
قال واذا كاتب عبده اوامه على مال شرطه عليه و قبل العبد ذلك صار مكاتبا ترجمہ ... جب مکاتب کیا اپنے غلام یا با ندی کو ایسے مال کے عوض جس کو اس پر شرط کیا ہے اور غلام نے اس کو قبول کر لیا تو وہ مکاتب ہو گیا۔
تشریح قوله كتاب ... الخ - بقول صاحب نہا یہ عقد اجارہ کے بعد عقد کتابت لانے کی مناسبت یہ ہے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک ایسا عقد ہے جس سے غیر مال کے مقابلہ میں مال اس طرح حاصل کیا جاتا ہے کہ اس میں ذکر عوض کے ساتھ اصلالہ ایجاب وقبول کی احتیاج ہوتی ہے اور علامہ اتقانی صاحب غایۃ البیان نے جو یہ کہا ہے کہ کتابت کو عناق کے بعد لانا چاہیے تھا اس واسطے کی کتابت کا مال ولاء ہے اور مال ولاء احکام عشق میں سے ہے۔ اسی لئے حاکم شہید نے کافی میں کتاب المکاتب اور کتاب ولاء کو کتاب العتاق کے بعد ذکر کیا ہے۔ یہ مناسب نہیں کیونکہ عتاق میں غلام کی ذات کو اپنی ملک سے بلا عوض نکالا جاتا ہے اور کتابت میں یہ بات نہیں ہے بلکہ اس میں ملک رقبہ ایک شخص کیلئے ہوتی ہے اور اس کی منفعت غیر کے لئے ہوتی ہے اور یہ بات اجارہ کے زیادہ مناسب ہے۔ لانه نسبة الذاتيات اولى من نسبته العرضيات ۔ رہا صاحب کافی کا ولاء کو ذکر کرنا سو وہ عناق کے ساتھ ولاء کی مناسبت کے بیان کے لئے ہے نہ کہ عقاق کے ساتھ مکاتب کی مناسبت کے بیان کے لئے ۔ قوله المكاتب ... الخ - لفظ مكاتب، کا تبہ مکاتبتہ سے اسم مفعول ہے بمعنی مال معین کی ادائیگی کی شرط پر آزاد کرنا اور یہ اصل میں كتب (ن) كتابہ سے ہے بمعنی جمع کرنا۔ چنانچہ لشکر کے ایک مجتی گروہ کو کتیبہ کہتے ہیں۔ اور اسی سے کتاب ہے کہ وہ جامع ابواب و فصول ہوتی ہے۔ ومنه يقال كتب النعل والقربة جواتے یا مشک کو دوہرے تسمہ سے ہی دیا۔ کافی و کفایہ وغیرہ میں اس کی شرعی اور اصطلاحی تعریف یوں کی گئی ہے : " الكتابة تحرير يدا في الحال و رقبة عند اداء المال غلام کو تصرف کے لحاظ سے بالفعل اور رقبہ کے اعتبار سے ادا ئیگی بدل کتابت کے بعد آزاد کرنے کو کتابت کہتے ہیں یعنی عقد کتابت کے بعد غلام تصرف کے بعد اعتبار سے آزاد ہو جاتا ہے بایں معنی کہ اس کو اپنی کمائی میں تصرف کا اختیار حاصل ہو جاتا ہے۔ لیکن رقبہ اور ذات کے اعتبار سے ادائیگی بدل کتابت کے بعد آزاد ہوتا ہے۔ گویا ملک ید بالفعل حاصل ہوتی ہے اور ملک رقبہ باعتبار انجام ۔ فائدہ علامہ دمیری نے شرح منہاج میں لکھا ہے کہ معنی مذکور میں کتابت ایک اسلامی لفظ ہے جو زمانہ جاہلیت میں معروف نہیں تھا۔ بقول بعض سب سے پہلے جس شخص کو مکاتب کیا گیا وہ حضرت عمر فاروق کا غلام ابومیہ تھا۔
قوله واذا كاتب الخ - علامہ عینی فرماتے ہیں کہ امام قدوری نے لفظ کا تب باب مفاعلت سے استعمال کیا ہے جو دو کے
The Book of Mukatab. He said: When he makes his male slave or female slave a mukatab for some property which he stipulates upon him, and the slave accepts that, he becomes a mukatab. Translation: When he makes his male slave or female slave a mukatab in exchange for property which he stipulates upon him, and the slave accepts it, then he becomes a mukatab. Commentary on the word 'Kitab': According to the author of al-Nihayah, the reason for bringing the contract of kitaba after the contract of ijara is that each of them is a contract by which property is obtained in exchange for something other than property, in such a way that it requires the mention of the exchange (iwad) along with the establishment of the contract (ijab and qabul). And what Allamah Atqani, author of Ghayat al-Bayan, said that kitaba should be brought after itq because the property of kitaba is wala' and wala' is among the rulings of liberation; therefore Hakim Shahid in al-Kafi mentioned Kitab al-Mukatab and Kitab al-Wala' after Kitab al-Itq. This is not appropriate because in itq the very being of the slave is removed from one's ownership without compensation, whereas in kitaba this is not the case; rather, in it the ownership of the body (raqaba) is for one person and its usufruct (manfa'ah) is for another, and this is more appropriate for ijara. 'Because the attribution of substances is prior to the attribution of accidents.' As for the mention of wala' by the author of al-Kafi, that is to explain the association of wala' with itq, not to show the association of kitaba with itq. Regarding the word 'al-mukatab': the word 'mukatab' is a passive participle from 'katabahu mukatabatan', meaning to free on the condition of payment of a specified property, and originally from 'kataba' meaning to gather. Thus a gathered group of an army is called a 'kutibah'. And from this comes 'kitab' because it gathers chapters and sections. And from it is said 'kutiba al-na'l wa al-qirbah' (the shoe or waterskin is stitched with double strips). In al-Kafi, al-Kifayah, etc., its legal and technical definition is given as: 'Kitaba is the freeing of the hand immediately and the neck upon payment of property', meaning: after the contract of kitaba, the slave becomes free with regard to disposal (tasarruf) immediately but free in his person (raqaba) after payment of the kitaba price. So the ownership of the hand is obtained immediately, and the ownership of the person is contingent upon completion. Benefit: Allamah Dumayri wrote in Sharh al-Minhaj that this meaning of kitaba is an Islamic term not known in pre-Islamic times. According to some, the first person to be made a mukatab was Abu Maysara, the slave of Umar al-Faruq. Regarding the statement 'wa idha kataba': Allamah Ayni says that Imam Quduri used the word 'kataba' from the form mufa'ala, which indicates two...
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the validity of the kitaba contract and provides a legal definition of the term 'mukatab'. The author begins with the matn from al-Hidayah: when a master makes his male or female slave a mukatab for a specified property (e.g., a sum of money) and the slave accepts, the contract is valid and the slave becomes a mukatab. This means he is granted immediate permission to earn and trade, but his full emancipation occurs only upon payment of the stipulated amount. The commentary then discusses why this chapter is placed after the chapter on ijara (lease). The reason is that both contracts involve the exchange of property (the slave's earnings) for something other than property (the slave's usufruct), and both require offer and acceptance. The scholar Atqani argued that kitaba should follow the chapter on itq (emancipation) because the price of kitaba is considered a form of wala' (clientage), which is an effect of itq. However, the commentator refutes this: in itq, the slave is freed without any payment, whereas in kitaba, the master retains ownership of the slave's person until payment. This makes kitaba analogous to ijara, where the owner transfers usufruct while retaining ownership. Thus the placement after ijara is more appropriate. The passage then defines the word 'mukatab' literally and technically. Literally, it means 'one who is freed on condition of payment', derived from 'kitaba' meaning 'to gather'. Technically, it means 'freeing the hand immediately and the neck upon payment'—i.e., the slave gains the ability to earn and dispose of property immediately, but becomes fully free only after paying the agreed amount. A benefit (fa'idah) is mentioned: the term 'kitaba' is an Islamic coinage, not known in pre-Islamic Arabia. The first person to be made a mukatab was Abu Maysara, a slave of Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him). Finally, the commentary notes that Imam al-Quduri used the form 'kataba' from the mufa'ala pattern, indicating that the contract occurs between two parties (the master and the slave).

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has been made a mukatab by his master through a contract of kitaba; he gains permission to earn and will become free upon payment of the stipulated property.
كتابة (kitaba): A contract whereby the master stipulates that the slave will pay a specified amount of property and then become free, and the slave is permitted to earn immediately. The text defines it as 'freeing the hand immediately and the neck upon payment of property.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, after a slave becomes a mukatab, what happens to his ability to earn and his freedom?
A) He becomes completely free immediately.
B) He is permitted to earn immediately but becomes free only after paying the stipulated amount.
C) He must be freed immediately and pay later.
D) He is not allowed to earn until he pays.

Key Takeaway
Kitaba is a valid contract that grants the slave immediate earning capacity but conditional full freedom, distinguished from both full emancipation (itq) and pure hire (ijara) by its unique combination of immediate hand freedom and deferred neck freedom.

Ruling on the Permissibility of Kitabah and the Nature of the Command
Explaining the legal ruling on kitabah and the nature of the Quranic command.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the Quranic command for kitabah is mustahabb (recommended) rather than wajib (obligatory) or mubah (permissible), and state the evidence and the condition that determines its recommendation.

Core Idea
The Quranic command for kitabah is recommended, not obligatory, because the condition 'if you know good' would be meaningless if it were merely permissible.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, the author addresses a key fiqh question: is the Quranic command to grant kitabah (a contract of manumission) obligatory or merely recommended? By examining the verse and its condition, and by invoking scholarly consensus, the Hanafi school establishes that the command is for recommendation (nadb), rejecting both obligation and pure permissibility. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to how a condition can shift the default meaning of an imperative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is kitabah – the contract between master and slave for gradual emancipation. Determine its hukm level in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is Quran 24:33: 'So contract them if you know good in them.' Note that the dalil is qat'i in transmission (Quran) but zanni in indication (dalala) due to the condition.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form (amr) normally indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. However, the attached condition 'if you know good' would be superfluous if the act were merely permissible (mubah) – it only has legal effect if it elevates the act to recommendation. Thus the command is for nadb.
This is the core Hanafi argument: the condition gives meaning only if the ruling is above ibaha.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Dawud al-Zahiri, Imam Ahmad, and a few others consider the command obligatory. Their evidence is the apparent imperative without qualification. The Hanafi response is that the condition and consensus shift it to nadb.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position is mustahabb (recommended). The majority of fuqaha (Hanafi, Maliki, Shafi'i) hold this view. The condition prevents ibaha, and ijma prevents wujub.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers the nadb view, and it is the established madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المكاتب
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳
درمیان مقتضی اشتراک ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ آقا اپنی طرف سے حق نامہ لکھتا ہے اور غلام قسطوں کی ادائیگی ۔ اس لحاظ سے اصل فعل میں دونوں مشترک ہیں ، پس آقا مکاتب بالکسر ہے اور غلام مكاتب بالفتح۔
مکاتب بنانے کی شرعی حیثیت
اما الجواز فلقوله تعالى فكاتبوهم ان علمتم فيهم خيرالله وهذا ليس امر ایجاب باجماع بين الفقهاء وانما هو امر ندب هو الصحيح ففى الحمل على الاباحة الغاء الشرط اذهو مباح بدونه اما الندبية فمعلقة به والمراد بالخير المذكور على ما قيل ان لا يضر بالمسلمين بعد العتق فان كان يضر بهم فالافضل ان لا يكاتبه وان كان يصح لو فعله واما اشتراط قبول العبد فلانه مال يلزمه فلابد من التزامه
ترجمہ بہر حال جائز ہونا سوارشاد باری کی وجہ سے ہے تو ان کو لکھ کر دے دو اگر سمجھو ان میں کچھ نیکی اور یہ امر ایجاب نہیں باجماع فقہا، بلکہ امر استحباب ہے یہی صحیح ہے پیس اباحت پر محمول کرنے میں شرط کو خو کرنا ہے کیونکہ کتابت تو اس کے بغیر بھی مباح ہے رہا استحباب سودہ شرط کے ساتھ معلق ہے۔ اور خیر مذکور سے مراد جیسا کہا گیا ہے یہ ہے کہ غلام آزادی کے بعد مسلمانوں کو نقصان نہ پہنچائے اگر وہ ان کے لئے مضر ہو تو افضل یہ ہے کہ اس کو مکاتب نہ کرے اگر چہ صحیح ہو جائے گا اگر کر لیا۔ رہا غلام کے قبول کرنے کا شرط ہونا سو اس لئے کہ وہ مال ہے جو اس کو لازم ہو گا تو اس کا التزام ضروری ہے۔
تشریح قوله الجواز الخ - عقد کتابت کے جواز کی دلیل حق تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے ”فـكــاتبـوهـم ان علمتم فيهم خیرا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی کا غلام یا لونڈی کہے کہ میں اتنی مدت میں اس قدر مال تجھ کو کما دوں تو مجھے آزاد کر دے تو مالک کو چاہیئے کہ قبول کرلے اور لکھ دے جب کہ وہ سمجھے کہ واقعی اس غلام یا لونڈی کے حق میں آزادی بہتر ہوگی ۔ قید غلامی سے چھوٹ کر چوری یا بد کاری اور طرح طرح کی بدمعاشیاں کرتا نہ پھرے گا۔ سعید بن منصور نے حضرت ام سلمہ سے روایت کی ہے۔ ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: اذا كان لاحد اكن مکاتب فملک ما یو ڈی فلتحتجب منه وفيه احادیث كثيرة سواه نیز کتابت کی مشروعیت پر امت کا اجماع ہے۔ قوله وهذا ليس الخ -- مذکورہ آیت میں کاتبوا امر وجوب کے لئے ہو یا غیر وجوب کیلئے بہر صورت عقد امر با جماع فقہاء حسن شعمی سفیان ثوری، امام مالک، امام شافعی وغیرہ حکم ایجابی نہیں بلکہ حکم مندوب ہے۔
قوله باجماع بين الفقهاء .... الخ - تاج الشريعة ، صاحب معراج و صاحب کفایہ وغیرہ نے کہا ہے کہ اجماع فقہاء کی قید کے ذریعہ۔ داؤد ظاہری اصفہانی، اس کے متبعین ، عمرو بن دینار ، ضحاک، اسحاق عطاء اور امام احمد وغیرہ کے قول سے احتراز ہے کہ امر مذکور ایجابی ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر کوئی غلام اپنے آقا سے مکاتبہ کی درخواست کرے اور آقا اس میں خیر سمجھے تو اس کو مکاتب کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اس پر یہ اشکال ہوتا ہے کہ صاحب کشاف نے آیت مذکورہ کی تفسیر میں کہا ہے۔
و هذا الامر للندب عند عامة العلماء وعن الحسن ليس ذاك بعزم ان شاء كاتب وان شاء لم يكاتب وعن عمر هي عزمة من عزمات الله وعن ابن سيرين مثله وهو مذهب داؤد اهـ.
پس حضرت عمر جو فقہ و روایت میں مشہو راجلہ صحابہ میں سے ہیں اور حضرت ابن سیرین جو اعیان تابعین اور کبار فقہاء میں سے ہیں۔ جب ان کے نزدیک امر مذ کو برائے وجوب ہے تو اجماع فقہاء کا دعویٰ کیسے صحیح ہو سکتا ہے؟
جواب یہ ہے کہ کشاف کا مذکورہ مضمون صرف اس پر دال ہے کہ اس امر کا برائے وجوب ہونا ان حضرات سے مروی ہے نہ یہ کہ ان کا مقرر مذہب یہی ہے کہ کتابت و ابنب ہے حالانکہ صاحب ہدایہ کا کلام اس پر مبنی ہے جو فقہاء کا مقر ر مذ ہب ہے۔ قوله هو الصحيح ... الخ - ہوا نح کہہ کر ہمارے بعض مشائخ کے اس قول سے احتراز ہے کہ امر مذکور برائے اباحت ہے نہ کہ برائے ندب جیسے آیت واذ احلتم فاصطا دوا، فاذا قضيت الصلوة فانتشرو افى لارض وابتغو امن فضل الله “ میں ہے۔ وجہ احتراز یہ ہے کہ اباحت پر محمول کرنے میں شرط ان علمتم فيهم خيرا “ کا لغو ہونا لازم آتا ہے یعنی یہ شرط بے فائدہ ہو جاتی ہے حالانکہ کلام الہی اس سے منزہ ہے ) اس لئے کہ کتابت تو اس شرط کے بغیر بھی مباح ہے رہا اس کا مندوب ہونا ( جو مباح سے بڑھ کر ہے) سو وہ اس شرط کے ساتھ وابستہ ہے پس مندوب ہونے میں شرط کا فائدہ ہے تو اس پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔
Book of Mukatab. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu Commentary of Hidaya Volume 13. Between the two, a contractual relationship exists because the master writes the contract from his side and the slave pays the installments. In this respect, in the actual action, both are partners: the master is mukatib (the one who contracts) and the slave is mukatab (the one contracted). The Shar'i status of making a mukatab: As for permissibility, due to the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'So contract them if you know good in them.' This is not a command of obligation by consensus of the fuqaha; rather it is a command of recommendation (nadb) – that is correct. For carrying it upon permissibility (ibaha) would nullify the condition, because kitabah is permissible without it. As for recommendation, it is attached to the condition. The meaning of 'khair' mentioned, according to what has been said, is that he does not harm the Muslims after emancipation. If he would harm them, it is better not to contract him, although it would be valid if he did. As for the condition of the slave's acceptance, it is because it is wealth that becomes obligatory upon him, so his commitment is necessary. Commentary: The evidence for the permissibility of the contract of kitabah is the command of Allah the Exalted: 'So contract them if you know good in them.' The point is that if someone's slave or maid-servant says, 'I will earn for you such and such wealth in such a period, then free me,' the owner should accept and write the contract when he thinks that freedom is indeed better for that slave or maid-servant. [He should ensure that] after being freed from the shackles of slavery, he does not go around stealing, committing wickedness, and various kinds of mischief. Sa'id bin Mansur narrated from Umm Salamah: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: If one of you has a mukatab and he possesses enough to pay, then let her observe hijab from him.' There are many other hadith besides this. Also, there is consensus of the Ummah on the legitimacy of kitabah. His saying: 'This is not a command of obligation...' – in the mentioned verse, 'write contract' is a command – whether it is for obligation or non-obligation, in any case, by consensus of the fuqaha: Hasan al-Basri, Sufyan al-Thawri, Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, etc., it is not obligatory but recommended. His saying: 'by consensus of the fuqaha...' – Taj al-Shari'ah, the author of al-Mi'raj and the author of al-Kifayah said that by the phrase 'consensus of the fuqaha' they intend to exclude the view of Dawud al-Zahiri al-Isfahani, his followers, 'Amr bin Dinar, al-Dahhak, Ishaq, 'Ata', and Imam Ahmad, etc., who hold that the mentioned command is obligatory, to the extent that if a slave asks his master for kitabah and the master sees good in him, it is necessary to contract him. An objection is raised: The author of al-Kashshaf said in the interpretation of the mentioned verse: 'This command is for recommendation according to the general scholars. From al-Hasan: It is not a firm resolve; if he wishes he contracts, if he wishes he does not contract. From 'Umar: It is a determination from the determinations of Allah. From Ibn Sirin similarly. And this is the madhhab of Dawud.' Then [on page 118]: Hazrat 'Umar, who is well-known in jurisprudence and narration among the senior Companions, and Hazrat Ibn Sirin, who is among the distinguished Tabi'un and senior fuqaha – when in their view the mentioned command is for obligation, how can the claim of consensus of the fuqaha be correct? The answer is that the mentioned content of al-Kashshaf only indicates that the view of obligation is narrated from these personalities, not that it is their established madhhab that kitabah is [obligatory], whereas the statement of the author of al-Hidayah is based on what is the established madhhab of the fuqaha. His saying: 'and it is correct...' – by saying 'correct' he excludes the view of some of our mashayikh that the mentioned command is for permissibility (ibaha), not for recommendation (nadb), as in the verse 'and when you are halal, then hunt' and 'when the prayer is concluded, then disperse in the land and seek of Allah's bounty.' The reason for exclusion is that carrying it upon ibaha would render the condition 'if you know good in them' meaningless – i.e., this condition becomes useless, whereas the speech of Allah is free from that because kitabah is permissible without this condition. As for its being recommended (which is higher than ibaha), that is attached to the condition. So the benefit of the condition is in the recommendation, so it is carried upon that.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a detailed fiqh commentary on the opening of Kitab al-Mukatab. It first establishes the linguistic meaning: mukatib is the master, mukatab is the slave, because they both participate in the contract. The main ruling is that the Quranic command 'fakatibuhum' (so contract them) is not obligatory (wajib) by scholarly consensus (ijma'), but rather recommended (mustahabb/nadb). The author explains why it cannot be merely permissible (mubah) because then the condition 'if you know good in them' would be superfluous since kitabah is mubah even without it. The condition only makes sense if it elevates the act to recommendation. The meaning of 'khair' (good) is interpreted as the slave not harming Muslims after freedom, which aligns with the Maqasid of protecting the community. A narrration from Umm Salamah is cited to show the effect on hijab. The passage then confronts an objection: if 'Umar and Ibn Sirin thought it was wajib, how can there be consensus? The answer is that these are isolated reports not their established madhhab; the established position of the fuqaha is that it is nadb. The Hanafi position is clear: kitabah is recommended when the slave is trustworthy, but permissible even if not, though better avoided. The author also references that Imam Ahmad and others consider it obligatory but this is rejected by the majority.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract (kitabah) with his master to pay a sum of money in installments in exchange for his freedom.
كتابة (kitabah): A contract between a master and his slave whereby the slave agrees to pay a specified amount of money in installments, after which he becomes free.
ندب (nadb): A legal recommendation; an act that is rewarded but not sinful to leave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the Quranic command 'fakatibuhum' considered for recommendation (nadb) rather than obligation (wujub) or mere permissibility (ibaha)?
A) Because the condition 'if you know good in them' would be meaningless if the act were merely permissible, as kitabah is permissible even without the condition.
B) Because the verse is abrogated by another verse.
C) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not practice it himself.
D) Because there is consensus that it is forbidden.

Key Takeaway
Kitabah is mustahabb (recommended) when the slave is likely to be good after freedom; the condition in the verse prevents it from being wajib or merely mubah.

Meaning of Khair and Condition of Slave's Acceptance in Kitabah
Explaining the interpretation of 'khair' in the verse and why the slave must accept the kitabah contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi interpretation of 'khair' in the Kitabah verse and explain why the slave's acceptance is a condition for the validity of the contract.

Core Idea
'Khair' means the slave will not harm Muslims after freedom; its absence does not invalidate the contract.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses two key issues regarding the contract of kitabah. First, it clarifies the meaning of 'khair' (goodness) mentioned in the Quranic verse, presenting various interpretations from the Salaf and settling on a maqasid-oriented view. Second, it explains why the slave's explicit acceptance is a necessary condition for the contract's validity. Understanding these points helps distinguish between conditions of validity and recommendations for optimal practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Locate the term 'khair' in the passage and note that it is subject to multiple interpretations from the Companions and early scholars. List the main interpretations: earning ability, trustworthiness, piety, and the composite view that the slave will not harm Muslims.
2
Determine the preferred interpretation and its legal weight
Identify that al-Hidayah prefers the interpretation that 'khair' means the slave will not harm Muslims after emancipation. Recognize that this is a condition for recommendation (nadb), not for validity. The passage states that if the slave lacks 'khair', it is better not to contract, but if contracted, it is permissible without dislike.
This is a key distinction between a condition of validity and a condition of optimal practice.
3
Analyze the cross-madhhab disagreement on 'khair'
Note that Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i agree with the Hanafi view that contracting without 'khair' is permissible without dislike, while Imam Ahmad, Ishaq, and others consider it makruh. Understand that the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is whether the act is considered disliked or not.
4
Examine the condition of the slave's acceptance
The passage states that the slave's acceptance is necessary for the validity of kitabah because the contract imposes a financial obligation (mal) on the slave. Without consent, the obligation cannot be binding. The three Hanafi imams are unanimous on this.
This is a condition for validity (shart al-sihhah), not merely recommendation.
5
Synthesize the two rulings
Combine the two findings: 'khair' is a recommendation, while acceptance is a condition. A valid kitabah requires the slave's acceptance but does not require the slave to possess 'khair'. If 'khair' is absent, it is still valid, though it is better to avoid such a contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله والمراد بالخير .... الخ - آیت مذکورہ میں خیر آیا ہے اس کی تفسیر حضرت ابن عباس ، ابن عمر ، زید بن اسلم اور حضرت عطاء سے حرضت وقوت ادا یعنی کسب ( و کمائی ) اور سفیان ثوری وحسن بصری سے امانت و دین، مجاہد، طاؤس ، ابو صالح اور ابراہیم نختی سے مال وصلاح ، صدق و وفا ، امانت وادار منقول ہے صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بقول بعض خیر سے مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ غلام آزاد ہونے کے بعد مسلمانوں کو ضرر نہ پہنچائے۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ اگر وہ امین و دیندار اور کمائی کرنے والا نہ ہو تو وہ مسلمانوں کے حق میں مضر ہی ہوگا۔ تو اس صورت میں افضل ہے کہ اس کو مکاتب نہ کرے۔ لیکن اگر کر ہی دیا تو بلا کراہت جائز ہوگا۔ امام مالک اور امام شافعی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ البتہ امام احمد ، اسحاق ، ابوالحسین بن القطان شافعی کے نزدیک مکروہ ہے۔ قوله واما اشتراط ... الخ - غلام کے قبول کرنے کی شرط اس لئے ہے کہ کتابت کی وجہ سے اس کے ذمہ مال لا زم ہوگا تو یہ ضروری ہے کہ وہ اپنے ذمہ لازم ہونا قبول کرے۔ ائمہ ثلاثہ بھی اس کے قائل ہیں۔
His saying: 'and the meaning of khair...' – In the mentioned verse, 'khair' appears. Its interpretations are narrated: from Ibn 'Abbas, Ibn 'Umar, Zayd bin Aslam, and 'Ata': strength and ability to pay (i.e., earning). From Sufyan al-Thawri and al-Hasan al-Basri: trustworthiness and religion. From Mujahid, Tawus, Abu Salih, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: wealth and righteousness, truthfulness and fidelity, trustworthiness and piety. The author of al-Hidayah says: According to some, the meaning of khair is that the slave does not harm the Muslims after emancipation. It is obvious that if he is not trustworthy, religious, and earning, he will be harmful to the Muslims. In that case, it is better not to contract him. But if he does contract him, it is permissible without dislike (karahah). Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i also hold this view. However, according to Imam Ahmad, Ishaq, and Abul Husayn bin al-Qattan al-Shafi'i, it is disliked (makruh). His saying: 'and as for the condition of acceptance...' – The condition of the slave's acceptance is because kitabah imposes a financial obligation on him, so it is necessary that he accept the obligation on himself. The three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) also hold this view.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage clarifies two sub-issues. First, the meaning of 'khair' (good) in the Quranic verse. The author mentions multiple interpretations from the Salaf, ranging from earning ability to trustworthiness and piety. Then he presents the preferred view of al-Hidayah (and some others) that khair means the slave will not harm Muslims after freedom. This is a Maqasid-oriented interpretation focusing on public welfare. If the slave would cause harm, it is better not to contract him, but if contracted, it is valid. The author notes that Malik and Shafi'i agree, while Ahmad and others deem it makruh. Second, the passage explains why the slave's acceptance is a condition for kitabah: because the contract makes a financial obligation (mal) binding on him, which requires his explicit consent. The three Imams (the Hanafi school's founders) are unanimous on this point.

Key Terms
خير (khair): Goodness in the slave that makes kitabah recommendable; specifically, that he will not harm Muslims after freedom, interpreted as trustworthiness, earning ability, and piety.
قبول (qabul): The slave's verbal acceptance of the kitabah contract, which is necessary for its validity because it imposes a financial obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hidayah's preferred interpretation, what is the meaning of 'khair' in the verse 'if you know good in them'?
A) The slave must be wealthy.
B) The slave will not harm Muslims after emancipation.
C) The slave must be a scholar.
D) The slave must have a specific skill.

Key Takeaway
The slave's acceptance is a condition for kitabah's validity; 'khair' is only a recommendation for optimal practice.

Mukatab is Not Freed Until Full Payment of the Price
Establishing that the mukatab remains a slave until he pays the entire kitabah price, with hadith evidence and Companions' ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a mukatab becomes free and explain the hadith evidence that proves full payment is required.

Core Idea
A mukatab remains a slave until he pays every dirham of the kitabah price—partial payment does not free him.

This passage establishes a key rule in the law of kitabah: a slave who enters into a mukatab contract does not become free incrementally. Even if he pays most of the agreed sum, he remains in slavery until the last dirham is paid. The author cites two hadith and notes a difference among the Companions, then confirms that the Hanafi school follows the view of Zayd ibn Thabit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the first line: 'He is not freed except by paying the entire price.' That is the core legal statement.
The ruling applies to the mukatab's status, not the validity of the contract.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
Two hadith are given. The first says if a mukatab pays all but ten dinars, he is still a slave. The second says the mukatab is a slave as long as even one dirham remains. These are clear textual proofs.
The hadith are ahad but their meaning (dalala) is qati' according to the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the Companions' ikhtilaf
The text mentions that there was ikhtilaf among the Companions. The commentary indicates that 'Umar and 'Uthman may have held a different view, but the Hanafi school adopts Zayd's view.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; the Hanafi tarjih is based on the explicit hadith.
4
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The author states 'what we have chosen is the saying of Zayd'. This is the operative ruling: full payment is necessary.
No intra-Hanafi disagreement exists on this point.

And he is not freed except by paying the entire price (badal kitabah), because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Any slave who is made a mukatab for one hundred dinars, then he pays all except ten dinars, he is still a slave.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as even one dirham remains unpaid.' There is ikhtilaf among the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) regarding this, and what we have chosen is the saying of Zayd (may Allah be pleased with him). Translation: He will not be freed except by paying the entire kitabah price, because the Prophet's command: 'Any slave who is made a mukatab for one hundred dinars, then he pays all except ten dinars, he is still a slave.' And the Prophet said: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as even one dirham remains unpaid.' Regarding this, there is ikhtilaf among the Companions, and what we have chosen is the saying of Zayd ibn Thabit. Commentary: According to us (the Hanafis), the slave is mukatab only when he has paid the entire kitabah price. 'Umar, 'Uthman...
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that a mukatab does not become free until he pays the entire stipulated price in full. Two hadiths are cited: (1) If a mukatab pays all but ten dinars, he remains a slave. (2) The mukatab is a slave as long as even one dirham remains. The author notes that there was ikhtilaf among the Companions on this issue. Some Companions (e.g., 'Umar, 'Uthman, as the commentary begins to list) may have held that partial payment effects partial freedom, but the Hanafi school adopts the view of Zaid ibn Thabit, which is that freedom only occurs upon full payment. This ruling is consistent with the principle that the debt of kitabah is like any other debt until fully discharged, and the slave's status does not change incrementally. The proof is from clear hadith.

Key Terms
بدل کتابت (badal al-kitabah): The price or sum of money that the mukatab agrees to pay in installments in exchange for his freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this lesson, what is the status of a mukatab who has paid all but ten dinars of his kitabah price?
A) He becomes free because he paid most of it.
B) He remains a slave until he pays the remaining ten dinars.
C) He becomes free but must pay the ten dinars as a debt.
D) The contract is nullified and he returns to being a full slave.

Key Takeaway
The mukatab is not freed until he pays the entire kitabah price; partial payment does not change his slave status.

The Command for Kitabah: Mustahabb, Not Wajib
Explains the Hanafi ruling on the nature of the command for kitabah and the condition of the slave's acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the Quranic command for kitabah is mustahabb rather than wajib, and identify the condition (khayr) that supports this view.

Core Idea
The Quranic condition 'if you know good in them' shows the command for kitabah is recommended, not obligatory.

The Quran commands masters to write kitabah for slaves who request it. Is this command obligatory, recommended, or merely permissible? The Hanafi school, relying on the internal evidence of the condition 'khayr', argues that it must be mustahabb (recommended). This lesson explores the reasoning, contrasts it with other scholarly positions, and clarifies the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic command and its condition
Locate the verse (Surah al-Nur, 24:33) where Allah commands kitabah with the condition 'if you know good in them' (khayr). Understand that the imperative form alone does not settle the issue.
2
Understand the spectrum of positions
Recall that scholars differ: some (Umar, Ibn Sirin) considered it wajib; others (Imam Ahmad) makruh; the Hanafi school says mustahabb; some earlier Hanafi mashayikh said mubah.
The Hanafi position avoids both extremes.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof from the condition
If the command were mubah, the condition 'khayr' would be futile because kitabah is permissible even without khayr. To give meaning to the condition, the command must be for recommendation, where khayr is a relevant criterion.
This is a linguistic-legal argument (wajh al-dalalah).
4
Compare with the counterarguments
Examine the opposing views: those who claim wajib rely on the imperative's apparent force; those who claim makruh fear harm from the slave. The Hanafi response: Umar and Ibn Sirin's view is a narration, not their established madhhab; harm is addressed by the very condition of khayr.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the Hanafi view, kitabah is recommended but not obligatory; it is valid even without khayr, though better with it. Under Imam Ahmad's view, it is disliked if khayr is absent. The difference affects the master's reward and the permissibility of the act.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

قوله واما اشتراط ... الخ - غلام کے قبول کرنے کی شرط اس لئے ہے کہ کتابت کی وجہ سے اس کے ذمہ مال لا زم ہوگا تو یہ ضروری ہے کہ وہ اپنے ذمہ لازم ہونا قبول کرے۔ ائمہ ثلاثہ بھی اس کے قائل ہیں۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 12. Book of the Mukatab. Then Hadrat Umar, who is among the famous jurists and narrators of the Companions, and Hadrat Ibn Sirin, who is among the eminent Tabi'un and great jurists. When in their view the mentioned command is for obligation, then how can the claim of consensus of the jurists be correct? The answer is that the mentioned content of Kashshaf only indicates that this command being for obligation is narrated from them, not that their established madhhab is that kitabah is obligatory, whereas the statement of Sahib al-Hidayah is based on what is the established madhhab of the jurists. His saying: 'it is the correct one' etc. - By saying 'huwa' he avoids the saying of some of our mashayikh that the mentioned command is for permissibility not for recommendation, like in the verse 'And when you have completed the pilgrimage, then hunt' and 'And when the prayer is concluded, then disperse in the land and seek of Allah's bounty'. The reason for avoidance is that carrying it upon permissibility would necessitate the condition 'if you know good in them' becoming futile, i.e. this condition becomes useless, whereas the speech of Allah is free from this. Hence, kitabah is also permissible without this condition; as for its being recommended (which is higher than permissible), it is tied to this condition. So in recommendation, the condition has benefit, so it will be carried upon it. His saying: 'and the meaning of khayr' etc. - In the mentioned verse, 'khayr' appears. Its interpretation from Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar, Zayd ibn Aslam, and Ata is strength and ability to pay, i.e., earning. From Sufyan al-Thawri and Hasan al-Basri is trustworthiness and religion. From Mujahid, Tawus, Abu Salih, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i is wealth and righteousness, truthfulness and fulfillment, trustworthiness and discipline. Sahib al-Hidayah says that according to some, the meaning of 'khayr' is that the slave should not cause harm to Muslims after being freed. It is obvious that if he is not trustworthy, religious, and earning, he will be harmful for Muslims. In that case, it is better not to make him a mukatab, but if he does, it is permissible without detestability. Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i also hold this view. However, according to Imam Ahmad, Ishaq, and Abu al-Husayn ibn al-Qattan al-Shafi'i, it is makruh. His saying: 'and as for the condition' etc. - The condition of the slave's acceptance is because due to kitabah, wealth becomes obligatory on him, so it is necessary that he accepts it being obligatory on himself. The Three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) also hold this view.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah addresses two key issues concerning the contract of kitabah (a slave's contract for freedom). First, it clarifies the nature of the command in the Quranic verse (Surah al-Nur, 24:33) to write kitabah for slaves who seek it. Some scholars, including Hadrat Umar and Ibn Sirin, understood the command as obligatory (wajib). However, the Hanafi school, supported by the majority, holds that it is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib. The proof lies in the condition 'if you know good in them' (khayr). If the command were for permissibility (ibaha), the condition would be futile since kitabah is permissible even without good. The condition adds benefit only when the command is for recommendation. This reasoning rebuts any claim of consensus on obligation. The text also explores the meaning of 'khayr', quoting various early authorities—ranging from earning ability to trustworthiness and piety. Sahib al-Hidayah prefers the interpretation that 'khayr' means the slave will not harm Muslims after freedom, which encompasses religiosity and earning capacity. Here, different schools diverge: Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i agree with the Hanafi position that kitabah is permissible without dislike (karahah), while Imam Ahmad, Ishaq, and some others consider it makruh (disliked). The second issue is the condition of the slave's acceptance. Kitabah imposes a financial obligation on the slave, so the slave's acceptance is necessary for the contract's validity. This is agreed upon by the Hanafi school and the other three imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad).

Key Terms
کتابت (kitabah): A contract between a master and his slave whereby the slave earns freedom by paying a specified sum in installments.
خیر (khayr): In this passage, khayr means that the slave will not harm Muslims after being freed, encompassing trustworthiness, religiosity, and earning capacity.
مندوب (mandub): A recommended act that is not obligatory; performing it brings reward, but omitting it is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the nature of the command for kitabah in the Quran?
A) It is obligatory (wajib).
B) It is recommended (mustahabb).
C) It is merely permissible (mubah).
D) It is disliked (makruh).

Key Takeaway
The condition 'khayr' shifts the Quranic command for kitabah from mere permissibility to recommendation, making it mustahabb but not wajib, and this is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Mukatab Does Not Become Free Until Full Payment
States the ruling that the mukatab is not free until he pays the entire kitabah price, with Hadith proofs and Sahaba ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a mukatab becomes free, cite the hadith proof, and explain the tarjih among the Sahaba ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
A mukatab is not free until he pays every last dirham — partial payment does not grant freedom.

This passage clarifies a critical point in the kitabah contract: the precise moment the slave gains freedom. While some Companions considered partial payment sufficient, the Hanafi school, following Zayd ibn Thabit, insists on full payment based on explicit Prophetic hadith. We will examine the evidence and understand why this ruling is sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the kitabah contract. What is the ruling according to the Hanafi school? The mukatab does not become free until he pays the entire kitabah price.
The ruling is that freedom is conditional on full payment.
2
Locate the primary hadith proof
Find the hadith cited in the passage: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him.' Also the hadith about paying all but ten dinars. Note their chains (Amr ibn Shu'ayb, Umm Salamah).
Both hadiths are ahad but accepted by the majority.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
How do these hadiths prove the ruling? The explicit wording shows that any unpaid amount, however small, keeps the slave in bondage. The imperative to pay fully is implied.
The dalala is qati (decisive) even though thubut is zanni.
4
Note the Sahaba ikhtilaf and Hanafi tarjih
Some Companions (e.g., Umar in one report, Ibn Mas'ud) held that paying most of the price frees the mukatab or makes him a debtor. However, the Hanafi school chooses the view of Zayd ibn Thabit, which is supported by the hadiths and is the view of the majority of scholars.
Tarjih authority: Sahib al-Hidayah explicitly chooses Zayd's saying.

قوله وفيه اختلاف الصحابه .... الخ - یعنی مکاتب کب آزاد ہوگا ؟ اس کے بارے میں آثار صحابہ مختلف ہیں ۔ چنانچہ عبد الرزاق نے حضرت جابر بن سمرہ سے روایت کیا ہے۔ ان عمر بن الخطاب قال: اذا ادى المكاتب الا الشطر فلارق علیہ “ اور ابن شیبہ نے حضرت عمر سے اس کے خلاف یوں روایت کیا ہے ۔ " انه قال : المكاتب عبد مابقی علیه در هم نیز عید الرزاق نے حضرت عائشہ، زید بن ثابت ، ابن عمر، اور حضرت ام سلمہ سے بھی روایت کیا ہے اور حضرت ابن مسعودؓ سے روایت کیا ہے قال: اذا اذى قدر ثمنه فهو غريم اور حضرت ابن عباس سے روایت کیا ہے۔
قال : اذا بقى على المكاتب خمس اواق او خمس دود او خمسة أوسق فهو غريم. صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے عشق مکاتب کی بابت حضرت زید بن ثابت کا قول اختیار کیا ہے۔ جو مسند شافعی ومصنف عبد الرزاق و ابن ابی شیبہ اور سنن بیہقی میں مروی ہے۔ وذکرہ البخاری تعلیقاً ۔
The freedom of the mukatab will only be after payment of the kitabah price. He is not freed except by paying all the price, because the Prophet peace be upon him said: 'Any slave who is made a mukatab for one hundred dinars and pays all but ten dinars, he remains a slave.' And the Prophet peace be upon him said: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him.' And there is difference of opinion among the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. And what we have chosen is the saying of Zayd, may Allah be pleased with him. Translation: He will not be freed except by paying the full kitabah price, because the Prophet decreed that a slave made mukatab on a hundred dinars who pays all but ten dinars remains a slave, and the Prophet said: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him.' And there is disagreement among the Companions about this, and we have chosen the saying of Zayd ibn Thabit. Commentary on his saying: 'and he is not freed' etc. - According to us, a slave becomes a mukatab only when he pays the entire kitabah price. Umar, Uthman, Zayd ibn Thabit, Aisha, Umm Salama, Urwa ibn al-Zubayr, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, al-Zuhri, Qasim, Salim, Sulayman ibn Yasar, Ata, Qatada, Sufyan al-Thawri, al-Awza'i, Ibn Shihab, Ibn Abi Layla, Ishaq, Abu Thawr, Abu Sulayman, Imam Malik, Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Ahmad - in short, the majority of jurists hold this view. His saying: 'any slave' etc. - Its takhrij is by the authors of the four Sunan, al-Daraqutni, and al-Hakim from Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that the Prophet said: 'Any slave who is made a mukatab for one hundred uqiyas and pays all but ten uqiyas, he is a slave, and any slave who is made a mukatab for one hundred dinars...' The other hadith's takhrij is by Imam Abu Dawud through the mentioned chain from the Prophet: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham of the kitabah remains upon him.' And Ibn Adi in al-Kamil narrated it from Umm Salama that she said: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham or an uqiya remains upon him.' Also Imam Malik in al-Muwatta from Ibn Umar, and Ibn Abi Shayba from Umar, Uthman, Ali, Zayd ibn Thabit, and Aisha as a mauquf narration: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as anything of his kitabah remains upon him.' His saying: 'and there is difference of opinion among the Companions' etc. - i.e., when does the mukatab become free? Regarding this, the reports of the Companions differ. Thus, Abd al-Razzaq narrated from Jabir ibn Samura that Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'When the mukatab pays all but half, there is no recapture upon him.' And Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from Umar the opposite: 'He said: The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him.' Also Abd al-Razzaq narrated from Aisha, Zayd ibn Thabit, Ibn Umar, and Umm Salama. And from Ibn Mas'ud: 'He said: When he pays an amount equal to his value, he is a debtor.' And from Ibn Abbas: 'He said: When five uqiyas or five... or five wasqs remain upon the mukatab, he is a debtor.' Sahib al-Hidayah says: We have chosen the saying of Zayd ibn Thabit regarding the matter of the mukatab. It is narrated in Musnad al-Shafi'i, Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Abi Shayba, and Sunan al-Bayhaqi. And al-Bukhari mentioned it as a ta'liq.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage establishes a fundamental ruling of the Hanafi school: the mukatab (a slave under a kitabah contract) does not become free until he has paid the entire kitabah price, every last dirham. The proof comes from two hadiths of the Prophet (peace be upon him): the first states that if a mukatab pays all but ten dinars of a hundred, he remains a slave; the second states that the mukatab is a slave as long as even one dirham remains unpaid. These hadiths are narrated through reliable chains. The passage then notes that there was disagreement among the Companions on this issue. Some, like Umar, had a different view (e.g., that paying most of the price suffices for freedom). Others, like Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Abbas, considered the mukatab a debtor after paying a certain amount. However, the Hanafi school follows the view of Zayd ibn Thabit, which is also the view of the majority of Companions and later jurists, including the Four Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad). This view is that the mukatab remains a slave until full payment. The passage provides the chain of transmission for the hadiths and lists the many scholars who uphold this position. The reliance on Zayd's view is justified by its strength and widespread acceptance.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract with his master to earn his freedom by paying a specified sum.
بدل کتابت (badal al-kitabah): The price agreed upon in the kitabah contract that the slave must pay to the master for his freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling regarding the freedom of a mukatab?
A) He becomes free after paying half the price.
B) He becomes free after paying the full price.
C) He becomes free after paying an amount equal to his value.
D) He becomes free when the master declares it.

Key Takeaway
A mukatab does not become free until he pays the entire kitabah price; any remaining amount, however small, keeps him in slavery.

Freedom of the Mukatab Upon Payment Without Explicit Condition
Ruling that the mukatab becomes free upon payment even if the master did not explicitly condition freedom on payment, by analogy to sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the mukatab becomes free upon payment of the kitabah price without need for explicit condition, and explain the qiyas to sale.

Core Idea
Payment of the kitabah price itself frees the mukatab, as the contract's inherent consequence (muqtada al-'aqd), by analogy to sale.

In the Hanafi school, the kitabah contract (a contract of manumission by payment) inherently effects freedom upon full payment, even if the master never explicitly stated that payment would lead to freedom. This ruling is derived from the principle of muqtada al-'aqd (the contract's inherent consequence) and is supported by consensus of the majority, though Imam al-Shafi'i holds that an explicit conditional phrase is required. In this lesson, we will unpack the reasoning and explore the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the payment of the full kitabah price by a mukatab slave. The ruling under the Hanafi school is that he becomes free immediately upon payment, regardless of whether the master explicitly conditioned freedom on payment or even intended it.
The ruling applies even if the master said nothing about freedom or explicitly denied it.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to a sale contract. Just as ownership transfers in a sale upon payment of the price without needing explicit stipulation, so too does freedom transfer in kitabah upon payment without explicit condition.
The underlying principle is that the contract's inherent consequence (muqtada al-'aqd) is automatically established.
3
Understand the illa (effective cause)
The illa is that both sale and kitabah are commutative contracts where the consideration (price) is exchanged for a right (ownership or freedom). The contract's nature (muqtada al-'aqd) directly links payment to the right, making explicit stipulation unnecessary.
The illa is jaliyyah (clear) and extracted via tahrir al-manat.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Imam al-Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i requires the master to explicitly state a conditional phrase (e.g., 'I have made you a mukatab on condition that if you pay, you are free'). Without it, the mukatab does not become free even after payment.
The Shafi'i view is based on the idea that freeing a slave is a separate act of piety that cannot be implied from the contract alone.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Hanafi, the mukatab is freed upon payment and can then marry, inherit, etc. Under Shafi'i, he remains a slave until an explicit condition is fulfilled, potentially delaying his freedom and affecting his legal capacity.
The difference affects the mukatab's status, rights, and obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بدل کتابت ادا کرنے سے غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا اگر چہ آقا نے اس بات کی پہلے سے صراحت نہ کی ہو
ويعتق بادائه وان لم يقل المولى اذا اديتها فانت حر لان موجب العقديثبت من غير التصريح به كما في البيع ولا يجب حط شى من البدل اعتبار ابالبيع
ترجمہ اور آزاد ہو جائے گا بدل کتابت ادا کرنے سے اگر چہ آقا نے یہ نہ کہا ہو کہ جب تو ادا کر دے تو آزاد ہے۔ کیونکہ عقد کا موجب ثابت ہو جاتا ہے اس کی تصریح کے بغیر جیسے بیع میں ہے اور بدل کتابت سے کچھ کم کرنا ضروری نہیں بیع پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔ تشریح قوله ويعتق بادائه ... الخ جب مکاتب بدل کتابت ادا کر چکے تو وہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اگر چہ آ قانے یہ کہا ہو کہ جب بدل کتابت ادا کر دے تو تو آزاد ہے۔ نیز آقا نے کتابت سے اس کی آزادی کی نیت کی ہو یانہ کی ہو ۔ جو ہر نفی میں ابن بنٹ نعیم کی کتابت نوادر النفقہاء سے منقول ہے کہ اس کے جواز پر علماء کا اجماع ہے بجز امام شافعی کے ان کے یہاں آزاد نہ ہوگا یہاں تک کہ آقا یہ کہے كاتبتك على كذا ان اديته فانت حر ۔ چنانچہ شرح و جیز میں ہے ان لم يصرح بالتعليق بالا داء) ولا نواه لم يحصل
The slave will become free by paying the kitabah price, even if the master did not previously specify this. He is freed by its payment, even if the master did not say: 'When you pay it, you are free', because the consequence of the contract is established without explicit stipulation, as in sale. And it is not necessary to deduct anything from the price, by analogy to sale. Translation: He will be freed by paying the kitabah price, even if the master did not say: 'When you pay it, you are free', because the consequence of the contract is established without explicit stipulation, as in sale, and no reduction of the price is required, by analogy to sale. Commentary on his saying: 'and he is freed by its payment' etc. When the mukatab has paid the kitabah price, he will be freed, even if the master said: 'When you pay the kitabah price, you are free' or not. Also, whether the master intended his freedom by the kitabah or not. In Jawahir al-Fiqh, from Ibn [؟] Naim's book Nawadir al-Fiqhaha, it is narrated that there is consensus of the scholars on its permissibility, except for Imam al-Shafi'i. According to him, he will not be freed until the master says: 'I have made you a mukatab for such and such, if you pay it, you are free.' Thus, in Sharh al-Wajiz, it is stated: 'If he does not explicitly condition it on payment, nor intends it, freedom does not occur.'
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage clarifies that the effect of the kitabah contract is freedom upon payment, even if the master did not explicitly state that freedom is conditional on payment. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that the contract itself inherently produces this result, just as in a sale contract, ownership transfers without explicit stipulation. The master's intention or explicit condition is not required. The passage then notes that there is a consensus of scholars on this point, except for Imam al-Shafi'i, who requires an explicit conditional statement from the master (e.g., 'I have made you a mukatab for such and such; if you pay, you are free'). According to the Hanafi school, the contract of kitabah is sufficient to effect freedom upon full payment. Additionally, no reduction of the kitabah price is required, by analogy to sale where the full price must be paid. This analogy (qiyas) establishes the ruling clearly.

Key Terms
موجب عقد (muqtada al-'aqd): The legal consequence of a contract that follows from the contract itself without needing explicit stipulation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a mukatab become free from his master?
A) Only when the master explicitly says 'if you pay, you are free'.
B) When he pays the kitabah price, even if the master did not explicitly condition freedom on payment.
C) When the master announces his intention to free him, regardless of payment.
D) When a judge declares him free.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the kitabah contract automatically frees the slave upon full payment, analogous to the transfer of ownership in a sale.

Freedom of Mukatab by Full Payment
Ruling on mukatab freedom with proof and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a mukatab is freed by full payment without the master's explicit condition, and explain the Hadith proof and Hanafi reasoning.

Core Idea
Payment itself frees the mukatab; no explicit condition needed.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that a mukatab (slave under a kitaba contract) becomes free upon full payment, regardless of whether the master explicitly conditioned freedom on payment. The ruling is based on Hadith and the analogy to sale contracts. You will explore the evidence and the reasoning behind this stance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is the mukatab completing payment of the kitaba. The Hanafi ruling is that freedom is achieved automatically upon full payment, without any additional statement from the master.
This is the core ruling: payment = freedom.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
The text cites Hadith from Amr ibn Shu'ayb: 'Any slave who makes a kitaba for one hundred uqiyas and pays it except ten uqiyas is a slave...' This shows that full payment is the threshold for freedom.
The Hadith is ahad, so it is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The negative construction 'except ten uqiyas' (فاداها الا عشر اواق) indicates that partial payment does not free; only complete payment does. The implication is that payment itself effects freedom.
The Hanafi interpretation relies on the apparent meaning (zahir) of the Hadith.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf (Dispute)
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the master must explicitly condition freedom on payment (e.g., 'if you pay, you are free'), otherwise the mukatab remains a slave even after payment.
The text does not detail Shafi'i proof but mentions the choice of Zayd ibn Thabit's view.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih (Preference)
The author of al-Hidayah chooses the view of Zayd ibn Thabit and the Hanafi position, arguing that the kitaba contract itself implies freedom upon payment, analogous to a sale where ownership transfers by contract.
This is the mufta bihi position for Hanafis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن عمرو بن شعیب عن ابیہ عن جدہ ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: ايما عبد كاتب على مأته اوقية فاداها الا عشر اواق فهو عبد، وايما عبد كاتب على مائة دينار... [؟] ...وعنه صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: المكاتب عبد مابقى عليه من كتابة درهم. وعن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما: المكاتب عبد مابقى عليه شئ من كتابته. وعن عمر بن الخطاب قال: اذا ادى المكاتب الا الشطر فهو حر [؟]. وعن ابن مسعود قال: اذا ادى قدر ثمنه فهو غريم. وعن ابن عباس قال: اذا بقى على المكاتب خمس اواق او خمس دود او خمسة أوسق فهو غريم. ثم قال صاحب الهداية: واختارنا قول زيد بن ثابت. ثم قال: ويعتق بادائه وان لم يقل المولى اذا اديتها فانت حر لان موجب العقد يثبت من غير التصريح به كما في البيع.
From Amr ibn Shu'ayb, from his father, from his grandfather: The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Any slave who makes a contract of kitaba for one hundred uqiyas and pays it except ten uqiyas is a slave, and any slave who makes a contract for one hundred dinars...' And from him ﷺ: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains from his kitaba.' And from Ibn Umar: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as anything remains from his kitaba.' And from Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'When the mukatab pays except half, he is free.' And from Ibn Mas'ud: 'When he pays the equivalent of his value, he is a debtor.' And from Ibn Abbas: 'When there remains upon the mukatab five uqiyas or five dinars or five wasqs, he is a debtor.' Then the author of al-Hidayah said: 'We have chosen the saying of Zayd ibn Thabit.' Then he said: 'He becomes free by his payment, even if the master did not say: If you pay it, you are free, because the effect of the contract is established without explicit statement, as in sale.'
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This lesson presents a ruling from the chapter of kitaba (contract of manumission). The passage first provides Hadith evidence establishing that a mukatab remains a slave until the full kitaba is paid, and records differing views among the Companions on partial payment. The author of al-Hidayah states the Hanafi position: freedom is achieved by complete payment, regardless of whether the master explicitly conditioned freedom on payment. The analogy is to a sale contract, where ownership transfers by the contract itself without explicit statement. This position is supported by the Hadith and the choice of Zayd ibn Thabit. The implicit opposition (Imam al-Shafi'i requiring explicit condition) is addressed in the commentary but not detailed here.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered a contract with his master to pay a sum in exchange for freedom.
كتابة (kitābah): The contract of manumission between master and slave for a fixed payment.
بدل كتابة (badal al-kitābah): The payment agreed upon in the kitaba contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Upon payment of the full kitaba, even without explicit condition.

D) When he pays the equivalent of his market value.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a mukatab is freed by full payment alone, based on Hadith and the nature of the kitaba contract.

No Obligatory Reduction of Kitaba for Master
Inter-madhhab dispute on whether master must reduce the kitaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on reduction of kitaba, explain the Shafi'i evidence from Quran 24:33, and evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal.

Core Idea
The master is not obligated to reduce the kitaba; the Quranic command is for recommendation, not obligation.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the master's duty to reduce the kitaba (manumission payment) for a mukatab. The Hanafi school holds that reduction is recommended (mustahabb) but not obligatory, while the Shafi'i school argues it is wajib based on a Quranic imperative. We will trace the proofs and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling in the opening sentence: reduction is not obligatory (wajib); it is merely recommended (mustahabb). The analogy to sale—a seller is not obliged to reduce the price—supports this.
2
Identify the Shafi'i proof
Locate the Quranic verse cited by Imam al-Shafi'i: 'And give them from the wealth of Allah which He has given you' (24:33). Note that he interprets the imperative 'give' as indicating obligation (wujub).
3
Analyse the Hanafi rebuttal
Examine the three refutation points: (1) the addressees are all Muslims, not just masters; (2) the 'wealth' refers to zakat, not kitaba; (3) the imperative here indicates recommendation (nadb), not obligation. Also note the inconsistency critique from al-Jawhar al-Naqi.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical difference: Hanafis allow the master to choose; Shafi'is require reduction. This affects whether the master is sinful if he does not reduce.
5
Note the tarjih
Understand that the Hanafi position is the mufta bihi (operative for fatwa), supported by the text's reasoning and accepted by later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجب حط شى من البدل اعتبارا بالبيع. قال الله تعالى: وَآتُوهُمْ مِنْ مَالِ اللَّهِ الَّذِي آتَاكُمْ. واستدل به الشافعي على وجوب الحط. والجواب: أن المخاطبين بالآية عامة المسلمين، لا الموالى خاصة؛ والمراد بالمال المال الصدقي الذي يجب في الأموال. وأيضا الأمر للندب لا للوجوب. وفى الجوهر النقى: العجب من الشافعي كيف حمل الأمر في قوله تعالى فَكَاتِبُوهُم على الندب وفي قوله وَاتُوهُم على الوجوب.
And it is not obligatory to reduce any part of the payment, by analogy to sale. Allah said: 'And give them from the wealth of Allah which He has given you.' Al-Shafi'i used this as proof for the obligation of reduction. The answer: Those addressed in the verse are all Muslims, not specifically the masters; and the intended wealth is the charity wealth that is obligatory upon assets. Also, the command is for recommendation, not obligation. And in al-Jawhar al-Naqi: It is surprising of al-Shafi'i that he interprets the command in 'so contract kitaba with them' as recommendation, and the command in 'and give them' as obligation.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This lesson addresses the inter-madhhab dispute about whether it is obligatory (wajib) for the master to reduce the kitaba (payment). The Hanafi position is that reduction is not wajib; it is merely mustahabb. The matn states this by analogy to sale: just as the seller is not obliged to reduce the price, the master is not obliged to reduce the kitaba. Al-Shafi'i and others argue from the Quranic verse (24:33) 'And give them from the wealth of Allah which He has given you,' interpreting the imperative 'give' as obligatory. The Hanafi refutation: (1) the addressees are not the masters alone but all wealthy Muslims, (2) the 'wealth' refers to zakat/sadaqah, not the kitaba, and (3) the imperative here indicates recommendation (nadb), not obligation (wujub). The passage also cites a critique from al-Jawhar al-Naqi noting inconsistency in al-Shafi'i's methodology. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that reduction is not wajib.

Key Terms
حط (hatt): Reduction or remission of part of the kitaba by the master.
ندب (nadb): Recommendation; an act that is encouraged but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, the master's reduction of the kitaba is:
A) Wajib (obligatory).
B) Mustahabb (recommended).
C) Makruh (disliked).
D) Haram (forbidden).

Key Takeaway
The master is not obligated to reduce the kitaba; the Quranic command is interpreted as recommendation (nadb) by the Hanafi school.
