Immediate Payment in Kitabah: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Hanafi and Shafi'i dispute on immediate payment in kitabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on immediate payment in kitabah, explain each school's proof, and apply the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Hanafis allow immediate payment in kitabah; Shafi'is require installments — the text and analogy decide.

The kitabah contract (manumission by payment) raises a key dispute: can the master demand immediate payment from the slave, or must it be deferred in installments? The Hanafi school permits both, while Imam al-Shafi'i insists on installments. This lesson unpacks the proofs and practical consequences of each view, sharpening your ability to analyse ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
What exactly is the point of disagreement? Is it the permissibility of immediate payment, or something else?
The dispute is whether the condition of immediate payment (halan) in a kitabah contract is valid.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
What do the Hanafis rule and what evidence do they cite?
Hanafi: both immediate and deferred are permissible. Proof: general Qur'anic command (fakatibuhum) without condition of installments; analogy to sale.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
What does al-Shafi'i hold and what is his evidence?
Shafi'i: immediate payment invalid; installments necessary. Proof: the mukatab is incapable of paying at once due to prior slavery; unlike salam where the seller is free.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How do the Hanafis rebut the Shafi'i objection?
The contract itself establishes ability; the general text prevails; kitabah is based on leniency, not strictness.
5
Determine the practical consequence
What is the thamarah al-khilaf? How does the ruling differ in application?
If immediate payment fails: Hanafi returns the slave to slavery; Shafi'i invalidates the contract from the start.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجوزان يشترط المال حالا ويجوز مؤجلا ومنجما وقال الشافعى لا يجوز حالا ولابد من تنجيم لان عاجز عن التسليم في زمان قليل لعدم الاهلية قبله للرق بخلاف السلم على اصله لانه اهل للملك فكار احتمال القدرة ثابتا وقد دل الاقدام على العقد عليها فتثبت به ولنا ظاهر ما تلونا من غير شرط التنجيم ولان عقد معاوضة والبدل مقصود به فاشبه الثمن فى البيع فى عدم اشتراط القدرة عليه بخلاف السلم على اصلنا لان المسلم فيه معقود عليه فلابد من القدرة عليه ولان مبنى الكتابة على المساهلة فيمهله المولى ظاهرا بخلاف السلم لان مبناه على المضايقة في الحال كما امتنع من الاداء يرد الى الرقة [؟] ترجمہ اور جائز ہے یہ کہ شرط کیا جائے مال فی الحال یا میعادی قسط وار ، امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جائز نہیں۔ فی الحال کی شرط کرنا اور قسط وار ہونا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ تھوڑے زمانہ میں ادائیگی سے عاجز ہے اس سے پہلے بوجہ رقیت عدم اہلیت کی وجہ سے بخلاف سلم کے اصول پر کیونکہ وہ ملکیت کا اہل ہے۔ پس قدرت کا احتمال ثابت رہا اور عقد پر اقدام کرنا اس پر دال ہے تو اس سے قدرت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ اور ہماری دلیل ظاہر ہے اس آیت کا جو ہم نے تلاوت کی قسط وار کی شرط کے بغیر ، اور اس لئے کہ کتابت بھی عقد معاوضہ ہے اور بدل معقود بہ ہے۔ پس بیچ میں شمن کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ اس پر قدرت کی شرط نہ ہونے میں۔ بخلاف سلم کے ہمارے اصول پر کیونکہ مسلم فیہ معقود علیہ ہے تو اس پر قدرت کا ہونا ضروری ہے اور اس لئے کہ کتابت کا مدار آسانی پر ہے۔ پس آقاء بظاہر اسے مہلت دے گا بخلاف سلم کے کیونکہ اس کا مدار نگی پر ہے اور فی الحال کی شرط میں جو نہی ادائیگی سے رکے گا فور غلامی کی طرف لوٹا دیا جائے گا۔ تشريح .. قوله ويجوزان يشترط .... الخ عقد کتابت کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ کتابت حالہ کتابت مؤجلہ، کتابت حالہ یہ ہے کہ غلام بدل کتابت فی الحال ادا کر دے۔ بان يقول المولى كاتبت على الف درهم صرح به ابو الليث [؟] في فتاواه) کتابت مؤجلہ یہ ہے کہ بدل کتابت میعادی اور قسط واری ہو ۔ بان يقول: كاتبتك على الف درهم الى سنة يؤدى كل شهر من النجم كذا، میں نے تجھے ایک سالہ میعادی ہزار درہم کے عوض مکاتب کیا کہ ہر ماہ اتنی قسط ادا کرتے رہنا۔ ہمارے یہاں اور ظاہر الروایہ میں امام احمد کے یہاں یہ دونوں صورتیں جائز ہیں۔ رویانی وغیرہ بعض شوافع نے بھی اس کو اختیار کیا ہے۔ اور بقول ابن التین۔ امام مالک سے اس بارے میں کوئی نص نہیں۔ لیکن جواہر مالکیہ میں ہے۔ قال ابو بكرة ظاهر قول مالك ان التنجيم والتاجيل شرط فيه .. ثم قال: وعلما ونا يقولون ان الكتابة الحالة جائزة. قوله وقال الشافعى ... الخ - امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ فی الحال ادا کرنے کی شرط جائز نہیں بلکہ قسط وار ہونا ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ مکاتب فی الحال اس کی ادائیگی سے عاجز ہے اس واسطے کی عقد کتابت سے پہلے اس میں بوجہ رقیت ملک کی اہلیت نہیں تھی اور عقد کتابت کے بعد قلیل زمانہ میں مال کثیر کما لینے کی قدرت عادة ثابت نہیں ہوتی۔ پس وہ فی الفور بدل کتابت ادا نہیں کر سکتا لہذا قسط وار ہونا ضروری ہے۔ قوله بخلاف السلم على اصله .. الخ - بخلاف بیع سلم کے کہ وہ فی الحال امام شافعی کے قاعدہ پر جائز ہے اس لئے کہ سلم کی صورت میں عقد سلم سے پہلے مسلم الیہ کو اسکے آزاد ہونے کی وجہ سے ملکیت کی لیاقت حاصل ہے تو بحر متعین نہ ہوا بلکہ قدرت کا احتمال ثابت رہا۔ یعنی آزاد آدمی کا ظاہر حال یہی ہے کہ وہ بالفعل ہر مال پر قادر ہے جس کی دلیل مسلم الیہ کا عقد سلم پر اقدام کرنا ہے۔ پس سلم میں فی الحال ادائیگی کی شرط کرنا جائز ہے۔ بخلاف کتابت کے کہ اس میں مکاتب بوجہ مملوکیت کسی مال پر قادر نہیں تھا تو وہ فی الحال ادا نہیں کر سکتا ۔ لہذا اس میں فی الحال ادائیگی کی شرط لگانا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ قوله ولنا ظاهر ماتلونا ... الخ - ہماری دلیل ... ایک تو ظاہر آیت فکا تبوهم " ہے کہاس میں تخیم تا جیل یعنی فی الحال یا و قسط وار ہونے کی شرط لگانا نص پر زیادتی ہے جو ایک طرح سے نسخ کے درجہ میں ہوتی ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کتابت بھی ایک عقد معاوضہ ہے جس میں عوض معقود یہ ہے کہ مال ادا کر کے غلام کو اپنے نفس کی آزادی حاصل ہوگی ۔ پس کتابت میں یہ مال ایسا ہو گیا۔ جیسے بیچ میں شمن ہوتا ہے کہ اس میں قدرت کا ہونا شرط نہیں ہے۔ اسی لئے قبضہ سے پہلے اس کا استبدال جائز ہے۔ اور یہ یمن ہونے کی علامت ہے۔
He said: It is permissible to stipulate the payment as immediate, and permissible as deferred and in installments. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible as immediate, and installments are necessary, because he is incapable of delivery in a short time due to lack of capacity before due to slavery, unlike salam according to his principle, because he is capable of ownership, so the possibility of ability remains, and proceeding with the contract indicates it, so it is established. And for us, the apparent meaning of what we recited without the condition of installments, and because it is a commutative contract and the consideration is intended, so it resembles the price in sale in not stipulating ability, unlike salam according to our principle, because the salam commodity is the subject matter, so ability is necessary, and because kitabah is based on leniency, so the master gives him time apparently, unlike salam because it is based on strictness. If he refrains from payment, he is returned to slavery. ... (translation of Urdu commentary continues with explanation of the two types, Shafi'i argument, and Hanafi response).
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of stipulating immediate payment (halan) in a kitabah contract. The Hanafi school allows both immediate and deferred payment in installments (munajjam), while Imam al-Shafi'i requires installments. The Shafi'i argument is that a mukatab slave is incapable of paying a large sum immediately due to his prior slavery, unlike salam where the seller is a free person capable of ownership. The Hanafi response relies on the general command in the Qur'an (fakatibuhum) without specifying installments, and on qiyas to sale where the price need not be immediately payable. The text further explains that the Hanafi position is based on the nature of kitabah as a commutative contract analogous to sale, and on the principle of leniency (musahalah) in kitabah. The discussion includes the distinction between kitabah hallah (immediate) and kitabah mu'ajjalah (deferred), noting that both are valid in the Hanafi school and in the Zahir al-Riwayah. The Shafi'i argument that a slave cannot have the ability to pay immediately is countered by the Hanafi view that the contract itself establishes the ability, and the condition of installments is an addition to the text.

Key Terms
کتابت (kitabah): A contract of manumission where a slave agrees to pay a sum to the master in exchange for freedom
حالا (halan): Immediate payment, paid at the time of contract
منجما (munajjaman): Deferred payment in installments (nujum)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a kitabah contract stipulates immediate payment and the slave fails to pay, what happens?
A) The contract is void and the slave remains a slave
B) The slave is returned to slavery
C) The contract becomes deferred automatically
D) The slave is freed anyway

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows both immediate and deferred payment in kitabah, relying on the general Qur'anic command and analogy to sale, while the Shafi'i school requires installments due to the slave's presumed inability.

Permissibility of Immediate Payment in Kitaba: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Explains the Hanafi position on immediate vs deferred kitaba with proofs and response to Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on kitaba hala, identify the Shafi'i objection, and apply the Hanafi response using the Quranic imperative and qiyas to sale.

Core Idea
Kitaba with immediate payment is valid because the Quranic command is absolute and ability to pay is not a condition in commutative contracts.

The contract of kitaba can be structured with immediate payment (hala) or deferred instalments (mu'ajjala). The Shafi'i school insists that instalments are necessary because the slave cannot pay immediately. The Hanafi school disagrees and argues that both forms are valid based on the absolute Quranic command and analogy to sale.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two forms of kitaba
Identify the difference between kitaba hala (immediate lump sum) and kitaba mu'ajjala (deferred instalments). Both are recognised in Hanafi fiqh.
The master may stipulate 'on the condition that you pay 1000 dirhams immediately' (hala) or 'pay 1000 dirhams over one year in monthly instalments' (mu'ajjala).
2
State the Hanafi position
Confirm that the Hanafi school permits both forms. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and it is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi).
This is recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Recognise the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that kitaba hala is invalid because the slave, being a mamluk before the contract, lacks ownership capacity and cannot reasonably acquire wealth quickly after the contract to pay a lump sum.
The Shafi'i school requires instalments (tajil/tanjim) as a condition.
4
Analyse the Hanafi proofs
Two main proofs: (1) The Quranic imperative 'fakatibuhum' is absolute and does not specify instalments; adding such a condition is an unwarranted addition akin to abrogation. (2) Qiyas to sale: just as a sale is valid even if the buyer does not have the price at the time of contract, so is kitaba.
The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i objection: the substitute in kitaba has two aspects – as a price (thaman) and as a sold item (mabi'). The dissolution upon inability to pay reflects the sale aspect, but the condition of ability at contract formation is not required.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In Hanafi law, a master can make a mukatab with immediate payment due; in Shafi'i law, such a contract would be invalid unless instalments are stipulated.
This difference affects the validity of the contract itself.

Source Text

Key Terms
كتابة (kitaba): A contract by which a slave agrees to pay a sum to his master in exchange for his freedom.
حالہ (hala): Immediate payment, where the whole sum is due at the time of contract.
مؤجلہ (mu'ajjala): Deferred payment in instalments over a specified period.

Kitaba for a Minor Slave: Conditions and Wording
Ruling on kitaba for a minor slave and required wording

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid kitaba of a minor slave and distinguish between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the minor's capacity.

Core Idea
A minor who understands buying and selling can validly enter kitaba because he can give consent.

This passage from al-Hidayah discusses whether a minor slave (saghir) can be made a mukatab. The Hanafi school permits it if the minor understands transactions, while Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees. We will examine the conditions, the wording required, and the basis of the disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making a minor slave a mukatab. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) if the minor understands buying and selling.
The text states: 'وتجوز كتابة العبد الصغير اذا كان يعقل البيع والشراء' (kitaba of a minor slave is valid if he understands buying and selling).
2
Isolate the key condition: understanding transactions
The minor must be 'aqil (capable of understanding the transaction). This is necessary for valid acceptance (qabul).
The condition is that he 'ya'qil al-bay'a wa al-shira' (understands buying and selling).
3
Locate the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees with the Hanafi ruling. The difference is built on the issue of a minor's permission (idhn al-sabi) in trade.
The text says: 'والشافعي يخالفنا فيه وهو بناء على مسألة اذن الصبي في التجارة' (al-Shafi'i differs with us, and it is built on the issue of a minor's permission in trade).
4
Analyse the wording conditions for kitaba
The author gives two examples of valid wording: explicit kitaba with deferred payment and instalments, and a conditional phrasing with instalments. A narration from Abu Hafs invalidates the latter if payment is conditional on a single payment.
The first example: 'جعلت علیک الفا توديها...' (I have made one thousand due from you...). The second: 'اذا أديت الى الفا كل شهر مائة' (if you pay me one thousand, one hundred each month...).

Effect of Valid Kitabah: Exiting Yad but Not Milk
General ruling on kitabah's effect on possession and ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal effect of a valid kitabah contract on the mukatab's possession and ownership, and explain the Hanafi proof and its practical consequence regarding travel.

Core Idea
Kitabah transfers yad (possession) but not milk (ownership); the mukatab gains earning freedom while remaining owned.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational ruling of kitabah: upon a valid contract, the mukatab exits the master's direct physical control but remains his property. This dual status has significant practical consequences, especially regarding the mukatab's ability to trade, travel, and manage his affairs. We will explore the textual proof and the reasoning behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal effect
State the two-part ruling: the mukatab leaves the master's yad (possession) but not his milk (ownership).
This is the core of the passage.
2
Understand the reason for leaving yad
Analyze why the mukatab exits the master's possession: to realize the meaning of kitabah (al-damm, joinder) or to achieve the purpose (payment of badal).
3
Understand the reason for retaining milk
Identify the proofs: the hadith (implicitly 'al-mukatab 'abd ma baqiya 'alayhi dirham') and the contractual nature of kitabah as a commutative contract requiring equality.
Immediate freedom would negate equality.
4
Recognize the practical consequence: authority to travel
Note that the mukatab may travel (long or short) even if the master forbids him, because the purpose of kitabah requires earning.
5
Note the madhhab dispute on travel
Compare the Hanafi position with Imam Malik and the second Shafi'i view, which require the master's permission.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate and has practical implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تشریح .... قوله واذا صحت ... الخ- جب عقد کتابت صحیح ہو جائے تو مکا تب اپنے آقا کے قبضہ سے نکل جاتا ہے پر اس کی ملا سے نہیں نکلتا۔ قبضہ سے نکل جانا تو اس لئے ہے تا کہ کتابت کے معنی جونم (ملانا) ہے وہ متحقق ہوں گو یا مکاتب اپنے قبضہ کو اپنی ملکیت کی جانب ملاتا ہے یعنی فی الحال اسکو اپنے ہاتھ کی کمائی کا اختیار اور انجام کار اپنی ذات کی آزادی حاصل ہو جاتی ہے پس با اختیار ذات کے اختیار سے مل جاتا ہے یا آقا کے قبضہ سے نکل جانا اس لئے ہے تا کہ کتابت کا جو مقصد ( اداء عوض ) ہے وہ حاصل ہو۔ ہا تب کو خرید وفروخت کا اور سفر میں جانے کا اختیار حاصل ہو جاتا ہے ( سفر طویل ہو یا قصیر ) اگر چہ آقا نے اس کو سفر میں جانے سے منع ردیا ہو ۔ امام احمد اور ایک قول میں امام شافعی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ ان کا دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ آقا کی اجازت کے بغیر سفر میں نہیں جاسکتا۔ م مالک کا قول بھی یہی ہے۔ اور بعض شوافع نے طویل وقصیر سفر میں فرق کیا ہے۔
Book of Kitabah. When kitabah becomes valid, the mukatab leaves the possession of the master but does not leave his ownership. As for leaving his possession, it is to realize the meaning of kitabah which is joinder (al-damm); thus he joins his possession-ownership to his self-ownership, or to realize the purpose of kitabah which is payment of the badal, so he has the authority to sell, buy, and travel even if the master forbids him. As for not leaving his ownership, it is due to what we have narrated [the hadith] and because it is a contract of exchange built on equality, and that is negated by immediate emancipation and realized by its delay, because a type of ownership is established for him and a right is established in the dhimma in one respect. So if the master emancipates him, he becomes free by his emancipation because he is the owner of his person, and the badal of kitabah is dropped from him because he undertook it only in exchange for obtaining freedom, and it has been obtained without it. Translation: When kitabah becomes valid, the mukatab came out of the master's possession but did not come out of his ownership. Coming out of the master's possession is for the realization of kitabah, and that is joinder; so the mukatab joins his possession-ownership to his personal ownership, or for the realization of the purpose of kitabah, which is payment of the badal. Thus the mukatab becomes authorized to buy, sell, and travel, even if the master forbids him. And not coming out of the master's ownership is due to the hadith we narrated, and because kitabah is a contract of exchange requiring equality, and this is lost by immediate freedom and realized by its delay, because the mukatab obtains a type of ownership and a right in the dhimma from one aspect. Explanation: 'His statement: and when it becomes valid...' - When the contract of kitabah becomes valid, the mukatab goes out of the master's possession but not out of his ownership. Going out of possession is so that the meaning of kitabah (joinder) is realized, or the mukatab joins his possession to his ownership, i.e., he gains authority over his earnings and eventually his own freedom, so he joins with the authority of his self, or so that the purpose of kitabah (payment of badal) is achieved. The mukatab obtains authority to buy, sell, and travel (whether long or short journey) even if the master forbade him. Imam Ahmad and in one narration Imam Shafi'i hold this view. Their second view is that he cannot travel without the master's permission. Imam Malik's view is also this. And some Shafi'is differentiate between long and short travel.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Kitabah. It establishes the core legal effect of a valid kitabah contract: the mukatab (slave contracted for freedom) leaves the master's physical possession and control (yad) but remains in the master's ownership (milk). The commentary explains that the reason for leaving the master's yad is to realize the very meaning of kitabah (which is 'joinder' - joining the mukatab's control over his earnings to his own self) or to achieve the purpose of kitabah (payment of the badal). Thus, the mukatab gains the ability to buy, sell, and travel freely, even against the master's prohibition. Imam Ahmad and a view of Imam al-Shafi'i agree; another Shafi'i view and Imam Malik require the master's permission for travel, with some Shafi'is distinguishing between long and short journeys. The proof for not leaving milk includes a hadith (likely 'al-mukatab 'abd ma baqiya 'alayhi dirham') and rational reasoning: kitabah is a commutative contract based on equality, which would be destroyed by immediate freedom since the master would lose the badal. Delayed freedom preserves equality. The mukatab gains a type of ownership and a right in the dhimma.

Key Terms
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitabah with his master, agreeing to pay a sum in exchange for freedom.
يد (yad): Physical possession and control; the master's direct authority over the slave's person and labor.
ملك (milk): Ownership; the master retains legal title to the mukatab until full payment of badal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, after a valid kitabah contract, which of the following is true?
A) The mukatab is fully free and no longer owned by the master.
B) The mukatab leaves the master's possession but remains in his ownership.
C) The mukatab must obtain the master's permission for any sale or purchase.
D) The mukatab cannot travel even if the master allows it.

Key Takeaway
A valid kitabah transfers possession from master to mukatab but not ownership; this enables the mukatab to earn and travel freely while remaining the master's property.

Master's Emancipation of Mukatab Drops Badal
Ruling on the effect of master's voluntary emancipation of the mukatab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a master voluntarily emancipates his mukatab and explain why the badal (payment) is dropped.

Core Idea
Master's emancipation overrides kitabah and drops the debt because payment was only for freedom, already obtained.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario within the kitabah contract: what happens if the master, after a valid kitabah, decides to free the slave voluntarily? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling with logical reasoning (ta'lil). This demonstrates how the master's ownership rights intersect with the contractual obligations of kitabah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the master's voluntary emancipation (itq) of the mukatab after a valid kitabah. The ruling: the slave becomes free immediately.
The master retains ownership of the mukatab's person despite the kitabah.
2
Trace the consequence for the badal
The badal al-kitabah (payment) is dropped from the mukatab's liability. It is not transferred or reduced; it is entirely cancelled.
This is not a forgiveness or remission; it is a legal cancellation due to the failure of consideration.
3
Follow the ta'lil (reasoning)
The mukatab undertook to pay badal only in exchange for freedom. Since freedom has been granted directly, the obligation to pay has no basis and thus falls away.
This is a logical analogy (qiyas) with any contract where the object becomes impossible.
4
Confirm the condition for the ruling
The ruling applies only if the master still owns the mukatab at the time of emancipation – that is, the kitabah had not been rescinded or completed.
If the mukatab had already paid the badal, emancipation would be redundant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله فان اعتقه الخ - اگر مکاتب کرنے کے بعد آقا نے غلام کو آزاد کر دیا تو آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ آقا ابھی تک اس کی ات کا مالک ہے اور جب وہ آزاد ہو گیا تو اس کے ذمہ سے بدل کتابت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس نے یہ مال دینے کا التزام اسی طور پر لیا تھا کہ اس کے عوض آزادی حاصل ہو ۔ حالانکہ وہ اس کے بغیر ہی آزاد ہو گیا تو وہ اس کا ذمہ دارنہ رہا۔
His statement: 'then if he emancipates him etc.' - If after kitabah the master frees the slave, then he will become free. Because the master still owns his person, and when he becomes free, the badal of kitabah is dropped from his dhimma. Because he undertook to give this wealth only in exchange for obtaining freedom, and freedom has been obtained without it, so he is not liable for it.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This is a ruling statement explaining the consequence if the master voluntarily emancipates the mukatab after a valid kitabah. The mukatab becomes free immediately by the master's act of emancipation because the master still has ownership (milk) over the mukatab's person (as established in the previous lesson). Simultaneously, the badal (payment) originally due under the kitabah contract is dropped from the mukatab's liability. The reason is that the mukatab undertook the obligation of payment only as a quid pro quo for obtaining freedom. Since freedom has been granted directly without requiring payment, the consideration fails, and the obligation is void. This is a straightforward ruling with logical reasoning (ta'lil).

Key Terms
عتق (itq): The master's act of freeing the slave voluntarily; distinct from kitabah which is contractual freedom.
بدل کتابت (badal al-kitabah): The payment owed by the mukatab to the master under the kitabah contract; drops upon master's emancipation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The badal is halved.
C) The badal is dropped entirely.
D) The badal transfers to the mukatab's heirs.

Key Takeaway
Master's emancipation of a mukatab frees the slave and drops the badal because the payment was only consideration for freedom, which is already granted.

Master's Cohabitation with Mukatabah Obligates 'Aqr
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a master's cohabitation with his mukatabah, identify the proof from the Quran and the legal reasoning, and compare the positions of the schools.

Core Idea
A master must pay 'aqr for cohabiting with his mukatabah because she has a right over her body through the kitabah contract.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a nuanced issue: what happens when a master has sexual intercourse with his own mukatabah (female slave under a kitabah contract)? Ownership normally grants full access, but kitabah confers on the slave a right over her own person. The Hanafi school rules that the master becomes liable for 'aqr (compensatory dower). We'll unpack the proof, the dispute with Imam Malik, and the consequences if cohabitation is stipulated in the kitabah contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the master's cohabitation with his mukatabah. The ruling: payment of 'aqr becomes wajib (obligatory) upon the master.
'Aqr is the dower of a similar woman, not a fixed amount.
2
Locate the dalil and wajh al-dalalah
The text argues that the mukatabah has become 'more entitled to her parts' (ajza') to achieve the purpose of kitabah (earning freedom). The Quranic verse 'and seek with your wealth' (4:24) shows that the benefits of the vulva are compensable, like wages.
The Quranic reference is used as a broad principle, not a direct command.
3
Note the ikhtilaf with Imam Malik
Imam Malik holds that no 'aqr is due because the master still retains ownership; cohabitation is like with any other slave. The Hanafi response: kitabah grants her a right over her body for earning, so its use requires compensation.
Also note the view of Imam Ahmad and a transmission from 'Imam Nafd' regarding stipulation.
4
Understand the secondary ruling on stipulation
If the master stipulates cohabitation in the kitabah contract, the contract becomes fasid (invalid) according to Hanafis and Shafi'is, because it contradicts the purpose of kitabah. Malik says only the condition is invalid; Ahmad says both are valid.
This shows how the ruling on 'aqr ties into the validity of the underlying contract.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, the master pays 'aqr and may be punished; under Maliki, no payment; under Ahmad, if stipulated, no punishment.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi view.

Source Text

قوله واذا وطى المولى.. الخ - اگر آقا نے اپنی مکاتبہ باندی سے وطی کر لی تو اس کے ذمہ عقر لا زم ہوگا۔ یعنی اسی جیسی عورت کا جو مہر ہوتا ہو وہ دینا پڑے گا۔ امام شافعی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ امام مالک کے نزدیک عقر واجب نہ ہوگا۔ امام ند فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مکاتبہ سے وطی کرنے کی شرط کر لی ہو تو واجب ہوگا ورنہ نہیں بلکہ سزادی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ یہ ولی حرام ہے۔ بہر کیف حناف و شوافع کے نزدیک وحی شرط کرنے کی صورت میں کتابت فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ امام مالک کے نزدیک شرط فاسد ہوگی اور عقد صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ امام احمد کے نزدیک شرط وعقد دونوں صحیح ہوں گے۔
قوله لا نها صارت اخص .... الخ - وجوب عقر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مکاتبہ مذکورہ آقا کی بہ نسبت اپنے اجزاء کی زیادہ مختار ہو چکی ہے تا کہ اس کے ذریعہ سے کتابت کا مقصود حاصل کیا جائے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ آقا کو مال کتابت حاصل ہو اور اس کے عوض میں باندی کو زادی حاصل ہو۔ اور عورت کے منافع بضعہ چونکہ بمنزلہ اجر اوراعیان ہیں " حيث قابلها الشرع بالا عيان قال الله تعالى وان تبتغوا باموالکم لہذا اسکا استحقاق بھی باندی ہنی کو حاصل ہے۔ پس اس سے منفعت حاصل کرنے میں آقا ضامن ہوگا۔
His statement: 'and when the master cohabits etc.' - If the master cohabits with his mukatabah slave-woman, then 'aqr (dower) becomes obligatory upon him, meaning he must pay a dower like that of a similar woman. Imam Shafi'i also holds this view. According to Imam Malik, 'aqr is not obligatory. Imam [Nafd?] says that if he stipulated cohabitation in the kitabah contract, then it becomes obligatory; otherwise not, rather he will be punished because it is illicit intercourse. In any case, according to Hanafis and Shafi'is, if cohabitation is stipulated, the kitabah becomes invalid (fasid). According to Imam Malik, the condition is invalid but the contract remains valid. According to Imam Ahmad, both the condition and the contract are valid. His statement: 'because she has become more entitled to her parts etc.' - The proof for the obligation of 'aqr is that the mukatabah has become more entitled to her parts relative to the master, so that through that the purpose of kitabah is achieved, which is that the master obtains the badal of kitabah and in exchange the slave-woman obtains freedom. And since the benefits of the vulva are like wages and property - because the Law treats them as property (Quran: 'and seek with your wealth'), therefore she has the right to them. Thus, if he derives benefit from her, the master is liable.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute concerning the master's cohabitation with his mukatabah. The ruling: If the master has intercourse with his mukatabah, he must pay 'aqr (the dower of a similar woman). The proof is that the mukatabah has become 'more entitled to her own parts' (ajza') than the master, meaning she has a claim over her body because the purpose of kitabah is to enable her to earn and gain freedom. The benefits of her body (manafi' bud') are legally compensable, as indicated by the Quranic verse 'and seek with your wealth' (marriage context). Therefore, the master must pay. Imam Shafi'i agrees. Imam Malik holds no 'aqr is due. A transmission from Imam Nafd' (perhaps a later Hanafi or a misrendering of Nafi'?) says 'aqr is due only if stipulated; otherwise punishment. The commentary notes that among Hanafis and Shafi'is, if the master stipulates cohabitation in the kitabah contract, the kitabah itself becomes fasid (invalid) because it conflicts with the purpose. Imam Malik says only the condition is fasid, contract valid. Imam Ahmad says both are valid.

Key Terms
عقر ('aqr): A dower or compensation paid by a man who has intercourse with a woman without a valid marriage or ownership right over her vulva; here applied to the master's intercourse with his mukatabah.
مكاتبة (mukatabah): A female slave under a kitabah contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a master has intercourse with his mukatabah without her consent, what must he pay?
A) Nothing, because she is his property.
B) A fixed fine of 10 dirhams.
C) 'Aqr (the dower of a similar woman).
D) The badal (kitabah payment) is reduced.

Key Takeaway
A master who cohabits with his mukatabah must pay 'aqr because the kitabah contract gives her a right over her body, making compensation wajib.

Master's Assault on Mukatabah: Compensation without Qisas
Ruling on master's liability for assault on mukatabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a master assaults his mukatabah and explain why qisas is not applied.

Core Idea
Master's assault on mukatabah requires compensation but no qisas due to shubha.

In this passage, we examine the legal consequences when a master physically assaults his mukatabah slave-woman, her child, or damages her property. The Kitabah contract transforms the relationship, making the master liable for compensation while barring qisas due to residual ownership ambiguity. This ruling balances the mukatabah's rights with the master's partial interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The master's janiyah (assault) on his mukatabah, her child, or her property. The ruling: compensation is wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited: the mukatabah is entitled to her own parts (ajza'), and the master is like a stranger (ajnabi) regarding her person and earnings.
This is a qiyas: master compared to ajnabi.
3
Understand the exception
Why is qisas not obligatory? Due to shubha (ambiguity) from the master's residual ownership.
Shubha prevents qisas but not compensation.
4
Note the expansion
The principle extends to assault on her child and property, with appropriate compensation (diyah or equivalent value).
Property: mithl or qimah.
5
Appreciate the wisdom
The ruling prevents the master from destroying her property, preserving the purpose of kitabah.
Without liability, master could harm with impunity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وان جنى عليها .... الخ - اگر آقا نے اپنی مکاتبہ باندی پر یا اس کے بچہ یا مال پر جنایت کی تو آقا کے ذمہ یہ جرم لازم ہوگا۔ جنی جنایت نفس کی صورت میں دیت اور جنایت مال کی صورت میں مثل مال یا اس کی قیمت دینی پڑے گی۔ کیونکہ پہلے گزر چکا کہ مکاتبہ کو پنے اجزاء کی خود ہی مستحق ہے البتہ شبہ کی وجہ سے قصاص لازم نہ ہوگا جیسا کہ شمس الائمہ بیہقی کی کفایہ میں مصرح ہے۔ اور اتلاف شبہ کی وجہ سے قصاص لازم نہ ہوگا۔ کہ مکاتب اور مکاتبہ کی کمائی اور ان کی ذوات کے حق میں آقامشل اجنبی کے ہوتا ہے تو اجنبی کی طرح وہ بھی ضامن وگا۔ اگر یہ حکم نہ دیا جائے تو آقا اس کے مال کو تلف کر ڈالے گا اور عقد کتابت سے جو مقصود ہے اس کا حصول محال ہو جائے گا۔
His statement: 'and if he assaults her etc.' - If the master commits an assault upon his mukatabah slave-woman or upon her child or property, then this crime is obligatory upon him. In case of assault upon the person, he must pay diyah; in case of assault upon property, the equivalent or its value must be paid. Because it has already passed that the mukatabah is herself entitled to her parts. However, due to shubha (ambiguity), qisas is not obligatory, as is explicitly stated in Shams al-A'immah al-Bayhaqi's Kifayah. And due to the shubha, qisas is not obligatory. Because the mukatab and mukatabah's earnings and their persons are treated like a stranger (ajnabi) regarding them, so he is liable like a stranger. If this ruling were not given, the master would destroy her property, and the purpose of the kitabah contract would become impossible to achieve.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the master's criminal assault (janiyah) on his mukatabah, her child, or her property. The ruling: The master is liable for compensation. For assault on the person, he pays diyah (blood money); for property, he pays the equivalent or its value. However, qisas (retaliation) is not imposed because of shubha (ambiguity) - the master has a partial ownership (milk) over the mukatabah, which creates a doubt sufficient to prevent qisas. The proof is that the mukatabah is entitled to her own parts (ajza') due to the kitabah contract; the master is like an outsider (ajnabi) in matters of her earnings and self. If he were not liable, he would destroy her property, defeating the purpose of kitabah. This is based on the authority of Shams al-A'immah al-Bayhaqi's Kifayah.

Key Terms
جنایة (janiyah): Criminal act causing harm to person or property; here includes assault on body (nafs) and property (mal).
شبهة (shubha): Ambiguity or doubt in legal ownership that mitigates the full penal consequence (like qisas).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master knowingly injures his mukatabah, what is the Hanafi ruling regarding qisas?
A) Qisas is obligatory because she is like a free person.
B) Qisas is not obligatory due to shubha (ambiguity).
C) Qisas is obligatory only if she dies.
D) The master must be executed.

Key Takeaway
When a master assaults his mukatabah, he must pay compensation, but qisas is barred because of the shubha (ambiguity) in ownership.

Master's Liability for Destroying Mukatabah's Property
Ruling when master destroys the mukatabah's property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a master destroys a mukatabah's property and explain the rationale (istihsan) behind it.

Core Idea
The master who destroys his mukatabah's property must compensate her like a stranger, to protect the kitabah contract's purpose.

The source passage addresses a unique situation: a master destroying the property of his own slave who is under kitabah. Although the master owns the mukatabah herself, the kitabah contract grants her independent ownership of her earnings. This passage clarifies that the master is treated as an outsider (ajnabi) with respect to that property, and if he destroys it, he must pay its value. The rationale is pure istihsan: otherwise, the master could frustrate the purpose of the contract, which is to allow the mukatabah to earn and buy her freedom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the master's destruction (itlaf) of property belonging to his mukatabah. The ruling is that he must pay its value (ghurum).
The text uses 'ghurum' which means he is liable for compensation.
2
Recognize the legal principle
The master is treated as a stranger (ajnabi) regarding the mukatabah's earnings and her person. This means his relationship as owner does not give him any special right over her acquired property.
This is an exception to the normal rule that a master owns the property of his slave.
3
Understand the rationale (istihsan)
If the master were not liable, he could destroy her property without consequence, thus preventing her from earning the badal and achieving freedom. The purpose of the kitabah contract would be defeated.
The ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) to protect the objective of the contract.
4
Note the implication for ownership
The ruling affirms that the mukatabah has independent ownership of her acquired property, even though she is still a slave. This is a key feature of the kitabah contract.
Compare with a regular slave who does not own property independently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اتل مالا لها غرم لان المولى كالاجنبي في حق اكسابها ونفسها اذ لم يجعل كذلك لاتلفه المولی قیمت حصول الغرض المبتغى بالعقد
And if he destroys her property, he pays its value, because the master is like a stranger (ajnabi) regarding her earnings and herself; otherwise, if it were not made so, the master would destroy her property, preventing the achievement of the purpose sought by the contract.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This is a concise ruling statement and proof: If the master destroys (atlafa) any property (mal) belonging to the mukatabah, he must pay its value (ghurum). The reason is that the master is treated as an ajnabi (outsider) in matters of her earnings and her person. If he were not held liable, he could destroy her assets, undermining the entire purpose of the kitabah contract, which is to allow the mukatabah to earn money to pay the badal and eventually gain freedom. The underlying rationale is istihsan based on necessity (darurah) to protect the objective of the contract.

Key Terms
اتلاف (itlaf): Destruction of property; the master's act of damaging or destroying the mukatabah's belongings.
مكاتبة (mukatabah): A female slave who has entered a contract of kitabah with her master, allowing her to earn money to purchase her freedom.
غرم (ghurum): Liability to pay compensation or value of destroyed property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling if a master destroys the property of his mukatabah?
A) He is not liable because he owns her.
B) He must pay the value of the property.
C) The badal of kitabah is reduced by the value.
D) He must compensate her with a slave of equal value.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the master must compensate the mukatabah for any property he destroys, treating him as a stranger to protect the purpose of the kitabah contract.

Mukatab's Right to Travel: Hanafi vs Other Schools
Ruling on mukatab's travel authority with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mukatab's travel authority and explain the inter-madhhab dispute, including the proofs and practical consequences.

Core Idea
The mukatab may travel without permission because kitabah is a commutative contract requiring equality.

The status of a mukatab (a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom) is unique in Islamic law: he remains a slave but gains certain rights to earn and trade. One such right is the ability to travel—even without the master's consent. The Hanafi school grants this right broadly, while other schools restrict it. In this lesson, we explore the reasoning behind the Hanafi position and the points of disagreement with other madhhabs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
What is the specific act being ruled upon? The passage deals with a mukatab traveling (both long and short journeys) without the master's permission. State the Hanafi ruling: it is permissible (mubah) and the master cannot forbid it.
Contrast with ordinary slaves who have no such right.
2
State the Hanafi Position
The Hanafi school holds that the mukatab may travel even if the master explicitly forbids it, for both long and short journeys. This is based on the nature of the kitabah contract.
The authority is zahir al-riwayah.
3
Identify Opposing Schools and Their Views
List the schools that disagree: Imam Malik and one opinion of Imam al-Shafi'i require the master's permission. Some Shafi'is distinguish between long and short journeys. Imam Ahmad and another Shafi'i opinion agree with the Hanafis.
Note that here 'opposing' means the view requiring permission.
4
Analyze the Proofs
The Hanafi proof has two parts: (1) hadith 'al-mukatab 'abd ma baqiya 'alayhi dirham' – he is still a slave, but the contract grants him rights; (2) qiyas (analogy) – kitabah is a commutative contract (mu'awada) requiring equality; if the mukatab were freed instantly, the master would lose ownership without payment. The opposing proof is based on the master's complete ownership.
The hadith is zanni in both transmission and meaning.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
What is the practical consequence (thamarah) of the dispute? Under the Hanafi view, the mukatab can travel and trade freely, enhancing his ability to earn his freedom. Under the opposing view, he must obtain permission, potentially delaying his emancipation.
This is a clear example of ikhtilaf with real-world impact on the mukatab's freedom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہا تب کو خرید وفروخت کا اور سفر میں جانے کا اختیار حاصل ہو جاتا ہے ( سفر طویل ہو یا قصیر ) اگر چہ آقا نے اس کو سفر میں جانے سے منع ردیا ہو ۔ امام احمد اور ایک قول میں امام شافعی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ ان کا دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ آقا کی اجازت کے بغیر سفر میں نہیں جاسکتا۔ م مالک کا قول بھی یہی ہے۔ اور بعض شوافع نے طویل وقصیر سفر میں فرق کیا ہے۔ قـولـه واما عدم الخروج .... الخ - اور آقا کی ملک سے خارج نہ ہونے کی دلیل ایک تو حدیث مذکور ہے۔’ا مکاتب عبد بقى عليه درهم وسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کتابت ایک عقد معاوضہ ہے جو جانبین سے مساوات کو چاہتا ہے۔ حالانکہ فی الحال غلام کے آزاد ہونے سے بات جاتی رہتی ہے۔ یعنی اگر وہ فی الحال آزاد ہو جائے اور آقا کی ملک سے نکل جائے تو غلام کو اپنی ذات کا عوض یعنی آزادی حاصل ہو ائے گی۔ حالانکہ آقا کو ابھی مال حاصل نہیں ہوا تو مساوات جاتی رہی۔ اور اگر وہ ادائیگی مال کے بعد آزاد ہو تو مساوات متحقق ہوگی۔ کیونکہ غلام کو ایک قسم کی مالکیت بھی حاصل ہوئی اور ایک راہ سے اس کے ذمہ حق بھی ثابت ہوا۔
The mukatab [slave] gets the authority to buy and sell and to travel (whether the journey is long or short), even if the master forbade him from traveling. Imam Ahmad and, in one opinion, Imam al-Shafi'i also hold this. Their second opinion is that he cannot travel without the master's permission. Imam Malik's opinion is also this. And some Shafi'is differentiated between long and short journeys. His statement: 'And as for not exiting...' - the proof that he does not exit from the master's ownership is, first, the mentioned hadith: 'A mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him.' And the second proof is that kitabah is a commutative contract that requires equality between the two sides. If he became free immediately, equality would be lost, as the slave would get freedom without the master receiving payment. If he becomes free after payment, then equality is realized because the slave gets a kind of ownership while also being liable for the debt.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on a mukatab's right to travel. The commentator explains that according to the Hanafi school, a mukatab (a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom) has the authority to engage in trade and travel, even if his master explicitly forbids travel. This applies to both long and short journeys. The author then presents an inter-madhhab dispute: Imam Ahmad and one opinion of al-Shafi'i agree with the Hanafi view, while another Shafi'i opinion, along with Malik, requires the master's permission. Some Shafi'is distinguish between long and short journeys. The proof for the Hanafi position is twofold: (1) the hadith 'al-mukatab 'abd ma baqiya 'alayhi dirham' (a mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains due from him), indicating he remains a slave and thus the master's ownership persists, but the kitabah contract grants him certain rights; (2) qiyas (analogy): kitabah is a commutative contract (mu'awada) that requires equality. If the mukatab became free immediately, the master would give up ownership without receiving payment, violating equality. But since payment is deferred, the slave remains under the master's ownership until payment, yet the kitabah contract gives him the freedom to earn and travel to fulfill the payment. Thus, the master cannot prevent travel because it would hinder the mukatab's ability to earn and pay.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered into a contract (kitabah) with his master to purchase his freedom by paying a sum in installments.
کتابت (kitābah): The contract between a master and his slave whereby the slave agrees to pay a price to earn his freedom.
عقد معاوضہ (aqd mu'awada): A commutative contract where each party gives something in exchange for something else, like sale.
مساوات (musāwāt): Equality or equivalence between the two sides of a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the Hanafi proof for allowing a mukatab to travel without the master's permission?
A) The hadith 'al-mukatab 'abd ma baqiya 'alayhi dirham' proves the master cannot restrict the mukatab.
B) Kitabah is like a sale (mu'awada); if the mukatab were freed immediately, equality would be lost, so he must be allowed to earn.
C) The mukatab is totally free upon signing the contract.
D) The master's permission is needed only for long journeys.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a mukatab to travel without the master's permission for any journey, based on the nature of kitabah as a commutative contract that requires the ability to earn.

Master's Liability for Jinayah on Mukatabah
Ruling on master's liability for harming his mukatabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the master's liability for jinayah on his mukatabah and explain the qiyas used to derive it.

Core Idea
The master is liable for harming his mukatabah because her rights under kitabah make him like a stranger.

You have learned that a mukatabah is a slave who has contracted to earn her freedom. But what happens if the master himself harms her person or property? This passage clarifies that the master is not immune: he must compensate for the harm, though due to his residual ownership, the severe penalty of qisas is replaced by financial liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State clearly: what is the master required to pay for aggression on the mukatabah's person? On her property? What is explicitly excluded (qisas)?
The text distinguishes between jinayah on the person (diyah) and on property (value or equivalent).
2
Examine the proof (qiyas)
The Hanafi school uses qiyas: the mukatabah's relation to her own parts and property is like that of a stranger. Therefore, the master is liable just as he would be for damaging a stranger's property.
The analogy is explicit: the master is treated as a stranger (ajnabi) in this context.
3
Understand the role of shubhah
Why is qisas not applied? Because the master still holds partial ownership, creating a shubhah (ambiguity) that suspends the extreme penalty. Financial compensation remains wajib.
Shubhah is a key Hanafi principle to mitigate punishments where rights are mixed.
4
Consider the policy rationale
Without this liability, the master could destroy the mukatabah's property or harm her with impunity, defeating the purpose of the kitabah contract—her eventual freedom.
This is a purposive argument supporting the qiyas.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., master wounds the mukatabah's child who is also part of the kitabah), determine the ruling using the same qiyas.
The child is mentioned in the passage as also covered by the ruling.

قوله وان جنى عليها .... الخ - اگر آقا نے اپنی مکاتبہ باندی پر یا اس کے بچہ یا مال پر جنایت کی تو آقا کے ذمہ یہ جرم لازم ہوگا۔ جنی جنایت نفس کی صورت میں دیت اور جنایت مال کی صورت میں مثل مال یا اس کی قیمت دینی پڑے گی۔ کیونکہ پہلے گزر چکا کہ مکاتبہ کو پنے اجزاء کی خود ہی مستحق ہے البتہ شبہ کی وجہ سے قصاص لازم نہ ہوگا جیسا کہ شمس الائمہ بیہقی کی کفایہ میں مصرح ہے۔ اور اتلاف شبہ کی وجہ سے قصاص لازم نہ ہوگا۔ کہ مکاتب اور مکاتبہ کی کمائی اور ان کی ذوات کے حق میں آقامشل اجنبی کے ہوتا ہے تو اجنبی کی طرح وہ بھی ضامن وگا۔ اگر یہ حکم نہ دیا جائے تو آقا اس کے مال کو تلف کر ڈالے گا اور عقد کتابت سے جو مقصود ہے اس کا حصول محال ہو جائے گا۔
His statement: 'wa in jana 'alayha...' - if the master committed an aggression (jinayah) on his mukatabah, or on her child, or on her property, then the master is liable for that crime. If the aggression was on her person, he must pay diyah (blood money); if on her property, he must pay the equivalent or its value. Because it has already passed that the mukatabah is the one entitled to her own parts. However, due to shubhah (ambiguity of ownership), qisas (retaliation) is not obligatory, as stated in Shams al-A'imma al-Bayhaqi's Kifayah. And because of shubhah, qisas is not obligatory. Indeed, the earning of a mukatab or mukatabah and their persons are like a stranger in relation to the master; so like a stranger, he is also liable. If this ruling were not given, the master would destroy her property, and the purpose of the kitabah contract would become impossible.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage addresses the liability of the master when he commits an aggression (jinayah) upon his mukatabah's life, her child (who is also a slave, but the child's ownership is separate?), or her property. The ruling is that the master is liable for compensation: if he kills or wounds her, he must pay diyah (unless it is intentional murder, but here due to shubhah no qisas); if he destroys her property, he must pay the equivalent or value. The proof is that the mukatabah is entitled to her own body parts (as established earlier) and her earnings, so the master is like a stranger in respect to them. However, because he still has some ownership rights, there is shubhah that prevents qisas but does not prevent financial compensation. The practical reasoning is that without such liability, the master could arbitrarily destroy the mukatabah's property and frustrate the kitabah contract.

Key Terms
جنایت (jināyah): A wrongful act causing harm to person or property, leading to liability for diyah or compensation.
شبہ (shubhah): Ambiguity in ownership or right that prevents the application of severe penalties like qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master kills his mukatabah, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) He is subject to qisas (retaliation).
B) He must pay diyah (blood money) but no qisas.
C) He is not liable because he owns her.
D) The mukatabah becomes free automatically.

Key Takeaway
The master is liable for harming his mukatabah's person or property because the kitabah contract grants her independent rights, but shubhah prevents qisas.

Defective Kitabah: Wine, Pig, or Slave's Price as Consideration
Ruling on defective kitabah with invalid consideration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kitabah with invalid consideration (wine, pig, or unknown price) and explain why each case renders the contract fasid.

Core Idea
Kitabah with wine, pig, or an unspecified price is fasid because the consideration is either non-property or grossly uncertain.

Kitabah is a contract of manumission where the slave pays a consideration to earn freedom. For such a contract to be valid, the consideration must be lawful property (mal) and known to both parties. This passage from Al-Hidayah examines three defective scenarios: when the consideration is wine, pig, or the slave's own price. Understanding these defects clarifies a foundational Hanafi principle: the consideration must be a valid mal and free from jahl fahish (gross ignorance).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the act is a kitabah contract made by a Muslim master with his slave. The ruling is that the contract is fasid (defective) in each of the three cases.
The ruling is by consensus of the three Hanafi imams.
2
Analyze the first defect: non‑property
For wine and pig, they are not considered mal for a Muslim. Therefore they cannot serve as valid consideration (badal). This makes the contract fasid.
This applies even if the master is a dhimmi, because the slave's right is to pay permissible property.
3
Analyze the second defect: jahl fahish
When the consideration is the slave's own price, it is unknown in amount, genus, and description. This is excessive ignorance (jahl fahish) that renders the contract fasid.
The text compares this to kitabah for an unspecified garment or animal.
4
Trace the proof and talil
The proof is the consensus of the Hanafi imams. The reasoning (talil) relies on the principle that a commutative contract requires a valid and known consideration.
The fasid contract can be corrected if the defect is removed (e.g., specifying the price).

اگر کسی مسلمان نے اپنے مسلمان غلام کو شراب یا خنزیر کے عوض یا خود اس غلام کی قیمت کے عوض مکاتب کیا۔ بان قال کا تبنک علی قیمتک۔ تو یہ کتابت با جماع احناف ائمہ ثلاثہ فاسد ہے (اسی طرح اگر آقازمی اور غلام مسلمان ہو تب بھی خمر وخنزیر پر کتابت صحیح نہ ہوگی ) اول یعنی خم و خنزیر پر کتابت کا فاسد ہونا تو اس لئے ہے کہ شراب اور خنزیر مسلمان کے حق میں متقوم مال نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے بدل ہونے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا تو عقد کتابت بلا بدل ہوالہذ ا فاسد ہوگا۔ قـولـه اما الاول .... الخ - كتابت برخمر اور کتابت بر خنزیر۔ در حقیقت دو مسئلے ہیں اس لئے تعبیر اما الاول سے نہیں ہونی چاہیے۔ لیکن جہت فساد جو عدم تحقق مالیت ہے اس میں چونکہ دونوں متحد ہیں تو گویا دونوں مسئلے ایک ہی ہیں ۔ اس لئے ان دونوں کو اول سے تعبیر کر دیا۔ نفس مسئلہ کی تحریر میں اس نکتہ کی طرف اشارہ بھی موجود ہے کہ موصوف نے ذکر قیمت کے وقت علی حرف جار کا اعادہ کیا ہے۔ ذکر خنزیر کے وقت اس کو نہیں لائے ۔ قـولــه واما الثاني ... الخ - دوم یعنی نفس غلام کی قیمت پر کتابت کا فاسد ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ غلام کی قیمت جنس ووصف جودة و ردار قادر مقدار ہر اعتبار سے مجہول ہے۔ جہالت قدر تو یہ ہے کہ قیمت سو دو سو ہے یا ہزار کچھ معلوم نہیں ۔ اور جہالت نفس اس لئے ہے کہ قیمت کبھی سونے سے ہوتی ہے کبھی چاندی ہے۔ یعنی قیمت کبھی دراہم ہوتے ہیں بھی دنا نیر، اور جہالت وصف یوں ہے کہ جید یا ردی یا اوسط کچھ بیان نہ کی ہو کہ یہ بالا تفاق فاسد ہے کیونکہ را بہ اور ثوب مختلف جنس ہے اور جو چیز مجبول الجنس ہو وہ ذمہ میں دین ثابت نہیں ہوتی جیسے نکاح میں ہے۔
Chapter on defective kitabah. He said: If a Muslim makes his slave a mukatab for wine or pig or for his (the slave's) price, the kitabah is fasid. As for the first, because wine and pig are not owned by a Muslim, as they are not property in his regard, so they are not suitable as a substitute, hence the contract is fasid. As for the second, because the slave's price is unknown in quantity, genus, and description, so the ignorance is gross, and it becomes as if he made kitabah for a garment or an animal. And because it specifies what is the requirement of a fasid contract, for the fasid contract requires payment of value. Translation: This chapter is on defective kitabah. When a Muslim makes his slave a mukatab for wine or pig or for the slave's own price, then the kitabah is fasid. The first (wine/pig) is because a Muslim is not entitled to wine and pig, as they are not property in his right, so they cannot be a substitute, thus the contract is fasid. As for the second (the slave's price), because the slave's price is unknown in quantity, genus, and description, so the ignorance is gross, and it becomes as if he made kitabah for a garment or an animal. And because it is an explicit stipulation of what a fasid contract requires, for a fasid contract requires payment of value. Commentary: 'fasl'... The rules of defective kitabah are brought after valid kitabah, due to inferiority. 'qawlahu wa idha kataba al-muslim...' - If a Muslim made his Muslim slave kitabah for wine or pig or for the slave's own price, then this kitabah is fasid by consensus of the three Hanafi imams. (Similarly if the master is dhimmi and the slave Muslim, still valid on khamr/khinzir? Actually it says kitabah will not be valid). The first (wine/pig) being fasid is because wine and pig are not property for the Muslim, so can't be valid consideration. 'qawlahu amma al-awwal...' - Kitabah on wine and kitabah on pig are actually two issues, so the expression 'amma al-awwal' is not fitting. But since the cause of fasd (lack of being property) is common, they are treated as one. The author points out that at the time of mentioning 'price' he repeated the preposition 'ala', but not when mentioning pig. 'qawlahu wa amma al-thani...' - The second, i.e., kitabah on the slave's price, being fasid is because the slave's price is unknown in genus, description, quality, and quantity. Ignorance of amount: whether it's one hundred, two hundred, or a thousand. Ignorance of genus: whether it is gold, silver, dirhams, or dinars. Ignorance of description: whether good, bad, or average. It is fasid by consensus, because a garment and an animal are of different genus, and a thing of unknown genus cannot be established as a debt in the dhimma, as in marriage.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage introduces the types of defective kitabah (kitabah fasidah). The ruling states that if a Muslim master makes his slave a mukatab with the consideration being wine (khamr), pig (khinzir), or the slave's own price (qimah), the kitabah is fasid. The reasons: (1) For wine and pig, they are not considered property (mal) according to a Muslim, so they cannot be valid substitutes in a commutative contract. This applies even if the master is a dhimmi and the slave is Muslim, because the slave's right is to pay permissible property. (2) For the slave's price, it is unknown (majhul) in three respects: quantity (amount), genus (gold, silver, etc.), and description (quality). This is excessive ignorance (jahl fahish) that invalidates the contract, similar to making kitabah on an unspecified garment or animal. Additionally, specifying the price as the slave's own value explicitly makes the contract fasid because a fasid contract already requires payment of value (as in a fasid sale). The commentary notes that wine and pig are technically two separate issues but are grouped together due to the common cause of non-property. It also discusses nuances of the preposition usage. The consensus (ijma) of the three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is cited for this ruling.

Key Terms
کتابت فاسدہ (kitābah fāsidah): A kitabah contract that is defective due to an invalid consideration (badal) or excessive ignorance, potentially corrigible if the defect is remedied.
قیمت (qīmah): The market price or value of the slave, which must be specified in amount, genus, and description to avoid jahl fahish.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is kitabah for the slave's own price considered fasid?
A) Because the slave cannot own property.
B) Because the price is unknown in amount, genus, and description.
C) Because the master must receive something other than the slave's value.
D) Because it leads to riba.

Key Takeaway
Kitabah is fasid if the consideration is not valid mal (wine, pig) or if it is subject to jahl fahish (unknown price); the ruling is based on Hanafi consensus and the principles of commutative contracts.

Invalid Kitabah: Wine, Pig, or the Slave's Own Value
Ruling and proofs for invalid kitabah plus objection/response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a kitabah contract is fasid when the consideration is wine, pig, or the slave's own value, and explain the two proofs: lack of property status and excessive ignorance (jahala fahisha).

Core Idea
A kitabah contract is invalid if the consideration is not valid property or is unknown.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya, al-Marghinani explains the ruling on invalid kitabah. The key issue is the validity of the consideration ('iwaḍ). When the consideration is wine or pig, it is not considered property (mal) for a Muslim, thus cannot serve as a valid substitute. When the consideration is the slave's own value, the value is unknown in multiple respects, leading to excessive ignorance that invalidates the contract. The passage also addresses a potential objection: why is a kitabah for an unspecified slave (e.g., average) valid while one for his value is invalid? The response distinguishes between incidental and intentional obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and ruling
The author states three scenarios: kitabah for wine, for pig, or for the slave's value. The ruling for all three is that the kitabah is fasid (invalid).
Note that the Hanafis categorize the contract as fasid (invalid but potentially correctable) rather than batil (void).
2
Analyze the first proof: consideration not valid property
For wine and pig, the reasoning is that wine and pig are not considered property (mal mutaqawwim) for a Muslim. Therefore, they cannot be a valid substitute ('iwaḍ) in a contract.
This is based on the Hanafi definition of mal as something customarily valued and permissible to benefit from.
3
Analyze the second proof: excessive ignorance (jahala fahisha)
For the slave's value, the value is unknown in three respects: quantity (amount), type (dirhams, dinars, etc.), and description/quality. This constitutes excessive ignorance, which invalidates the contract.
The text compares it to a kitabah for an unspecified cloth or animal, also invalid.
4
Consider the additional reasoning: specifying the invalid contract's requirement
The author adds that specifying the slave's value directly indicates the invalid contract's requirement because an invalid contract obligates only the value.
This reinforces the invalidity from a different angle.
5
Address the objection and response
Objection: if a kitabah for an unspecified slave (e.g., average) is valid, why is kitabah for his value invalid? Response: in the valid case, the obligation of value arises incidentally (hukman) due to the specification of the slave, not intentionally (qasdan). In the invalid case, the value is specified intentionally but is unknown.
Examples of calf and fetus illustrate incidental validity.

كتابت فاسدہ کا بیان ... مسلمان نے اپنے غلام کو شراب خنزیر یا اسکی قیمت پر مکاتب بنایا تو کتابت فاسد ہے

قوله واذا كاتب المسلم. الخ - اگر کسی مسلمان نے اپنے مسلمان غلام کو شراب یا خنزیر کے عوض یا خود اس غلام کی قیمت کے عوض مکاتب کیا۔ بان قال کا تبنک علی قیمتک۔ تو یہ کتابت با جماع احناف ائمہ ثلاثہ فاسد ہے (اسی طرح اگر آقازمی اور غلام مسلمان ہو تب بھی خمر وخنزیر پر کتابت صحیح نہ ہوگی ) اول یعنی خم و خنزیر پر کتابت کا فاسد ہونا تو اس لئے ہے کہ شراب اور خنزیر مسلمان کے حق میں متقوم مال نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے بدل ہونے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا تو عقد کتابت بلا بدل ہوالہذ ا فاسد ہوگا۔
قـولـه اما الاول .... الخ - كتابت برخمر اور کتابت بر خنزیر۔ در حقیقت دو مسئلے ہیں اس لئے تعبیر اما الاول سے نہیں ہونی چاہیے۔ لیکن جہت فساد جو عدم تحقق مالیت ہے اس میں چونکہ دونوں متحد ہیں تو گویا دونوں مسئلے ایک ہی ہیں ۔ اس لئے ان دونوں کو اول سے تعبیر کر دیا۔ نفس مسئلہ کی تحریر میں اس نکتہ کی طرف اشارہ بھی موجود ہے کہ موصوف نے ذکر قیمت کے وقت علی حرف جار کا اعادہ کیا ہے۔ ذکر خنزیر کے وقت اس کو نہیں لائے ۔
قـولــه واما الثاني ... الخ - دوم یعنی نفس غلام کی قیمت پر کتابت کا فاسد ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ غلام کی قیمت جنس ووصف جودة و ردار قادر مقدار ہر اعتبار سے مجہول ہے۔ جہالت قدر تو یہ ہے کہ قیمت سو دو سو ہے یا ہزار کچھ معلوم نہیں ۔ اور جہالت نفس اس لئے ہے کہ قیمت کبھی سونے سے ہوتی ہے کبھی چاندی ہے۔ یعنی قیمت کبھی دراہم ہوتے ہیں بھی دنا نیر، اور جہالت وصف یوں ہے کہ جید یا ردی یا اوسط کچھ بیان نہ کی ہو کہ یہ بالا تفاق فاسد ہے کیونکہ را بہ اور ثوب مختلف جنس ہے اور جو چیز مجبول الجنس ہو وہ ذمہ میں دین ثابت نہیں ہوتی جیسے نکاح میں ہے۔
سوال . اگر آقا نے مطلق غلام یا اوسط درجہ کے غلام پر مکاتب کیا تو یہ ہمارے اور امام مالک کے نزدیک صحیح ہے (اگر چہ امام شافعی اور امام احمد اس کے خلاف ہیں ) اس صورت میں اوسط درجہ کا غلام یا اس کی قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر وہ مکاتب اوسط درجہ کے غلام کی قیمت پیش کرے تو آقا کو اس کے قبول کرنے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ اگر قیمت کے عوض مکاتب کرنا فاسد ہوتا تو یہاں بھی صحیح نہ ہوتا۔
اور جب اس میں صحیح ہے تو پیش نظر مسئلہ میں جب اس نے قیمت کی تصریح کی ہے تو اس میں بھی کتابت صحیح ہونی چاہیے۔ جواب پیش نظر مسئلہ میں اگر قیمت واجب ہو تو اس قیمت کا وجوب قصد ا ہو گا نہ کہ حکماً کیوں کہ اس میں قیمت کی تصریح ہے اور قیمت مجہول ہے تو قصداً قیمت واجب کرنا ناممکن ہے اور اعتراض میں جو مسئلہ مذکور ہے۔ اس میں اگر قیمت واجب ہو تو قیمت کا وجوب حکما ہوگانہ کہ قصداً کیونکہ اس میں عبد کی تصریح ہے نہ کہ قیمت کی۔ اور شی کبھی حکما اور ضمن ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اگر چہ وہ قصد اثابت نہیں ہوتی۔ چنانچہ عجل ( گوسالہ ) کا اضحیہ جائز نہیں۔ لیکن ماں کے تابع ہو کر جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح جنین کی بیع جائز نہیں لیکن ماں کے تابع ہو کر جائز ہے۔ قوله ولا نه تنصيص .... الخ - نفس غلام کی قیمت پر کتابت کے فاسد ہونے کی دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس میں عقد فاسد کے حکم کی تصریح ہے کیونکہ عقد فاسد کا موجب و مقتضی یہی ہے کہ قیمت واجب ہو۔ ولـو نـص عـلـى العقد الفاسد ينعقد بوصف الفساد
فكذا اذا نص على موجبه
Chapter on invalid kitabah. He said: If a Muslim makes his slave a mukatab in exchange for wine or pig or for his value, the kitabah is invalid. As for the first, because the Muslim is not entitled to wine and pig, as they are not property in his regard, so they are not suitable as a substitute, thus the contract becomes invalid. As for the second, because his value is unknown in quantity, type, and description, so the ignorance is excessive, and it is like if he made him a mukatab for a garment or an animal, and because it is a specification of what necessitates the invalid contract, for the invalid contract necessitates the value.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya explains the ruling on an invalid kitabah (contract of manumission by payment) when the consideration is wine, pig, or the slave's own value. The author first states the ruling that such a kitabah is invalid. He then gives two reasons: (1) Wine and pig are not considered property (mal) for a Muslim, so they cannot serve as a valid substitute ('iwad) in a contract, rendering it invalid. (2) The slave's value is unknown (majhul) in quantity, type, and description, leading to excessive ignorance (jihalah fahishah), which invalidates the contract, similar to a kitabah for an unspecified cloth or animal. Additionally, specifying the value directly indicates the invalid contract's requirement (muqtada) because an invalid contract only obligates the value, not the specified non-property or unknown. The commentary then elaborates on the first reason, noting that both wine and pig are unified in their lack of property status, hence the author uses 'first' for both. For the second reason, it explains the types of ignorance: ignorance of amount (whether 100, 200, or 1000), of type (whether gold, silver, dirhams or dinars), and of quality (fine, average, or poor). This excessive ignorance makes the contract invalid by consensus of the Hanafi imams. The passage then addresses a potential objection: if making a mukatab for an unspecified slave (like an average slave) is valid, why is making it for the slave's value invalid? The answer is that in the valid case, the obligation of value arises incidentally (hukman) due to the specification of the slave, not intentionally (qasdan). In the invalid case, the value is specified intentionally but is unknown, so it cannot be valid. Examples of the calf (عجل) following the mother in sacrifice and the fetus following the mother in sale illustrate this incidental validity. Finally, the second reason is reiterated: specifying the invalid contract's requirement (value) makes the contract invalid because specifying an invalid contract's requirement renders the contract itself invalid.

Key Terms
كتابت فاسدہ (kitābat fāsida): An invalid contract of manumission by payment, where the defect is in the consideration (e.g., wine, pig, or unknown value).
عوض (ʿiwaḍ): The consideration or substitute in a contract, which must be valid property (mal mutaqawwim) and known.
جہالت (jahāla): Ignorance or uncertainty about the object of a contract; excessive jahala invalidates the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a kitabah contract invalid when the consideration is the slave's own value?
A) Because the value is not property
B) Because the value is unknown in quantity, type, and description
C) Because the slave cannot pay his own value
D) Because the contract is a gift, not a sale

Key Takeaway
A kitabah contract is fasid (invalid) when the consideration is not valuable property or is unknown in quantity, type, or quality.

Paying Wine in Invalid Kitabah: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on freedom via payment of wine in invalid kitabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar on whether a slave is freed by paying wine after an invalid kitabah, and state the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Paying wine can free a slave in invalid kitabah according to Zahir al-Riwayah, but Hanafi imams differ on the rationale.

In a previous lesson, we saw that a kitabah (contract of manumission) on wine or pig is invalid. But does this mean the slave is never freed by paying wine? On the contrary, the Hanafi school holds that the slave may still be freed, though the imams differ on the exact condition. This passage presents a parsing exercise: you must understand each imam's reasoning and the hierarchy of authority within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common ruling and the dispute
The matn (Quduri) states a general rule: if the slave pays the wine, he is freed. However, Zufar, Abu Yusuf, and Abu Hanifa each offer a different rationale or condition.
The mukhtalaf fih is whether and under what conditions payment of wine effects freedom.
2
Parse Zufar's position
Zufar says the slave is not freed by paying wine; he must pay the value (qima) of the wine. His reason: the true substitute (badal) in a contract is the value, not the wine itself.
Zufar considers wine as non-property for the purpose of being a valid substitute.
3
Parse Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf holds that the slave is freed either by paying the wine (as a substitute in form, badal suratan) or by paying its value (as a substitute in meaning, badal ma'nan).
He gives the slave an option: pay wine or pay value.
4
Parse Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa restricts freedom to cases where the master explicitly conditioned manumission on payment of the wine, e.g., 'If you pay these, you are free.' Then the freedom is by the condition (shart), not by the invalid kitabah contract.
This aligns with the principle that a condition can operate even if the underlying contract is invalid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the distinction from carrion
The text states 'there is no distinction in Zahir al-Riwayah' – the matn's ruling (freed by paying wine) is authoritative. It then explains why wine and pig differ from carrion and blood: wine and pig are considered property in a general sense (mal fi al-jumla), so the contract's meaning (freedom for consideration) can apply; carrion is not property at all, so freedom only occurs if explicitly conditioned.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شراب ادا کر دی تو آزاد ہو جائے گا یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء
قال فان ادى الخمر عتق وقال زفر لا يعتق الا باداء قيمة الخمر لان البدل هو القيمة وعن ابى يؤسف انه يعتق باداء الخمر لانه بدل صورة ويعتق باداء القيمة ايضا لأنه هو البدل معنى وعن ابي حنيفة انه انما يعتق باداء عين الخمر اذا قال ان اديتهما فانت حر لانه حينئذ يكون العتق بالشرط لا بعقد الكتابة وصار كما اذا كاتب على ميتة او دم ولا فصل فى ظاهر الرواية ووجه الفرق بينهما وبين الميتة ان الخمر والخنزير مال في الجملة فامكن اعتبار معنى العقد فيهما وموجبه العتق عند اداء العوض المشروط واما الميتة فليست يمال اصلا فلا يمكن اعتبار معنى العقد فيه فاعتبر فيه معنى الشرط وذلك بالتنصيص عليه
ترجمہ پھر اگر ادا کر دی شراب تو آزاد ہو جائے گا امام زفر فرماتے ہیں کہ آزاد نہ ہو گا۔ مگر قیمت خمر ادا کرنے سے کیونکہ عوض تو قیمت ہی ہے امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ اداء خمر سے آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ عوض ہے صورۃ اور اداء قیمت سے بھی آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ عوض ہے معنی ، اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ عین خمر ادا کرنے س اسی وقت آزاد ہو گا جب آقا نے یہ کہا ہو ۔ ان ادی تھا فانت حر کیونکہ اس صورت میں آزادی بوجہ شرط کے ہوگی نہ کہ عقد کتابت کی وجہ سے اور ایسا ہو گیا جیسے مردار یا خون پر مکاتب کیا۔ اور ظاہر الروایہ میں کوئی فرق نہیں اور خمر و خنزیر اور مردار میں وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ خمر وخنزیر فی الجملہ مال ہے تو ان میں معنی عقد کا اعتبار کرناممکن ہے اور اسکا مقتضی آزاد ہو جانا ہے عوض مشروط کی ادائیگی کے وقت، رہا مردار سودہ بالکل مال نہیں ہے۔ پس اس میں معنی عقد کا اعتبار کرنا ناممکن ہے تو اس میں معنی شرط کا اعتبار کیا گیا اور یہ اس کی تصریح ہی سے ہوگا۔ تشریح قوله فان ادى الخمر ... الخ - پھر اگر مکاتب مذکورہ پہلے مسئلہ میں شراب یا خر میری دیدے یا دوسرے مسئلہ میں اپنی
If he pays the wine, will he be freed or not? The statements of the jurists. He said: If he pays the wine, he is freed. Zufar said: He is not freed except by paying the value of the wine, because the substitute is the value. From Abu Yusuf it is narrated that he is freed by paying the wine, because it is a substitute in form, and he is also freed by paying the value, because it is the substitute in meaning. From Abu Hanifa it is narrated that he is only freed by paying the actual wine if he (the master) said: 'If you pay these two (the wine and the pig?) you are free,' because then the manumission is by the condition, not by the contract of kitabah, and it is like if he made a mukatab for carrion or blood. And there is no distinction in the Zahir al-Riwayah. And the distinction between them and carrion is that wine and pig are property in a sense, so it is possible to consider the meaning of the contract in them, and its requirement is freedom upon payment of the stipulated substitute. As for carrion, it is not property at all, so it is not possible to consider the meaning of the contract in it, so the meaning of the condition is considered in it, and that is by specifying it.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage discusses a further issue: if a slave has been made a mukatab in exchange for wine (or pig), and then he actually pays wine, is he freed? There is ikhtilaf among the Hanafi imams. The text presents the positions: (1) The author of the matn (Quduri) says generally that he is freed (by paying wine). (2) Zufar says he is not freed unless he pays the value of the wine, because the valid substitute (badal) is the value, not the wine itself. (3) Abu Yusuf holds that he is freed either by paying the wine (as a substitute in form) or by paying the value (as a substitute in meaning). (4) Abu Hanifa restricts freedom to cases where the master explicitly said 'If you pay these (the wine and pig), you are free' — then the manumission is by the condition (shart) and not by the kitabah contract itself. In that case, it is like a kitabah on carrion or blood, which does not effect freedom via the contract. The text then clarifies the distinction: wine and pig are considered property (mal) in a general sense, so the meaning of the contract (i.e., freedom in exchange for consideration) can be applied; thus, the slave is freed upon paying the wine as stipulated. Carrion and blood are not property at all, so the contract cannot carry that meaning; freedom only occurs if the master explicitly made it a condition. Therefore, in the case of wine and pig, there are multiple views, but the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to the Zahir al-Riwayah is that the slave is freed by paying the wine, as per the matn.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (ẓāhir al-riwāya): The well-known and authoritative transmitted rulings from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
بدل (badal): The substitute or consideration in a contract; in this context, the wine or its value.
شرط (shart): A condition; when the master says 'if you pay these, you are free,' the manumission is conditioned on payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, what is the ruling if a slave pays wine after an invalid kitabah?
A) He is not freed.
B) He is freed only if he also pays value.
C) He is freed.
D) He is freed only if the master explicitly conditioned it.

Key Takeaway
Despite an invalid kitabah on wine, the Hanafi mufta bihi holds that the slave is freed by paying the wine, based on the principle that wine is considered property in a general sense.
