Kitabah on a Slave of Medium Value: Validity and Price Obligation
Inter-madhhab dispute on kitabah with implicit price obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on kitabah for a slave of medium value and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i/Hanbali positions.

Core Idea
Kitabah on a medium-value slave is valid; the price becomes wajib by ruling, not by stipulation.

In this passage, the Hanafi school defends the validity of a kitabah contract made on a slave of unspecified but moderate value. The key is understanding how the price obligation arises implicitly—by ruling (hukman)—rather than by direct agreement. This distinction resolves the objection that the consideration is unknown and would render the contract fasid. We will follow the school's reasoning and compare it with opposing views.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the exact ruling: kitabah on an absolute or medium-value slave is valid (sahih). The price of the slave becomes wajib such that if the slave offers it, the master must accept.
Note the mention of Imam Malik's agreement; this is a rare Maliki-Hanafi convergence.
2
Identify the Opponent and Their View
The text names Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad as opponents. They presumably hold that an unspecified price creates gharar (uncertainty), invalidating the contract.
Their exact proof is not quoted; we infer from the response.
3
Follow the Opponent's Proof
The opponent argues: if kitabah in exchange for price were fasid, then this case (where no price is specified) would also be invalid. Since the price is unknown, intentional obligation of price (qasdan) is impossible.
This sets up the Hanafi counter-distinction.
4
Analyse the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response distinguishes: when the slave is specified, the price obligation is by ruling (hukman), not intentional (qasdan). A thing can become obligatory implicitly, just as a calf can be sacrificed following its mother, or a fetus sold following its mother.
These analogies show that implicit obligation is valid in Shariah.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: In the Hanafi school, the master is compelled to accept the price and free the slave. In the Shafi'i/Hanbali view, the contract would be invalid, so no obligation arises.
This difference directly affects the slave's ability to earn freedom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المكاتب
سوال . اگر آقا نے مطلق غلام یا اوسط درجہ کے غلام پر مکاتب کیا تو یہ ہمارے اور امام مالک کے نزدیک صحیح ہے (اگر چہ امام شافعی اور امام احمد اس کے خلاف ہیں ) اس صورت میں اوسط درجہ کا غلام یا اس کی قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر وہ مکاتب اوسط درجہ کے غلام کی قیمت پیش کرے تو آقا کو اس کے قبول کرنے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ اگر قیمت کے عوض مکاتب کرنا فاسد ہوتا تو یہاں بھی صحیح نہ ہوتا۔ 
اور جب اس میں صحیح ہے تو پیش نظر مسئلہ میں جب اس نے قیمت کی تصریح کی ہے تو اس میں بھی کتابت صحیح ہونی چاہیے۔ جواب پیش نظر مسئلہ میں اگر قیمت واجب ہو تو اس قیمت کا وجوب قصد ا ہو گا نہ کہ حکماً کیوں کہ اس میں قیمت کی تصریح ہے اور قیمت مجہول ہے تو قصداً قیمت واجب کرنا ناممکن ہے اور اعتراض میں جو مسئلہ مذکور ہے۔ اس میں اگر قیمت واجب ہو تو قیمت کا وجوب حکما ہوگانہ کہ قصداً کیونکہ اس میں عبد کی تصریح ہے نہ کہ قیمت کی۔ اور شی کبھی حکما اور ضمن ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اگر چہ وہ قصد اثابت نہیں ہوتی۔ چنانچہ عجل ( گوسالہ ) کا اضحیہ جائز نہیں۔ لیکن ماں کے تابع ہو کر جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح جنین کی بیع جائز نہیں لیکن ماں کے تابع ہو کر جائز ہے۔ قوله ولا نه تنصيص .... الخ - نفس غلام کی قیمت پر کتابت کے فاسد ہونے کی دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس میں عقد فاسد کے حکم کی تصریح ہے کیونکہ عقد فاسد کا موجب و مقتضی یہی ہے کہ قیمت واجب ہو۔ ولـو نـص عـلـى العقد الفاسد ينعقد بوصف الفساد
فكذا اذا نص على موجبه
Question: If the master makes a kitabah on an absolute slave or a slave of medium value, then this is valid according to us and Imam Malik (although Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad are opposed to it). In this case, the slave of medium value or its price becomes wajib to the extent that if that mukatab presents the price of the slave of medium value, the master will be compelled to accept it. If kitabah in exchange for price were fasid, then here too it would not be valid. And when it is valid here, in the present case when he has specified the price, the kitabah should also be valid. Answer: In the present case, if the price is wajib, then the obligation of that price will be intentional (qasdan) not by ruling (hukman), because in it there is specification of price and the price is unknown, so intentionally making the price wajib is impossible. And in the objection that is mentioned, if the price is wajib, then the obligation of price will be by ruling, not intentionally, because in it there is specification of the slave, not price. And a thing sometimes becomes proven by ruling and implicitly even if it is not proven intentionally. For example, the udhiyah (sacrifice) of a calf is not permissible, but it is permissible following its mother. Similarly, the sale of a fetus is not permissible, but it is permissible following its mother. His saying: 'And because the specification...' etc. - The second reason for the invalidity of kitabah on the price of the same slave is that in it there is specification of the ruling of a fasid contract, because the necessitation and requirement of a fasid contract is that the price becomes wajib. And if one specifies the fasid contract, it is concluded with the description of fasid, so likewise if one specifies its requirement.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage opens with a question about the validity of kitabah (contract of manumission) on a slave of medium value. The Hanafi school, along with Imam Malik, holds that it is valid, while Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold it invalid. The reasoning provided is that when the slave's price is paid, the master must accept it because the price becomes wajib (obligatory) as a substitute for the slave's value. The commentator then addresses an objection: if kitabah in exchange for price were fasid, then the same would apply here. The response distinguishes between intentional (qasdan) and ruling-based (hukman) obligation. When the slave is specified, the obligation of price is by ruling (implicit), not by direct stipulation. Analogies are given: the permissibility of sacrificing a calf following its mother, and selling a fetus following its mother. Finally, the text discusses the second reason for invalidity when one specifies the price itself: that amounts to specifying the effect of a fasid contract, and specifying the effect is like specifying the contract itself.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitabah with his master for manumission in exchange for a consideration.
کتابت (kitabah): The contract of manumission between master and slave.
قیمت (qimat): Price; the value of the slave used as consideration in the kitabah.
عقد فاسد (aqd fasid): Invalid contract; a contract that is defective in some condition but not completely void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a master makes kitabah on a slave of medium value, what is the ruling on the price?
A) The price becomes wajib, and the master must accept it if offered.
B) The price is not wajib; the slave must offer the slave himself.
C) The contract is invalid because the price is unknown.
D) The slave is freed immediately without paying anything.

Key Takeaway
Kitabah on a medium-value slave is valid; the price is wajib implicitly (hukman), not by explicit stipulation, and the master must accept it.

Payment of Wine in Kitabah and the Positions of the Hanafi Imams
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wine payment in kitabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions of the Hanafi imams regarding payment of wine in kitabah and identify the mufta bihi according to Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
A slave under kitabah is freed by paying wine or his own price, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of wine as consideration in a kitabah contract. While wine is generally not considered valuable property (mutaqawwim) for Muslims, the Hanafi school recognizes it as property (mal) in a general sense, allowing it to be valid consideration under certain conditions. The three leading imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—have differing narrations, but the established ruling (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that the slave is freed upon payment of wine or his own price, without needing the master to explicitly condition it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
Understand the core question: If a mukatab (slave under kitabah) pays wine (khamr) instead of the agreed consideration, does the slave become free?
Wine is not usually valid consideration in Islamic contracts due to its prohibition.
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah Position
According to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) in the well-established narrations, the slave is freed by paying the specific wine or by paying the price of his own person. This is the mufta bihi.
No distinction is made between whether the master conditioned payment or not; the contract of kitabah itself suffices.
3
Examine Imam Zufar's Objection
Imam Zufar holds that the slave is only freed by paying the value (qimah) of wine, not the wine itself, because the substitute in a fasid contract is always the price.
Zufar's view is based on analogy with a fasid sale.
4
Analyze the Narrawir (Nawadir) Narrations from Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa
Abu Yusuf has a narration that the slave is freed by wine in form (surah) and by price in meaning (ma'na). Abu Hanifa in Nawadir restricts freedom to when the master explicitly said 'If you pay the wine, you are free.'
These narrations are less authoritative than Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi and the Distinction from Carrion
The relied-upon view is the Zahir al-Riwayah position. The key distinction is that wine and pig (khinzir) are property in a general sense, so the contract can operate; carrion and blood are not property at all, so only a condition can effect freedom.
The ruling shows the Hanafi methodology of considering the nature of the subject matter.

لا يعتق الآ باداء قيمة نفسه وقال الزيلعي في التبيين وفي بعض نسخ الهدايه. وقال زفر لا يعتق الا باداء قيمة الخمر. وهو غلط من الكاتب .
قوله وعن ابي يوسف .... الخ - امام ابو یوسف سے روایت ہے کہ اگر مکاتب مذکور بعینہ شراب ادا کرے تو وہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ صوری عوض ہے اور اگر قیمت ادا کرے تب بھی آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ معنوی بدل ہے۔ شیخ سغناقی فرماتے ہیں کہ صاحب ہدایہ نے جو حکم ذکر کیا ہے۔ یہ ہمارے علماء ثلاثہ سے ظاہر الروایہ ہے جیسا کہ مبسوط اور ذخیرہ میں مذکور ہے۔ پس یہاں تحریر کا حق یہ تھا کہ نہ موصوف امام ابو یوسف کی تخصیص کرتے اور نہ کلمہ عن لاتے۔ صاحب عنایہ کہتے ہیں کہ شیخ سغناقی کی یہ بات اس وقت صحیح ہوگی جب و يعتق باداء القیمۃ ایضاً میں القیمۃ کے الف لام کو نفس مکاتب سے کنایہ مانا جائے اور اگر یہ خمر سے کنایہ ہو ۔ جیسا کہ غایہ البیان میں مذکور ہے تو اس صورت میں قیمت خمر کی ادائیگی سے مکاتب کا آزاد ہونا ممکن ہے امام ابو یوسف سے غیر ظاہر الروایہ ہو۔
الحاصل ... ائمہ ثلاثہ سے ظاہر الروایہ یہ ہے کہ کا تب مذکور بعینہ خمر ادا کرنے سے اور اپنی ذات کی قیمت ادا کرنے سے آزاد ہو جائے گا اور امام ابو یوسف سے جو روایت بکلمہ عن ذکر کی گئی ہے اس میں القیمۃ کے الف لام کو اگر خمر کے بدلہ میں مانا جائے تو مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ عین خمر کی ادائیگی سے بھی آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ روایت امام ابو یوسف سے ظاہر الروایہ کے خلاف ہے۔ قوله وعن ابي حنيفة ... الخ - اور نوادر میں امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ ادائیگی خمر سے آزاد اسی وقت ہو گا جب آقا نے اس سے یہ کہا ہو ان اديت الخمر فانت حر کہ اس صورت میں مکاتب آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اور اس پر اپنی ذات کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ وجوب قیمت تو اس لئے ہے کہ عقد فاسد میں جب معقود علیہ تلف کر دیا جائے تو اس میں قیمت ہی واجب ہوتی ہے جیسے بیع فاسد میں اگر مشتری کے پاس صبیح ہلاک ہو جائے تو اس کی قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اور عشق کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں یہ آزادی شرط مذکوران ادیت کی وجہ سے ہوگی نہ کہ عقد کتابت کی وجہ سے۔ اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے مردار یا خون کے عوض مکاتب کیا کہ ان کی ادائیگی سے اسی وقت آزاد ہوتا ہے جب آقا نے یہ کہا ہو ۔ اذا ادیت الميتة او الخمر فانت حر
قوله ولا فصل .. الخ - خمر اور خنزیر کے مسئلہ کی بابت ظاہر الروایہ میں شرط کے ذکر و عدم ذکر کا کوئی فرق نہیں بلکہ ان ادبیت الخمر فانت حر کہے یا نہ کہے بہر دو صورت آزاد ہو جائے گا اور نوادر کی روایت میں فرق ہے۔ سوظاہر الروایہ میں خمر دختر بر اور میتہ دوم کے درمیان وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ خمر و خنزیر تو فی الجملہ مال ہے۔ اگر چہ مسلمان کے حق میں متقوم مال نہیں ہے۔ تو مالیت کے اعتبار سے اس میں معنی عقد یعنی
Then if he pays wine, will he be freed or not? Statements of the jurists. He said: If he pays wine, he is freed. And Zufar said: He is not freed except by paying the price of wine, because the substitute is the price. And from Abu Yusuf: He is freed by paying wine because it is a substitute in form, and he is also freed by paying the price because it is the substitute in meaning. And from Abu Hanifa: He is only freed by paying the specific wine if he said 'If you pay them, you are free', because then freedom is by the condition, not by the contract of kitabah, and it becomes like when he makes kitabah on carrion or blood. And there is no distinction in Zahir al-Riwayah. And the aspect of distinction between them and carrion is that wine and pig are property in a general sense, so it is possible to consider the meaning of the contract in them, and its requirement is freedom upon payment of the stipulated consideration. As for carrion, it is not property at all, so it is not possible to consider the meaning of the contract in it, so the meaning of the condition is considered in it, and that is by specification. Translation: Then if he pays wine, he will be freed. Imam Zufar says he will not be freed except by paying the price of wine because the substitute is the price. From Imam Abu Yusuf it is narrated that he is freed by paying wine because it is a substitute in form, and he is also freed by paying the price because it is the substitute in meaning. And from Imam Abu Hanifa it is narrated that he is only freed by paying the specific wine when the master has said 'If you pay them, you are free' because in that case freedom is due to the condition, not due to the kitabah contract, and it becomes like when kitabah is made on carrion or blood. And in Zahir al-Riwayah there is no distinction. And the distinction between them and carrion is that wine and pig are property in a general sense, so it is possible to consider the meaning of the contract in them, and its requirement is freedom at the time of paying the stipulated consideration. As for carrion, it is not property at all, so it is not possible to consider the meaning of the contract in it, so the meaning of the condition is considered in it, and that is only by specification. Elaboration of his saying 'If he pays wine' etc. - Then if the aforementioned mukatab in the first case pays wine or khamr, or in the second case pays the price of his own person, he will be freed whether the master said to him 'If you pay it, you are free' or not. This is the Zahir al-Riwayah from our three imams. As for Zufar, he says he will not be freed without paying the price of his own person, because in a fasid kitabah, the substitute and consideration is the price just as in a fasid sale. Warning: In the copy of Hidayah before us, the phrase is 'And Zufar said he is not freed except by paying the price of wine.' The author of Kafi says this copy is problematic because it contradicts the common narrations in books. The common narration is: 'He is not freed except by paying the price of himself.' And al-Zayla'i said in al-Tabyin: 'In some copies of Hidayah it says: And Zufar said he is not freed except by paying the price of wine. This is an error of the scribe.' His saying 'And from Abu Yusuf...' - From Abu Yusuf it is narrated that if the aforementioned mukatab pays wine specifically, he is freed because it is a substitute in form, and if he pays the price, he is also freed because it is a substitute in meaning. Shaikh Sighnaqi says that the ruling mentioned by the author of Hidayah is the Zahir al-Riwayah from our three imams, as mentioned in Mabsut and Dhakhirah. So the right thing in writing was not to specify Imam Abu Yusuf alone and not to bring the word 'an'. The author of 'Inayah says that Shaikh Sighnaqi's statement is correct only if the definite article 'al' in 'al-qimat' in 'wa yu'taqu bi-ada'i al-qimati ayḍan' is taken as a reference to the mukatab himself. And if it is a reference to wine, as mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan, then the freeing of the mukatab by paying the price of wine is a non-Zahir al-Riwayah from Abu Yusuf. Conclusion: The Zahir al-Riwayah from the three imams is that the mukatab is freed by paying specific wine and by paying the price of his own person. And the narration from Abu Yusuf mentioned with the word 'an', if the definite article in 'al-qimat' is taken as a substitute for wine, the meaning is that he is freed by paying the specific wine. And it is obvious that this narration is contrary to Zahir al-Riwayah from Abu Yusuf. His saying 'And from Abu Hanifa...' - And in Nawadir, from Abu Hanifa it is narrated that he is freed by paying wine only when the master said 'If you pay the wine, you are free' because in that case the mukatab is freed, and the price of his own person becomes wajib. The obligation of price is because in a fasid contract when the subject matter is destroyed, its price becomes wajib, like in a fasid sale if the commodity perishes with the buyer, its price becomes wajib. And the reason for freedom is that in this case the freedom is due to the mentioned condition, not due to the kitabah contract. And it becomes like when kitabah is made on carrion or blood, that they are freed only when the master said 'If you pay the carrion or the blood, you are free.' His saying 'And there is no distinction...' - Regarding the issue of wine and pig, in Zahir al-Riwayah there is no distinction between mentioning the condition or not; rather, whether he says 'If you pay the wine, you are free' or not, in both cases he is freed. And in the Nawadir narration there is a distinction. So in Zahir al-Riwayah, the distinction between wine, pig, and carrion is that wine and pig are property in a general sense, even though for a Muslim they are not mutaqawwim property. So by virtue of being property, the meaning of the contract (i.e., ...)
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a mukatab (slave under kitabah) pays wine (khamr) instead of the agreed consideration. There are three positions within the Hanafi school. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, both Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani agree that the slave is freed by paying wine itself or by paying the price of his own person, without needing the master to specify a condition. This is because wine is considered property (mal) in a general sense, so the contract of kitabah can be effective. However, Imam Zufar holds that only paying the price (value) frees him, because the actual substitute is the price. Imam Abu Yusuf has a narration that paying wine frees him in form (surah) and paying price frees him in meaning (ma'na). Imam Abu Hanifa has a narration in Nawadir that restricts freedom to when the master explicitly conditioned payment of wine, likening it to kitabah on carrion or blood. The text also clarifies a variant reading in some copies of Hidayah regarding Zufar's view. The relied-upon view is the Zahir al-Riwayah position of the three imams.

Key Terms
خمر (khamr): Wine; intoxicating drink.
بدل (badal): Substitute; the consideration in a contract.
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The apparent/well-established narrations from Imam Muhammad's six core books.
نوادر (Nawadir): Rare transmissions not in the six core books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah, what is the ruling if a mukatab pays wine to his master?
A) The slave is freed only if the master explicitly conditioned payment.
B) The slave is freed by paying wine or the price of himself.
C) The slave is not freed; only the price of wine frees him.
D) The contract is void because wine is not valid property.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, wine is considered property in a general sense, making it valid consideration in a kitabah contract; the relied-upon view is that the slave is freed upon payment of wine or his own price.

intermediate
6 min
Mukatab's Freedom in Fasid Kitabah with Wine
Intra-Hanafi dispute on freedom conditions for mukatab in fasid kitabah with wine.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi Zahir al-Riwayah position on a mukatab's freedom in a fasid kitabah involving wine or his own value, and distinguish it from the positions of Zufar and the Nawadir narration of Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Paying wine or own value in fasid kitabah frees the mukatab, but compensation is due.

This lesson explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: when a mukatab (slave under kitabah) agrees to pay wine or his own value in a fasid (invalid) contract, does he become free? The authoritative Zahir al-Riwayah says yes, unconditionally, but rare narrations and other Hanafi imams differ. We will dissect the legal reasoning and determine the mufta bihi (operative) position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
The core question: In a fasid kitabah contract where the consideration is wine (khamr) or the slave's own value, what conditions trigger the mukatab's freedom?
Focus on the effect of the fasid contract and the nature of wine as mal (property).
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah Position
The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that the mukatab becomes free by paying the very wine or his own value, regardless of whether the master conditioned freedom on payment.
This is based on the idea that wine is mal in general, and in a fasid contract, the value or the formal substitute can effect transfer.
3
Examine Opposing Views
Imam Zufar holds that freedom only occurs by paying the slave's own value, not wine. In Nawadir, Abu Hanifa is reported to require an explicit condition (e.g., 'If you pay wine, you are free') and then the slave must pay his value.
Zufar argues wine is not muqawwam for Muslims; Abu Hanifa (Nawadir) sees the fasid contract as incapable of effecting freedom without a condition.
4
Analyse the Legal Reasoning
The Zahir al-Riwayah analogizes to fasid sale: if the sold item perishes, its value is due. Here, the slave's person (raqabah) cannot be returned, so value is due. Wine is treated as a valid substitute because it has monetary value, unlike maytah (carrion) or blood.
Key distinction: wine is mal, though not muqawwam for Muslims, but it can still be a formal exchange.
5
Apply Tarjih
The commentator affirms the Zahir al-Riwayah as the relied-upon position. The variant reading of Zufar attributing his view to 'paying value of wine' is declared a scribal error.
The mufta bihi is: the mukatab is freed by paying wine or own value without condition, but then must work (sa'i) to pay his own value.

عین خمر ادا کرنے سے آزاد ہو گیا تو اپنی قیمت میں مزدوری کرے
واذا عتق باداء عين الخمر لزمه ان يسعى فى قيمته لانه وجب عليه رد رقبته لفساد العقد وقد تعذر بالعتق فيجب رد قيمته كما فى البيع الفاسد اذا تلف المبيع . قال ولا ينقص عن المسمى ويزاد عليه لانه عقد فاسد فيجب القيمة عند هلاك المبدل بالغة ما بلغت كما فى البيع الفاسد وهذا لان المولى ما رضى بالنقصان والعبد رضى بالزيادة كيلا يبطل حقه فى العتق اصلا فتجب القيمة بالغة ما بلغت وفيما اذا کاتبه على قيمته يعتق باداء القيمة لانه هو البدل وامكن اعتبار معنى العقد فيه واثر الجهالة في الفساد بخلاف ما اذا كاتبه على ثوب حيث لا يعتق باداء ثوب لانه لا يوقف فيه على مراد العاقد لاختلاف اجناس الثوب فلا يثبت العتق بدون ارادته
ترجمہ جب وہ آزاد ہو گیا عین خمر ادا کر کے تو لازم ہے اس پر یہ کہ معایت کرے اپنی قیمت میں ۔ کیونکہ اس پر اپنا رقبہ پھیرنا واجب ہوا فساد عقد کی وجہ سے حالانکہ یہ عشق کیوجہ سے متعذر ہو گیا تو اپنی قیمت واپس کرنا واجب ہوگا جیسے بیج فاسد میں ہوتا ہے جب صبیح تلف ہو جائے اور کم نہیں کی جائے گی بیان کردہ مقدار سے اور اس پر زیادتی کی جاسکتی ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ تو عقد فاسد ہے تو مبدل تلف ہونے پر قیمت واجب ہوگی جہاں تک بھی پہنچے جیسے بیچ فاسد میں ہوتا ہے۔ اور یہ اس لئے ہے کہ آقا نقصان پر راضی نہیں ہوا اور غلام زیادتی پر راضی ہو گیا تاکہ محق میں اس کا حق باطل نہ ہو۔ لہذا قیمت واجب ہوگی جہاں تک بھی پہنچے ۔ اور غلام کو اس کی قیمت پر مکاتب کرنے کی صورت میں اداء قیمت سے آزاد اس لئے ہو جائے گا کہ قیمت ہی عوض ہے اور اس میں معنی عقد کا لقبار کرنا ممکن ہے اور جہالت کا اثر صرف فساد میں ہے بخلاف اس کے جب کپڑے پر مکاتب کیا کہ کپڑا ادا کرنے سے آزاد نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس میں عاقد کی مراد پر آگہی نہیں ہو سکتی۔ اجناس ثوب کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے پس اس کے ارادہ کے بغیر آزادی ثابت نہ ہوگی۔
تشریح قوله واذا عتق ... الخ ۔ مسئلہ مذکورہ میں جب مکاتب بعید شراب ادا کر کے آزاد ہو گیا تو وہ اپنی قیمت میں سعایت کریگا۔ یعنی اپنی قیمت کما کر آقا کو دے گا۔ کیونکہ یہاں فاسد عقد کی وجہ سے رد رقبہ واجب ہے مگر اسکے آزاد ہو جانے کی وجہ سے رہ رقبہ متعذر ہے۔ اس لئے قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ جیسے بیج فاسد میں اگر مشتری کے پاس طبع ہلاک ہو جائے تو قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے لیکن ظاہر الروایہ وہی ہے جو پہلے مذکور ہوا۔ قوله ولا ينقص الخ ۔ جس قیمت میں مکاتب مذکور سعایت کرے گا اس میں اس مقدار سے کم نہیں کیا جائے گا جو آقا کی طرف بیان ہوئی تھی۔ ہاں اس میں اضافہ ہو سکتا ہے جہاں تک بھی ہو۔ اس لئے کہ یہ عقد فاسد واقع ہوا تھا جیسے بیچ فاسد میں مبیع تلغب ہونے کے وقت اس کی قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے جتنی بھی ہو ایسے ہی یہاں بھی واجب ہوگی۔
Book of Mukatab. 128. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah volume 12: If he gives the value of his own self, he becomes free, whether the master said to him 'If you pay me, you are free' or not. This is the Zahir al-Riwayah from our three Imams. Imam Zufar says he will not become free without paying the value of his own self, because in invalid kitabah, the exchange is that very value, as in invalid sale.
Caution: In the copy under consideration of Hidayah, like some other copies, the phrasing is thus: 'And Zufar said: He does not become free except by paying the value of khamr.' The author of Kafi says that this copy is problematic because it is against the general narrations of books. In general narrations it is: 'He does not become free except by paying the value of his own self.' And al-Zayla'i said in al-Tabyin: 'In some copies of Hidayah: And Zufar said: He does not become free except by paying the value of khamr. This is a mistake by the scribe.'
His statement: 'And from Abu Yusuf... etc.' - It is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that if the mukatab pays the very wine (khamr), he becomes free, because it is a formal exchange; and if he pays its value, he also becomes free, because it is a meaningful substitute. Sheikh al-Sighnaqi says: The ruling that the author of Hidayah mentioned is the Zahir al-Riwayah from our three Imams, as mentioned in al-Mabsut and al-Dhakhirah. So here the right thing to write would be not to specify Imam Abu Yusuf and not to bring the word 'an'. The author of al-Inayah says that Sheikh al-Sighnaqi's statement will be correct when in 'wa yu'taqu bi ada'i al-qimati aydan' the lam-alif of 'al-qimah' is considered a kinayah for the mukatab himself. And if it is kinayah for khamr, as mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan, then in this case, (the possibility of) the mukatab becoming free by paying the value of khamr from Imam Abu Yusuf would be non-Zahir al-Riwayah.
Conclusion: The Zahir al-Riwayah from the three Imams is that the mukatab becomes free by paying the very wine and by paying the value of his own self. And in the narration mentioned from Abu Yusuf with the word 'an', if the lam-alif of 'al-qimah' is considered as a substitute for khamr, then the meaning would be that he becomes free by paying the very wine as well. And it is clear that this narration from Abu Yusuf is against the Zahir al-Riwayah. His statement: 'And from Abu Hanifah... etc.' - And in Nawadir it is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifah that freedom by paying wine occurs only when the master said to him: 'If you pay the wine, you are free.' In that case the mukatab becomes free, and the value of his own self becomes obligatory upon him. The obligatoriness of the value is because in a fasid contract, when the subject matter is destroyed, its value becomes obligatory, as in fasid sale if the sold item perishes in the possession of the buyer, its value becomes obligatory. And the reason for freedom is that in this case the freedom occurs due to the mentioned condition (if you pay) and not due to the contract of kitabah. And this becomes like the case where kitabah is made for maytah or blood: freedom from paying them occurs only when the master said: 'If you pay the maytah or wine, you are free.'
His statement: 'And there is no distinction... etc.' - Regarding the issue of wine and swine, in Zahir al-Riwayah there is no difference whether the condition is mentioned or not; rather, whether he says 'If you pay the wine, you are free' or not, in both cases he becomes free. But in the Nawadir narration there is a difference. So in Zahir al-Riwayah, the reason for the difference between wine, swine, and maytah and blood is that wine and swine are in general wealth, even though they are not muqawwam wealth for a Muslim. So, in terms of value, it is possible to consider in them the meaning of the contract, i.e., exchange. And the cause of the meaning of the contract is realized only when the conditioned exchange is paid. As for maytah and blood, they are absolutely not wealth, so it is impossible to consider the meaning of the contract in them. Therefore, in them the meaning of the condition will be considered, but this consideration occurs only when the master explicitly stated the condition, such as saying: 'If you pay the maytah or blood, you are free.'
(If) he becomes free by paying the very wine, then he should work for his value.
And if he becomes free by paying the very wine, it becomes obligatory upon him to strive for his value, because returning his person (raqabah) became obligatory due to the fasid contract, and it becomes impossible due to freedom, so returning his value becomes obligatory, as in fasid sale when the sold item perishes. He said: (The value) is not decreased below the named amount and may be increased, because it is a fasid contract, so the value at the time of destruction of the substitute is obligatory, whatever it may reach, as in fasid sale. This is because the master did not consent to a decrease, and the slave consented to an increase so that his right to freedom is not invalidated entirely. Thus the value becomes obligatory whatever it may reach. And in the case where he made kitabah for his value, he becomes free by paying the value, because it is the substitute, and it is possible to consider the meaning of the contract in it, and the effect of ignorance is only in fasid. Unlike the case where he made kitabah for a garment, where he does not become free by paying a garment, because the intention of the contracting parties cannot be known there due to the different types of garments. Thus freedom is not established without his intention.
Translation: When he becomes free by paying the very wine, it is incumbent upon him to strive for his value. Because returning his person became obligatory due to the fasid contract, but it became impossible due to freedom, so he must return his value, as in fasid sale when the sold item perishes. And it will not be reduced from the stated amount and may be increased over it. Because this is a fasid contract, so the value at the destruction of the substitute is obligatory, whatever it reaches, as in fasid sale. And this is because the master did not consent to a decrease and the slave consented to an increase, so that his right to freedom is not invalidated. Hence the value becomes obligatory whatever it reaches. And in the case where he made kitabah for his value, he becomes free by paying the value, because it is the substitute and it is possible to consider the meaning of the contract in it, and the effect of ignorance is only in fasid. Unlike the case where he made kitabah for a garment, as he does not become free by paying a garment, because the intention of the contracting parties cannot be known there due to the different types of garments. Hence freedom is not established without his intention.
Explanation of his statement 'And if he becomes free... etc.': In the mentioned issue, when the mukatab becomes free by paying the wine, he will work for his value, i.e., earn his value and give it to the master. Because here, due to the fasid contract, the return of the person is obligatory, but due to his freedom, the return of the person is impossible. Therefore his value becomes obligatory, as in fasid sale if the sold item perishes with the buyer, his value becomes obligatory. But the Zahir al-Riwayah is only what was mentioned earlier. His statement 'And it is not decreased... etc.': The value that the said mukatab will work for is not decreased from the amount that was stated by the master. Yes, it can be increased, however much it may be. Because this was a fasid contract, as in fasid sale, at the time of destruction of the sold item, its value is obligatory whatever it is. Similarly here it will be obligatory.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah discusses the legal rulings concerning a mukatab (a slave under a contract of kitabah) when the kitabah contract is fasid (invalid) and the consideration agreed upon is wine (khamr) or the slave's own value. The passage presents multiple opinions from the Hanafi school, highlighting the distinction between Zahir al-Riwayah (the authoritative transmitted rulings) and Nawadir (rare narrations). The core issue is whether paying the wine itself or its value results in freedom, and what obligations arise thereafter.

The author begins by stating the position of the 'three imams' (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani) from the Zahir al-Riwayah: if the mukatab pays the value of his own person (qimat nafsihi), he becomes free regardless of whether the master conditioned freedom on payment. This is because in a fasid kitabah, the true consideration is the value of the slave, analogous to a fasid sale where the price is the substitute for the sold item. Then the opinion of Imam Zufar is noted: he disagrees, holding that the slave does not become free until he pays his own value, because the consideration in a fasid contract is only that value.

A cautionary note follows about a variant reading in some copies of al-Hidayah, which attributes to Zufar the statement that the slave does not become free except by paying the value of khamr (wine). The commentator, following al-Zayla'i, declares this a scribal error, as the correct reading is 'value of himself'.

Next, a narration from Abu Yusuf is discussed: if the mukatab pays the very wine (ayn al-khamr), he becomes free because it is a formal exchange (suri 'iwad). If he pays its value (qimat al-khamr), he also becomes free because it is a meaningful substitute (ma'nawi badal). However, the commentator notes that this narration is not part of the Zahir al-Riwayah. The author of al-Inayah clarifies that the phrase 'by paying the value' (bi-ada' al-qimah) could mean either the value of the slave or the value of the wine, depending on interpretation.

The passage then presents a narration from Abu Hanifa in the Nawadir: freedom by paying wine occurs only if the master explicitly conditioned it by saying 'If you pay the wine, you are free.' In that case, the slave is freed but must pay his own value, because the freedom is due to the condition, not the fasid contract. The reason for obligating the value is analogized to a fasid sale where the sold item is destroyed. This is similar to the case of maytah (carrion) or blood: they are not property at all, so freedom only results if the master stated the condition.

The distinction between wine/swine and maytah/blood is explained: wine and swine are considered property (mal) in a general sense, though not muqawwam (valuable property) for Muslims. Therefore, the meaning of exchange can be considered in them, and this meaning realizes the contract's purpose once the exchange is paid. Maytah and blood are not property at all, so only the condition can effect freedom.

The final part covers the consequence of freedom: if freed by paying wine, the mukatab must work (sa'i) to pay his own value, because the fasid contract requires returning his person (raqabah), which is impossible after freedom. So he compensates with his value. The value is not limited to the named sum but can be higher, as in a fasid sale where the market value at the time of destruction is due. However, this is only according to the non-Zahir al-Riwayah opinion; the Zahir al-Riwayah was already stated. Also, if the kitabah was made for a specific garment, paying that garment does not free him because the types of garments vary, making intent unclear.

In summary, this passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi legal discussion, weighing the authoritative transmitted rulings against rare narrations and analogical reasoning.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract with his master, agreeing to pay a sum for his freedom.
کتابت فاسدہ (kitabah fasidah): An invalid kitabah contract due to impermissible consideration (e.g., wine) or other defects.
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwayah): The authoritative transmitted rulings from the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) as recorded in the six major works of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah of the Hanafi school, what happens when a mukatab pays the very wine (ayn al-khamr) agreed upon in a fasid kitabah contract?
A) He becomes free only if the master explicitly said 'If you pay wine, you are free'
B) He becomes free immediately without any condition, but must then work to pay his own value
C) He does not become free at all, because wine is not valid consideration
D) He becomes free only if he pays the value of the wine, not the wine itself

Key Takeaway
In a fasid kitabah, paying wine or one's own value effects freedom under the Hanafi Zahir al-Riwayah, but the mukatab must then compensate with his value.

The Kitabah Price: No Reduction Allowed, Ignorance Makes Fasid
Ruling with proof explaining price reduction and ignorance effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the kitabah price cannot be reduced below the specified amount and explain why ignorance of the price results in a fasid rather than a batil contract.

Core Idea
In kitabah, the master's consent is limited to the specified price; the slave may pay more, and ignorance of price makes the contract fasid, not batil.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah explains two critical points about the price in a kitabah (manumission) contract. First, the master has obligated the contract at a specific amount, so he is not willing to accept less; the slave may voluntarily pay more to secure his freedom. Second, an objection is raised: if the price is unknown, why is the contract not completely void (batil) like in the case of cloth? The commentator clarifies that ignorance of the price makes the contract defective (fasid) but not void, because the price can be determined by valuation, unlike the type of cloth which is too ambiguous.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
The text states that the kitabah price cannot be reduced below the musamma (specified amount); it may be increased. This protects the master's consent.
The master's right is tied to the specific amount he agreed to.
2
Locate the reason (talil)
The master obligated the contract at the musamma; he is not pleased with less. The slave agrees to more to avoid losing freedom. Reasoning is based on mutual consent.
The slave's agreement to more is voluntary, not coerced.
3
Analyze the objection regarding ignorance
An objector argues: if kitabah on cloth with unknown type is batil, why does unknown price not make the contract batil? The objection uses qiyas.
The objector assumes all ignorance has the same effect.
4
Examine the response and distinction
The commentator distinguishes: ignorance of price is resolvable by valuation, so contract is fasid; ignorance of cloth type is not resolvable (types vary widely), so contract is batil.
This highlights the Hanafi principle that resolvable ambiguity leads to fasid, not batil.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a slave is made mukatab on his price, he pays an amount that satisfies all valuers (e.g., the highest estimate) and is freed.
The price becomes known through expert valuation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وهذا لان المولى ... الخ - او پر جو یہ مذکور ہوا کہ قیمت مسمی سے کم نہیں کی جائے گی ہاں زائد ہوسکتی ہے اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ آقا نے عقد کتابت کو مقدار سمی میں واجب کیا ہے تو وہ اس سے کم پر راضی نہیں ہوا۔ البتہ غلام زائد مقدار سے راضی ہو گیا ہے تا کہ اس کا حق عشق فوت نہ ہو جائے اس لئے کہ اگر وہ زائد مقدار سے راضی نہیں ہوتا تو آقا اس کو آزاد کرنے سے باز رہے گا اور مکاتب کے ہاتھ سے شرف حریت جاتا رہے گا۔ نیز اس لئے بھی کہ جب مکاتب نے عقد فاسد پر اقدام کیا ہے۔ جب کہ وہ جانتا ہے کہ عقد فاسد میں قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے تو وہ قیمت کی ادائیگی سے راضی ہو گیا۔ گو قیمت مقدار سمی سے زائد ہو۔
قوله وفيما كاتب ... الخ - مسئلہ کے شروع میں علی خمر او خنزیر کے بعد جو او علی قیمتہ کہا تھا یہ اسی کی طرف راجع ہے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر غلام کو اسکی قیمت پر مکاتب کیا تو وہ اپنی قیمت ادا کر کے آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ قیمت ہی اس کا عوض ہے اور اس میں معنی عقد کتابت کا اعتبار کرنا بھی ممکن ہے۔ بایں طور کہ مکاتب اتنی قیمت ادا کرے جس میں قیمت لگانے والوں کو کوئی اختلاف نہ رہے۔ مثلاً ایک نے اس کی قیمت تمیں درہم لگائی دوسرے نے ۳۵ تیسرے نے ۴۰ اور مکاتب نے ۴۰ ادا کر دیئے تو وہ اپنی قیمت ادا کرنے والا ہو گیا۔
قوله واثر الجهالة ... الخ - سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ کپڑے کی طرح یہاں قیمت بھی تو مجہول ہے تو جیسے کپڑے پر مکاتب کرنے کی صورت میں کپڑا ادا کرنے سے آزادی نہیں ہوتی۔ ایسے ہی قیمت کی ادائیگی سے بھی آزادی نہیں ہونی چاہیے بلکہ عقد باطل ہو جانا چاہیے؟
جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قیمت کی جہالت کا اثر صرف عقد کے فاسد ہونے میں ہے کہ اس سے عقد فاسد ہوگا نہ کہ باطل اور فاسد عقد میں یہی قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے۔ بخلاف کپڑے کے کہ خالی کپڑا کہنے سے آقا کی مراد معلوم نہیں ہوسکتی۔ کیونکہ کپڑے کی اجناس مختلف ہیں ۔
His saying: And this is because the master... - Regarding what was mentioned that the price will not be reduced from the specified amount, yes it can exceed. The reason is that the master made the kitabah contract obligatory at the specified amount, so he is not pleased with less than that. However, the slave agreed to a greater amount so that his right of freedom would not be lost, because if he did not agree to more, the master would refrain from freeing him and the honor of freedom would leave the mukatab's hand. Also because when the mukatab proceeded with a fasid contract, knowing that in a fasid contract the price is obligatory, he agreed to pay the price even if it exceeds the specified amount.
His saying: And regarding what he made a kitabah on... - At the beginning of the issue after 'on wine or pork' he said 'or on his price', this refers back to that. Meaning: If the slave is made a mukatab on his price, he will be freed by paying his price, because the price is his compensation, and it is possible to consider the meaning of kitabah in that. In that the mukatab pays such a price as to leave no dispute among the valuers. For example, one valued him at 30 dirhams, another at 35, a third at 40, and the mukatab paid 40, then he has paid his price.
His saying: And the effect of ignorance... - This is a response to a question. The question: Just as in the case of cloth, here also the price is unknown, so just as in the case of kitabah on cloth, paying the cloth does not effect freedom, similarly paying the price should not effect freedom, rather the contract should be batil?
The summary of the answer: The effect of ignorance of the price is only in making the contract fasid, not batil, and in a fasid contract this price is obligatory. Unlike cloth, because saying merely 'cloth' does not reveal the master's intent, since cloth has different types.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. It addresses two issues: (1) the price in a kitabah contract cannot be less than the specified amount, but can be more, and (2) the effect of ignorance (jahala) of the price. The commentator explains that the master has obligated the contract at a specific amount, so he does not consent to less. The slave may agree to more to secure his freedom. Regarding kitabah on the slave's own price, the slave is freed by paying an amount that equalizes valuers' estimates. Then an objection is raised: if ignorance of the price makes the contract invalid in the case of cloth, why does it not invalidate here? The answer: ignorance makes the contract fasid, not batil, and in a fasid contract the price is still obligatory. In the case of cloth, the ambiguity is greater because cloth types vary, so the contract is batil. In the case of price, the amount can be determined by valuation, so the contract is fasid but valid for payment.

Key Terms
قیمت مسمی (qimat musamma): The specified price agreed upon in the kitabah contract.
عقد فاسد (aqd fasid): A contract that is defective in some condition but can be corrected; unlike batil, it has legal effects.
جہالت (jahala): Ignorance or ambiguity about the subject matter or price that affects contract validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a slave is made a mukatab on his own price, and three valuers estimate his price at 30, 35, and 40 dirhams, what amount must he pay to be freed?
A) The average of the three estimates (35 dirhams)
B) The lowest estimate (30 dirhams)
C) The highest estimate (40 dirhams) so that there is no dispute
D) Any amount agreed upon with the master

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi kitabah, the price must be known; if it is unknown but determinable, the contract is fasid and the slave is freed upon paying an amount that resolves all disputes among valuers.

Kitabah on a Specific Item of Another: The Hanafi Position and Disputes
Ruling on kitabah with another's specific item, with intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on kitabah when the consideration is a specific item of another, distinguish between Zahir al-Riwayah and the narration of Hasan, and compare with Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali positions.

Core Idea
Kitabah on a specific item of another is invalid in Zahir al-Riwayah because ability to deliver is a condition in compensatory contracts.

This lesson examines a nuanced issue in the law of kitabah: what if the master stipulates a consideration that is a specific item belonging to a third party? The Hanafi school has an established position (Zahir al-Riwayah) and a rare narration that differ, and other schools weigh in. Understanding this dispute reveals a key distinction between compensatory and non-compensatory contracts.

Guided Path
1
Examine the base ruling
The matn states that kitabah on a specific item of another is invalid because the slave cannot deliver it. This is the Zahir al-Riwayah.
The text uses 'la yajuz' indicating invalidity (fasid).
2
Identify the exception for currency
If the consideration is dirhams/dinars, even if owned by another, the contract is valid because they become a debt in the dhimmah.
Currency is not specific in compensations according to Hanafis.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Hasan ibn Ziyad narrates that Abu Hanifa allows it by analogy to mahr. Understand the analogy and the rebuttal.
The rebuttal distinguishes between compensatory and non-compensatory contracts.
4
Compare inter-madhhab positions
Maliki allows the slave to buy or pay price; Shafi'i and Hanbali invalidate even for currency.
Shafi'i and Hanbali treat currency as specific in all contracts.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Zahir al-Riwayah is relied upon; the narration of Hasan is nawadir.
The fatwa position is that kitabah on a specific item of another is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسی طرح مکاتب بنایا معین فی کے بدلے جو کسی کی ہے تو یہ کتابت جائز نہیں
قال و کذالک ان کاتبه على شيء بعينه لغيره لم يجز لانه لا يقدر على تسليمه ومراده شيء يتعين بالتعين حتى لو قال كاتبتك على هذه الالف الدرهم وهى لغيره جاز لانها لا تتعين فى المعاوضات فيتعلق بدراهم دين في الذمة فيجوز وعن ابي حنيفة رواه الحسن انه يجوز حتى اذا ملكه وسلمه يعتق فان عجز يرد في الرق لان المسمى مال والقدرة على التسليم موهومة فاشبه الصداق. قلنا ان العين في المعاوضة معقود عليه والقدرة على المعقود عليه شرط للصحة اذا كان العقد يحتمل الفسخ كما في البيع بخلاف الصداق في النكاح لان القدرة على ما هو المقصود بالنكاح ليس بشرط فعلى ما هو تابع فيه اولى

۱۳۱
كتاب المكاتب
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ اور امام ابوحنیفہ سے حسن نے روایت کی کہ عقد جائز ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر وہ اسکا مالک ہو کر آقا کو دے دے تو آزاد ہو جائے گا اور اگر عاجز ہو جائے تو رقیق کر دیا جائیگا۔ کیونکہ بھی مسمی مال ہے اور سپرد کرنے کی قدرت بھی موہوم ہے تو مہر کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ معاوضہ میں مال مین ہی معقود علیہ ہوتا ہے اور قدرت بھی موہوم ہے تو مہر کے مشابہ ہو گیا ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ معاوضہ میں مال عین ہی معقود علیہ ہوتا ہے اور معقود علیہ پر قدرت کا ہونا شرط ہے صحت عقد کے لئے جب کہ عقد قابل فسخ ہو جیسے بیع میں ہوتا ہے۔ بخلاف مہر کے جو نکاح میں ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ نکاح سے جو مقصود ہے اس پر قدرت کا ہونا شرط نہیں تو مہر جو تابع ہے اس پر قدرت بدرجہ اولی شرط نہ ہو گی۔
تشریح قوله على شئ بعينه لغيره .... الخ - لغیرہ لفظ شی سے حال ہے اورشی گونکرہ ہے جوذ والحال نہیں ہوسکتا۔ لیکن یہاں بعینہ صفت کی وجہ سے تخصیص آگئی اس لئے ذوالحال ہونا صحیح ہو گیا۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر آقا نے غلام کو کسی دوسرے شخص کی معین چیز مثلاً گھوڑے، کپڑے یا غلام کے عوض مکاتب کیا۔ تو ہمارے اور امام شافعی واحمد کے نزدیک یہ بھی فاسد ہے۔ کیونکہ غلام دوسرے کی چیز سپرد کرنے سے قاصر ہے۔ امام مالک کے نزدیک جائز ہے اب غلام وہ چیز خرید کر دے دے اور اگر مالک فروخت نہ کرے تو اسکی قیمت دے دے۔ قوله و مراده شي ... الخ - علی شی بعینہ میں لفظ شی سے امام محمد کی مراد ایسی چیز ہے جو معین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتی ہے۔ جیسے کپڑا، یہ گھوڑا ، یہ غلام ، یہ مکان وغیرہ اور اگر چہ وہ چیز متعین نہ ہوتی ہو۔ بان قال كاتبتك على هذه الالف الدراهم حالانکہ وہ ہزار درہم کسی غیر کی ملک ہے تو عقد کتابت جائز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ در اہم و دنانیر گوامانت و غصب میں متعین ہو جاتے ہیں۔ لیکن معاوضات میں متعین نہیں ہوتے ۔ پس عقد کتابت ایسے درا ہم سے متعلق ہو گا۔ جو غلام کے ذمہ قرض ہوں گے۔ امام شافعی و امام احمد کے یہاں اس صورت میں بھی کتابت جائز نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ ان کے یہاں درا ہم ودنا نیر بھی متعین ہوتے ہیں۔
قوله رواه الحسن .. الخ - صورت مسئلہ کی تشریح یہ ہے کہ غیر کی چیز پر مکاتب کرنے میں دو صورتیں ہیں ۔ وہ چیز معین کرنے سے متعین ہوگی جیسے گھوڑا ، غلام وغیرہ یا متعین نہ ہوگی۔ جیسے نقود یعنی در اہم ودنا نیر اول کی پھر دو صورتیں ہیں ۔ مالک اس کو جائز رکھے گایا نہیں۔ اگر جائز نہ رکھا تو پھر دو صورتیں ہیں۔مکاتب یا تو کسی ذریعہ سے اس کا مالک ہو کر آقا کو سپر دکرے گا یا نہیں۔ یہ کل چار صورتیں ہوئیں ۔ پس اگر وہ چیز معین کرنے سے متعین نہ وہ تو عقد کتابت جائز ہوگا ۔ جیسا کہ سابق قول میں بیان ہو چکا اور اگر متعین ہو جاتی ہو اور مالک اس کی اجازت نہ دے اور مکاتب کسی ذریعہ سے اس کا مالک بھی نہ ہو سکے تو ظاہر الروایہ میں جائز نہ ہوگا۔ اور حسن کی روایت میں جائز ہوگا۔ اب اگر مکا تب اس چیز کی ملکیت حاصل کر کے آقا کو دے دے تو آزاد ہو جائے گا اور اگر وہ نہ دے سکے تو رقیق کر دیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ جو چیز مسمی ہے وہ مال ہے اور سپرد کرنے کی قدرت بھی ( ثبوت ملک کے احتمال پر ) موہوم ہے تو مال غیر سے ہونے والا بدل کتابت عورت کے اس مہر کے مشابہ ہو گیا جو غیر کے مال سے ہو۔ مثلا کسی نے عورت سے غیر کے غلام پر نکاح کیا تو تسمیہ صحیح ہے اب اگر غلام کے مالک نے اجازت نہ دی تو عورت شوہر سے غلام کی قیمت لے گی نہ کہ مہر مثل ولو كانت التسمية فاسدة لرجعت بمهر المثل قـولـه قلنا ان العين ... الخ - ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ معاوضات میں مال عین ( بدل کتابت ) معقود علیہ ہوتا ہے اور عقد صحیح
Similarly, if he made a kitabah for a specific thing belonging to someone else, then this kitabah is not valid.
He said: And likewise, if he makes a kitabah on a specific thing belonging to another, it is not valid because he is not able to deliver it. His intent is a thing that becomes specific by being specified, so that if he said, 'I make you a mukatab for these thousand dirhams' while they belong to another, it is valid because they do not become specific in compensations, so it attaches to dirhams as a debt in the dhimmah, so it is valid. And from Abu Hanifa, al-Hasan narrated that it is valid, so that if he comes to own them and delivers them, he is freed; if he is unable, he is returned to slavery because the named thing is wealth and the ability to deliver is presumed, so it resembles the dower. We say: The specific thing in compensation is the object of contract, and ability over the object of contract is a condition for validity when the contract is subject to rescission, as in sale, unlike the dower in marriage because ability over what is intended in marriage is not a condition, so what is subsidiary is even more so not a condition.
Translation: Similarly, if he makes a kitabah on a specific thing belonging to another, it is not valid because the slave is not able to deliver it. His intent is a thing that becomes specific by being specified, so that if he said, 'I make you a mukatab for these thousand dirhams' while they belong to another, it is valid because dirhams do not become specific in compensations, so the contract attaches to dirhams as a debt in the dhimmah, so it is valid.
[PAGE_132]
... And from Abu Hanifa, al-Hasan narrated that the contract is valid, so that if he comes to own it and delivers it to the master, he is freed, and if he is unable, he is returned to slavery because the named thing is wealth and the ability to deliver is presumed, so it resembles the dower. We say: In compensation, the specific thing is the object of contract, and ability over the object of contract is a condition for validity when the contract is subject to rescission, as in sale, unlike the dower in marriage because ability over what is intended in marriage is not a condition, so what is subsidiary is even more so not a condition.
Elaboration of his saying 'on a specific thing belonging to another': The word 'belonging to another' is a hal from the word 'thing', and 'thing' is indefinite, so the hal cannot be from an indefinite. But here due to the adjective 'specific', it becomes specified, so the owner of the hal becomes valid. The issue is that if the master makes the slave a mukatab in exchange for a specific thing of another person, e.g., a horse, cloth, or slave, then according to us and Imam Shafi'i and Ahmad, this is fasid because the slave is incapable of delivering another's thing. According to Imam Malik, it is valid: the slave buys it and gives it, and if the owner does not sell, he gives its price. His saying 'and his intent is a thing...' - By 'thing' in 'on a specific thing', Imam Muhammad intends a thing that becomes specific by being specified, like cloth, this horse, this slave, this house, etc. And if the thing is not specific, such as if he said 'I make you a mukatab for these thousand dirhams' while they belong to another, the kitabah contract is valid because dirhams and dinars become specific in trusts and usurpation, but they do not become specific in compensations. So the kitabah contract attaches to dirhams that become a debt in the slave's dhimmah. According to Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad, even in this case the kitabah is not valid because for them dirhams and dinars are also specific.
His saying 'al-Hasan narrated' - The elaboration of the issue: There are two cases in kitabah on another's thing: either the thing becomes specific by being specified (like a horse, slave, etc.) or it does not become specific (like currency, i.e., dirhams and dinars). The first has two subcases: either the owner permits it or not. If not permitted, then two subcases: either the mukatab comes to own it through some means and delivers it, or not. So there are four total pictures. If the thing does not become specific by being specified, then the kitabah contract is valid, as explained earlier. If it does become specific and the owner does not permit and the mukatab cannot come to own it, then in Zahir al-Riwayah it is not valid, and in Hasan's narration it is valid. Now, if the mukatab acquires ownership of the thing and gives it to the master, he is freed; if he cannot give it, he is returned to slavery because the named thing is wealth and ability to deliver is presumed (by possibility of ownership), so the consideration from another's thing resembles the dower of a woman that is from another's wealth. For example, someone marries a woman on a slave belonging to another: the specification is valid; if the slave's owner does not permit, the woman takes from the husband the price of the slave, not the mahr mithl. If the specification were fasid, she would revert to mahr mithl. His saying 'We say the specific thing...' - The reason of Zahir al-Riwayah is that in compensations, the specific thing (badal al-kitabah) is the object of contract, and the contract is valid...
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of kitabah when the consideration is a specific item owned by a third party. The Hidayah matn states it is invalid because the slave cannot deliver it. However, if the consideration is dirhams or dinars (currency), it is valid because such items are not specific in compensations; they become a debt in the dhimmah. Imam Abu Hanifa has a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad that even for a specific item belonging to another, the contract is valid; if the slave acquires and delivers it, he is freed; otherwise he is returned to slavery. This is based on analogy to mahr: in marriage, the dower may be a specific item owned by another, and the marriage is valid; similarly, kitabah resembles mahr because both are compensations. The Zahir al-Riwayah rebuts: in compensatory contracts (like kitabah), the specific item is the object of contract and ability to deliver is a condition because the contract is subject to rescission (like sale). In marriage, the dower is subsidiary; the primary object is the marriage itself, so ability on the dower is not a condition. Thus, the analogy fails. The commentary then distinguishes between specific items (which become identified by specification) and non-specific (currency). It also notes the positions of other schools: Shafi'i and Ahmad ibn Hanbal consider kitabah invalid even for currency because they hold that dirhams and dinars become specific in all transactions; Malik considers it valid and allows the slave to buy the item or pay its price. The Zahir al-Riwayah (relied-upon position) is that kitabah on a specific item of another is invalid. The narration of Hasan is a weak (nawadir) transmission.

Key Terms
معين (mu'ayyan): A specific, identified item (e.g., this horse, this slave).
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The established position transmitted in the six core books of Imam Muhammad, relied upon for fatwa.
صداق (sidaq): Dower given in marriage. Used here for analogy: the dower can be a specific item belonging to another without invalidating the marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, if a master makes a kitabah on a specific horse belonging to another person, what is the ruling?
A) The kitabah is valid, and the slave must acquire the horse and deliver it.
B) The kitabah is invalid because the slave cannot deliver the horse.
C) The kitabah is valid, and the slave can pay the horse's price instead.
D) The kitabah is valid only if the horse's owner gives permission.

Key Takeaway
Kitabah on a specific item of another is invalid in the relied-upon Hanafi view because ability to deliver is a condition in compensatory contracts, distinguishing kitabah from marriage where the dower is subsidiary.

Kitabah on Another's Property: Effect of Permission (Ijazah)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on permission (ijazah) in kitabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the validity of kitabah when the consideration is a third-party 'ayn and the owner subsequently grants permission, and explain the qiyas used by each imam.

Core Idea
Permission after kitabah: Abu Hanifa invalidates, Muhammad validates by sale analogy, Abu Yusuf validates with value substitution like marriage dower.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on a specific kitabah scenario. When the master contracts with a slave using a specific property owned by another as consideration, and that owner later gives permission, the three great imams of the Hanafi school differ in their rulings. The dispute hinges on whether permission can cure the initial defect and on the underlying purpose of kitabah. We will unpack each position and its qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The case: a master contracts kitabah with his slave, stipulating as badal a specific 'ayn (non-fungible property) that belongs to a third party. After the contract, that third-party owner grants permission (ijazah). Is the contract valid?
2
Present Imam Muhammad's view
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds it valid. He draws an analogy to a sale of a third-party property: if the owner permits later, the sale becomes valid. Since kitabah is more lenient (tarkhīs), it should be even more deserving of validation.
Qiyas on sale with subsequent permission
3
Present Imam Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa holds it invalid. He analogizes to the state before permission (the contract was initially invalid). Moreover, kitabah's purpose is to enable the slave to earn and pay gradually; when the badal is a specific 'ayn, there is no need for earning, so the contract fails its objective.
Qiyas on the initial state; maqsad of kitabah
4
Present Imam Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf holds it valid regardless of permission, but with a practical distinction: if the owner permits, the specific property is due; if not, its value (qimah) is due. He analogizes to marriage dower (mahr), where the specification is valid and value substitutes if delivery is impossible.
Qiyas on mahr; specification is valid because it is property
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, the contract is void; under Muhammad, it becomes valid upon permission; under Abu Yusuf, it is valid from the start, but the slave may have to pay value if permission is not given.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو اجاز صاحب العين ذلك فعن محمد انه يجوز لانه يجوز البيع عند الاجازة فالكتابة اولى وعن أبي حنيفة انه لا يجوز اعتبارا بحال عدم الاجازة على ما قال في كتاب والجامع بينهما انه لا يفيد ملك المكاتب وهو المقصود لانها تثبت للحاجة الى الاداء منها ولا حاجة فيما اذا كان البدل عينا معينا والمسألة فيه على ما بينا وعن ابى يوسف انه يجوز اجاز ذلك او لم يجز غير انه عند الاجازة يجب تسليم عينه وعند عدمها يجب تسليم قيمته كما فى النكاح والجامع بينهما صحة التسمية لكونه مالا ولو ملک المكاتب ذلك العين فعن ابي حنيفة رواه ابويوسف انه اذا اداه لا يعتق وعلى هذه الرواية لم ينعقد العقد الا اذا قال له اذا اديت الى فانتحر فحينئذ يعتق بحكم الشرط وهكذا عن ابى يوسف وعنه انه يعتق قال ذلك اولم يقل لان العقد ينعقد مع الفساد لكون المسمى مالا فيعتق باداء المشروط ولو كاتبه على عين في يد المكاتب فقيه روايتان وهى مسألة الكتابة على الاعيان وقد عرف ذلك في الاصل وقد ذكرنا وجه الروايتين في كفاية المنتهى
If the owner of that property gives permission, then from Muhammad it is reported that it is permissible, because a sale is permissible with permission, so kitabah is more appropriate. From Abu Hanifa it is reported that it is not permissible, by analogy with the state of no permission, as stated in the book. The common factor between them is that it does not confer ownership of earnings to the mukatab, which is the purpose because kitabah is established for the need of payment from earnings, and there is no need when the consideration is a specific property. The issue is as we have explained. From Abu Yusuf it is reported that it is permissible regardless of permission, except that with permission the specific property must be delivered, and without permission its value must be delivered, as in marriage. The common factor is the validity of the specification because it is property. If the mukatab acquires ownership of that property, from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf narrated that if he pays it, he is not set free. According to this narration, the contract is not concluded unless the master said: 'When you pay me, you are free,' then he is set free by virtue of the condition. Similarly from Abu Yusuf, and from him also that he is set free whether he said it or not, because the contract is concluded with irregularity due to the property being property, so he is set free upon payment of what was stipulated. If he made a kitabah on property in the possession of the mukatab, there are two narrations, and this is the issue of kitabah on properties, known in the original work, and we have mentioned the basis of the two narrations in Kifayat al-Muntaha.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a specific case of kitabah (contract of manumission) where the consideration (badal) is a specific 'ayn (non-fungible property) that belongs to someone other than the master. The text presents three positions from the eponymous imams and then addresses a subsidiary issue when the slave later acquires ownership of that property.

The discussion begins with the scenario: the master makes a kitabah contract with the slave, stipulating a specific property owned by a third party as the consideration. If the third-party owner subsequently grants permission (ijazah) after the contract, is the contract valid?
- Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds it valid by analogy to a sale: if a person buys something from another without the owner's permission, the sale becomes valid upon subsequent permission. Since kitabah is based on leniency, it is more deserving of validity.
- Imam Abu Hanifa holds it invalid, drawing analogy to the state before permission (since the contract was initially invalid). The underlying rationale is that kitabah is meant to enable the slave to earn and pay gradually; when the consideration is a specific property, there is no need for the slave to earn, thus the purpose is lost.
- Abu Yusuf holds it valid regardless of permission, but with a practical distinction: if the owner permits, the specific property must be delivered; if not, the slave must deliver its value (qimah), similar to marriage dower (mahr), where the specification is valid because it is property, and if the specified item is not delivered, its value is due.

Next, consider the case where the slave himself acquires ownership of that specific property (e.g., through gift or purchase) after the contract. There are two narrations from Abu Yusuf:
- In one narration (also from Abu Hanifa): if the slave pays that property, he is not set free. The contract is not concluded unless the master specifically said: 'When you pay me, you are free.' In that case, payment would free him by virtue of the condition (shart), not the contract itself.
- In another narration: the slave is freed whether the master said that or not, because the contract is concluded despite its irregularity (fasad) due to the consideration being valuable property, so paying the stipulated item triggers freedom.

The text also mentions a separate issue: if the kitabah is on a property already in the slave's possession, there are two narrations (riwayatan) known in the original works. The commentator notes that he has explained the basis of these narrations in his own work Kifayat al-Muntaha.

This passage illustrates the Hanafi method of qiyas and istihsan in resolving contractual disputes, always considering the underlying purpose (maqsud) of kitabah: enabling the slave to earn for self-purchase.

Key Terms
كتابة (kitābah): A contract by which a slave is given freedom in exchange for payment of a specified consideration over time.
بدل (badal): The consideration or price payable by the mukatab for his freedom.
إجازة (ijāzah): Permission granted by the owner of the property after the contract, which may validate or affect the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the common factor (jami') between the views of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad?
A) Both consider the contract valid upon permission.
B) Both consider the contract invalid because the slave cannot earn.
C) Both focus on the idea that the contract does not confer ownership of earnings, which is the purpose.
D) Both rely on qiyas on sale.

Key Takeaway
The validity of kitabah on a third-party 'ayn after permission depends on the imam's qiyas: Abu Hanifa focuses on purpose, Muhammad on permission, Abu Yusuf on specification validity.

Kitabah on Another's Property: When the Slave Later Acquires the Specific Item
Intra-Hanafi dispute on effect of slave's later acquisition of the specified 'ayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two narrations from Abu Yusuf regarding the effect of the slave acquiring the specified third-party property after the kitabah contract, and determine whether the slave is freed upon payment.

Core Idea
If the slave later owns the property: one narration denies freedom without conditional statement; another grants freedom due to the contract's irregular validity.

This lesson explores a subsidiary issue arising from the previous dispute: what happens if the mukatab (slave) himself acquires ownership of the specified 'ayn after the kitabah contract? According to Abu Yusuf, there are two narrations. This scenario tests the limits of the contract's validity when the defect of third-party ownership is cured by the slave's subsequent ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sub-issue
After a kitabah contract on a third-party 'ayn, the slave later acquires that property (e.g., through gift or inheritance). He then offers it as payment. Does the slave become free?
2
Present the first narration from Abu Yusuf
In one narration (also attributed to Abu Hanifa via Abu Yusuf), if the slave pays the property, he is not set free. The contract is not considered concluded unless the master explicitly said: 'When you pay me, you are free.' If that condition was stated, he is freed by virtue of the condition, not the contract.
The contract itself is invalid; only a conditional promise activates freedom.
3
Present the second narration from Abu Yusuf
In another narration, the slave is freed whether the master said that or not. Here, the contract is considered concluded despite its irregularity (fasid). Since the consideration is valuable property, paying it triggers freedom even if the contract was defective.
The contract, though fasid, is still a valid basis for freedom upon payment.
4
Analyse the difference
The key difference lies in the effect of a fasid contract. In the first narration, fasid does not produce the effect of manumission; a conditional stipulation is required. In the second, the fasid contract is sufficient to effect freedom once the property is paid.
This reflects a broader Hanafi principle on irregular contracts: some fasid contracts may still produce certain effects.
5
Note the reference to another issue
The passage ends with a mention of another case: kitabah on property already in the slave's possession, with two narrations. The commentator says he explained the basis in Kifayat al-Muntaha, but it is not elaborated here.
This is a separate sub-issue not detailed in this lesson.

فلو اجاز صاحب العين ذلك فعن محمد انه يجوز لانه يجوز البيع عند الاجازة فالكتابة اولى وعن أبي حنيفة انه لا يجوز اعتبارا بحال عدم الاجازة على ما قال في كتاب والجامع بينهما انه لا يفيد ملك المكاتب وهو المقصود لانها تثبت للحاجة الى الاداء منها ولا حاجة فيما اذا كان البدل عينا معينا والمسألة فيه على ما بينا وعن ابى يوسف انه يجوز اجاز ذلك او لم يجز غير انه عند الاجازة يجب تسليم عينه وعند عدمها يجب تسليم قيمته كما فى النكاح والجامع بينهما صحة التسمية لكونه مالا ولو ملک المكاتب ذلك العين فعن ابي حنيفة رواه ابويوسف انه اذا اداه لا يعتق وعلى هذه الرواية لم ينعقد العقد الا اذا قال له اذا اديت الى فانتحر فحينئذ يعتق بحكم الشرط وهكذا عن ابى يوسف وعنه انه يعتق قال ذلك اولم يقل لان العقد ينعقد مع الفساد لكون المسمى مالا فيعتق باداء المشروط ولو كاتبه على عين في يد المكاتب فقيه روايتان وهى مسألة الكتابة على الاعيان وقد عرف ذلك في الاصل وقد ذكرنا وجه الروايتين في كفاية المنتهى
If the owner of that property gives permission, then from Muhammad it is reported that it is permissible, because a sale is permissible with permission, so kitabah is more appropriate. From Abu Hanifa it is reported that it is not permissible, by analogy with the state of no permission, as stated in the book. The common factor between them is that it does not confer ownership of earnings to the mukatab, which is the purpose because kitabah is established for the need of payment from earnings, and there is no need when the consideration is a specific property. The issue is as we have explained. From Abu Yusuf it is reported that it is permissible regardless of permission, except that with permission the specific property must be delivered, and without permission its value must be delivered, as in marriage. The common factor is the validity of the specification because it is property. If the mukatab acquires ownership of that property, from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf narrated that if he pays it, he is not set free. According to this narration, the contract is not concluded unless the master said: 'When you pay me, you are free,' then he is set free by virtue of the condition. Similarly from Abu Yusuf, and from him also that he is set free whether he said it or not, because the contract is concluded with irregularity due to the property being property, so he is set free upon payment of what was stipulated. If he made a kitabah on property in the possession of the mukatab, there are two narrations, and this is the issue of kitabah on properties, known in the original work, and we have mentioned the basis of the two narrations in Kifayat al-Muntaha.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a specific case of kitabah (contract of manumission) where the consideration (badal) is a specific 'ayn (non-fungible property) that belongs to someone other than the master. The text presents three positions from the eponymous imams and then addresses a subsidiary issue when the slave later acquires ownership of that property.

The discussion begins with the scenario: the master makes a kitabah contract with the slave, stipulating a specific property owned by a third party as the consideration. If the third-party owner subsequently grants permission (ijazah) after the contract, is the contract valid?
- Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds it valid by analogy to a sale: if a person buys something from another without the owner's permission, the sale becomes valid upon subsequent permission. Since kitabah is based on leniency, it is more deserving of validity.
- Imam Abu Hanifa holds it invalid, drawing analogy to the state before permission (since the contract was initially invalid). The underlying rationale is that kitabah is meant to enable the slave to earn and pay gradually; when the consideration is a specific property, there is no need for the slave to earn, thus the purpose is lost.
- Abu Yusuf holds it valid regardless of permission, but with a practical distinction: if the owner permits, the specific property must be delivered; if not, the slave must deliver its value (qimah), similar to marriage dower (mahr), where the specification is valid because it is property, and if the specified item is not delivered, its value is due.

Next, consider the case where the slave himself acquires ownership of that specific property (e.g., through gift or purchase) after the contract. There are two narrations from Abu Yusuf:
- In one narration (also from Abu Hanifa): if the slave pays that property, he is not set free. The contract is not concluded unless the master specifically said: 'When you pay me, you are free.' In that case, payment would free him by virtue of the condition (shart), not the contract itself.
- In another narration: the slave is freed whether the master said that or not, because the contract is concluded despite its irregularity (fasad) due to the consideration being valuable property, so paying the stipulated item triggers freedom.

The text also mentions a separate issue: if the kitabah is on a property already in the slave's possession, there are two narrations (riwayatan) known in the original works. The commentator notes that he has explained the basis of these narrations in his own work Kifayat al-Muntaha.

This passage illustrates the Hanafi method of qiyas and istihsan in resolving contractual disputes, always considering the underlying purpose (maqsud) of kitabah: enabling the slave to earn for self-purchase.

Key Terms
عقد فاسد (ʿaqd fāsid): An irregular contract that is not void (batil) but lacks a condition; it may produce some effects.
شرط (shart): A condition that, if attached to a contract, may affect its validity or trigger certain effects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first narration from Abu Yusuf regarding the slave's later acquisition of the specified property, what is required for the slave to be freed?
A) The slave must simply pay the property.
B) The master must have given permission for the kitabah beforehand.
C) The master must have said 'When you pay me, you are free' at the time of contract.
D) The slave must also pay an additional amount.

Key Takeaway
The fate of the slave upon acquiring the specified property depends on whether the contract is considered concluded: one narration requires a condition, the other does not.
