12 min
Kitabah on a Specific Item Owned by a Third Party: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kitabah with third-party badal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the validity of kitabah when the badal is a specific item owned by a third party, explain the analogy each imam uses, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving permission and later acquisition.

Core Idea
Analogy drives the intra-Hanafi split: sale (leniency) vs. non-permission (strictness) vs. marriage (flexibility).

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute where the consideration for a kitabah contract is a specific item belonging to someone else. The three eponymous imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad—each reach a different conclusion on whether the owner's permission (or lack thereof) validates the contract, and on the effect of the mukatab later acquiring the item. Their differences stem from different analogical reasoning (qiyas), each prioritizing a different analogy: sale, the default invalidity, or marriage. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how legal reasoning (istidlal) produces divergent rulings within the same school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize that the dispute is about the validity of a kitabah contract when the badal (consideration) is a specific item that at the time of contract is owned by a third party. The contract may be invalid (fasid) in itself, but the discussion focuses on whether the owner's permission or later acquisition by the mukatab can cure it.
The contract is initially defective because the mu'awwad (counter-value) is not owned by the contracting parties.
2
Analyze Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad holds that if the owner grants permission, the contract becomes valid. His proof is qiyas on sale: when someone buys a specific item from a third party with the owner's permission, the sale is valid. Since kitabah is more lenient than sale (it encourages manumission), it should be valid by primary analogy (awlā).
Key phrase: 'Kitabah is based on leniency (musāhala), sale on strictness (mudyāqah).'
3
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa maintains that the contract is invalid even with permission. He analogizes to the case where permission is absent—already ruled invalid—and argues that permission does not change the nature because the mukatab would be earning from the contract, but since the badal is a specific item, earnings are unnecessary. This is found in al-Jami' al-Saghir.
The 'common cause' (al-illa al-mushtaraka) is that earnings are superfluous when the substitute is a specific item.
4
Analyze Imam Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf considers the contract valid regardless of permission, drawing an analogy with marriage where the dower may be a specific third-party item. If the owner permits, the exact item is given; if not, its value is given. Thus, the contract is not void ab initio but becomes valid by paying the value if the owner refuses.
This view is the most flexible; it treats kitabah like nikah where the object of consideration is not required to be owned at contract.
5
Examine the later acquisition scenario
The passage then discusses what happens if the mukatab later becomes owner of that specific item. According to Sahib al-Riwayah (Zahir al-Riwayah, from Abu Hanifa via Abu Yusuf), paying that item does not free him unless the master explicitly conditioned freedom on payment (e.g., 'When you pay me, you are free'). Another transmission from Abu Yusuf (of the Companions of the Imla') holds that he is freed without such a condition, because the contract is fasid and payment of property effects freedom, akin to kitabah on wine.
Note the difference: condition-dependent vs. unconditional freedom.

قوله وعنه انه يعتق الخ - اور امام ابو یوسف سے دوسری روایت جو اصحاب املاء کی ہے یہ ہے کہ مکاتب آزاد ہو جائے گا خواہ آقا نے اذا ادیت الی فانت حر کہا ہو یا نہ کہا ہو۔ اس لئے کہ یہ عقد تو فاسد منعقد ہوگا کیونکہ جو چیز سمی ہے وہ مال ہے تو مال مشروط ادا کرنے پر آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ جیسے کتابت اگر شراب پر ہو اوڑہ شرب ادا کر دے تو آزاد ہو جاتا ہے۔
Then if that other person who owns that specific property (the kitabah substitute) gives permission, will the kitabah contract become valid or not? Regarding this, the transmissions differ. From Imam Muhammad comes the transmission that the contract will become valid because when buying something in exchange for the property of another, if the owner grants permission, the sale becomes valid, even though sale is based on strictness; so kitabah is even more valid since it is based on leniency. And from Imam Abu Hanifa via Ibn Sama'ah from Abu Yusuf: he narrated that the contract will not become valid (even if the owner gives permission), by analogy with the case of no permission, i.e., just as when there is no permission from the owner it is not valid, as stated in al-Jami' al-Saghir. Similarly, if he wrote him a kitabah on a specific thing belonging to another, it is not valid. So even with permission it will not be valid. The comprehensive reason and common cause is that in such a case, by obtaining this permission, he would acquire earnings from the kitabah contract, but earnings become owned because they are needed for paying the substitute, and when the substitute is a specific property, that need ceases. And from Imam Abu Yusuf: the contract is valid whether the owner of that thing grants permission or not. The only point is that if he grants permission, delivering that very thing becomes necessary; if he does not grant permission, delivering its value is not necessary, like in marriage. For the reason that the thing mentioned as dower is valid because it is also property. So just as in marriage when a specific dower is valid even though it belongs to another, and if that other person gives permission, the specific thing is given; otherwise its value is given, so here. And if the owner of that thing does not give permission, but the mukatab becomes the owner of that specific property through some means, then from Abu Hanifa via Abu Yusuf: if the mukatab pays that specific property, he will not be freed. This is the Zahir al-Riwayah. According to this transmission, the contract only concludes if the master said: 'When you pay me, you are free.' Then upon payment of the property, the mukatab becomes free by virtue of the condition. A similar saying is also attributed to Abu Yusuf from Hasan ibn Abi Malik, and the saying of al-Zafar is similar. And from Abu Yusuf another transmission from the Companions of the Imla': the mukatab will be freed whether the master said 'When you pay me, you are free' or not, because this contract is concluded as fasid, so when the specified thing is property, on paying that property he becomes free, just as if kitabah were on wine and he pays wine, he becomes free.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a kitabah contract when the consideration (badal) is a specific item owned by a third party. Three positions are recorded: (1) Imam Muhammad holds the contract becomes valid upon the owner's permission, by analogy with sale (where permission validates) and by preferring leniency in kitabah. (2) Imam Abu Hanifa holds it is invalid even with permission, analogizing to the case without permission, and also because earnings from the contract are unnecessary since the substitute is a specific item. (3) Imam Abu Yusuf holds it is valid regardless of permission, comparing it to marriage where a specific dower belonging to another is valid; if the owner permits, the specific item is given; if not, its value. The passage then discusses a scenario where the mukatab later acquires ownership of that specific item. According to the Zahir al-Riwayah (from Abu Hanifa via Abu Yusuf), paying that item does not free him unless the master conditioned freedom upon payment (e.g., 'When you pay me, you are free'), in which case the condition triggers freedom. Another transmission from Abu Yusuf (from the Companions of the Imla') says he is freed regardless of such a condition, because the contract is fasid and payment of property effects freedom, analogous to kitabah on wine.

Key Terms
عقد کتابت (aqd al-kitabah): Contract of manumission whereby a slave agrees to pay his master a sum in installments in exchange for freedom upon full payment.
بدل کتابت (badal al-kitabah): The consideration or payment specified in the kitabah contract for freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah, if a mukatab later acquires ownership of the specific item that was the badal (but originally belonged to a third party) and pays it to the master, when does he become free?
A) He becomes free immediately upon payment.
B) He becomes free only if the master had said 'When you pay me, you are free'.
C) He does not become free under any circumstances.
D) He becomes free if the original owner also grants permission.

Key Takeaway
The validity of kitabah on a third-party item hinges on which imam's analogy is followed; the Zahir al-Riwayah endorses Abu Hanifa's strict view requiring explicit condition for freedom upon later acquisition.

Two Transmissions on Kitabah with a Specific Item in the Mukatab's Possession
Ruling on kitabah when the badal is a specific item already in the mukatab's possession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conflicting Hanafi transmissions regarding kitabah on a specific item in the mukatab's possession and explain the nature of this intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Two transmissions from al-Mabsut disagree on kitabah with a specific item—one validates, one invalidates.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a kitabah contract is valid when the consideration is a specific item already owned by the mukatab. The source presents two contradictory transmissions from the same foundational work, al-Mabsut, and notes that the reason for the conflict is discussed elsewhere. Understanding this transmission conflict is crucial for recognizing that not all Hanafi rulings are settled—some remain as unresolved differences in transmission (ikhtilaf al-riwayah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is kitabah (a contract of manumission by payment) where the consideration (badal) is a specific item (ayn) already in the mukatab's possession (e.g., his earnings). The dispute is whether such a contract is valid.
The mukatab is a slave who has entered a kitabah agreement.
2
Locate the two transmissions
Two transmissions from al-Mabsut: (1) from Kitab al-Shurb – the contract is valid; (2) from Kitab al-Mukatab – the contract is not valid.
Both are from the same authoritative source (zahir riwayah).
3
Understand 'Kitabah ala al-A'yan'
This is the technical term for kitabah where the badal is a specific, identified item rather than a fungible (dayn). The passage states this is the well-known issue.
The distinction between 'ayn and dayn is important in Hanafi muamalat.
4
Recognise the authority level
Both transmissions come from al-Mabsut, a core text of Zahir al-Riwayah, so both carry authoritative weight. This is not a case of weak vs. strong transmission.
The passage does not indicate which transmission is mufta bihi.
5
Note the unresolved nature
The passage refers to Kifayat al-Muntaha for the reason behind the two transmissions but does not resolve the conflict here. This indicates an ongoing ikhtilaf al-riwayah.
In practice, a mufti would need to consult later tarjih sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ولو كاتبه على عين ... الخ - اگر آقا نے غلام کو ایسے معین مال پر مکاتب کیا جو ا سکے قبضہ میں ہے یعنی وہ اس کی کمائی ہے (بـان كـان مـاذو نافى التجارة ) تو اس کی بات دو روایتیں ہیں۔ اصل یعنی مبسوط کی کتاب الشرب کی روایت یہ ہے کہ عقد جائز ہے اور کتاب المکاتب کی روایت یہ ہے کہ جائز نہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مال معین پر مکاتب کرنا ہی کتابت علی الاعیان کا مسئلہ ہے جو اصل یعنی مبسوط میں معروف ہے اور دونوں روایتوں کی وجہ 9 ہم نے کفایتہ المنتہی میں ذکر کی ہے۔
His saying: 'And if he made a kitabah with him on a specific property...' - if the master made a kitabah with the slave on a specific property that is in his possession, i.e., it is his earnings (if he is permitted to trade), then there are two transmissions regarding it. In al-Mabsut, in the Book of Wine (Kitab al-Shurb), the transmission is that the contract is valid, and in the Book of Kitabah (Kitab al-Mukatab) the transmission is that it is not valid. The author of al-Hidayah says: 'Making a kitabah on specific property is the issue of kitabah 'ala al-a'yan (kitabah on specific items), which is well-known in al-Mabsut, and we have mentioned the reason for the two transmissions in Kifayat al-Muntaha.'
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific intra-Hanafi dispute regarding kitabah when the consideration (badal) is a specific item that is already in the mukatab's possession, such as earnings from trade. Two contradictory transmissions are recorded: one from Kitab al-Shurb in al-Mabsut says the contract is valid; the other from Kitab al-Mukatab says it is invalid. The commentator notes that this is the well-known issue of kitabah 'ala al-a'yan. The author of al-Hidayah (presumably al-Marghinani) refers to his work Kifayat al-Muntaha for the reason behind the two transmissions. The passage does not provide a resolution or preference between them, leaving the matter as a difference in transmission.

Key Terms
کتابت علی الاعیان (kitabah 'ala al-a'yan): Kitabah where the consideration is a specific, identified item (e.g., a particular slave, a specific garment) rather than a fungible like currency.

Kitabah with Condition to Return a Non-Specified Slave: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on kitabah where the master conditionally promises to give a non-specified slave to the mukatab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding kitabah with a condition to return a non-specified slave and evaluate the validity of the contract based on the reasoning of each imam.

Core Idea
A condition to return a non-specified slave in kitabah is invalid per Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf validates it by deducting the slave's value.

This passage presents an internal disagreement among the founding Hanafi jurists on the validity of a kitabah contract that includes a condition for the master to return a non-specified slave to the mukatab. Understanding this dispute sharpens our ability to analyze the legal reasoning behind each position and to appreciate how the school manages ikhtilaf within its own tradition.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify the legal scenario: a master (mawla) makes a kitabah contract with his slave for 100 dinars on the condition that the master will give a non-specified slave to the mukatab. Then note that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule the contract invalid (fasid), while Abu Yusuf rules it valid.
The dispute is exclusively within the Hanafi school; later jurists typically side with the majority.
2
Analyze the evidence of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They argue that the slave cannot be excepted from the dinars because only the slave's value can be excepted, and value is not a valid substitute in kitabah. Thus, the condition introduces uncertainty (gharar) that invalidates the contract.
Their reasoning relies on the principle that badal (consideration) must be known and deliverable as property.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's reasoning
Abu Yusuf treats the condition as a valid partial return of consideration. He divides the 100 dinars proportionally between the value of the mukatab and the value of an average slave; the slave's portion is deducted, and the mukatab pays the remainder. He bases this on the permissibility of using an absolute (unspecified) slave as a substitute in kitabah, defaulting to the average.
Abu Yusuf's method seeks to salvage the contract by making the condition quantifiable and thus removing uncertainty.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Abu Yusuf's view, the contract stands and the mukatab's debt is reduced by the value of an average slave; under the view of the two imams, the entire contract is invalid from the outset.
This difference affects whether the mukatab can gain freedom through the contract or must start anew.
5
Extract the underlying principle regarding badal
All three imams agree that the badal (consideration) in kitabah must be known and deliverable as property. The disagreement is whether the condition of returning a non-specified slave can be resolved by valuation or whether it introduces fatal uncertainty.
This case illustrates how a single principle can yield different rulings when applied to a specific condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان كاتبه على مائة دينار على ان يرد المولى اليه عبدا بغير عينه فالكتابة فاسدة عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابويوسف هي جائزة ويقسم المائة الدينار على قيمة المكاتب وعلى قيمة عبد وسط فتبطل منها حصة العبد فيكون مكاتبا بما بقى لان العبد المطلق يصلح بدل الكتابة وينصرف الى الوسط فكذا يصلح مستثنى منه وهو الاصل في ابدال العقود ولهما انه لا يستثنى العبد من الدنانير وإنما يستثنى قيمته والقيمة لا تصلح بدلا فکذلک مستثنی
ترجمہ اگر مکاتب کیا اس کو سو اشرفیوں پر بائیں شرط کہ آقا اس کو ایک غیر معین غلام واپس دے گا تو کتابت فاسد ہے۔ طرفین کے نزدیک۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ یہ کتابت جائز ہے اور سواشرفیوں کو کتابت کی قیمت پر اور اوسط درجہ کے غلام کی قیمت پر تقسیم کے جائے گا۔ پس سواشرفیوں میں سے غلام کا حصہ مستثنی ہو کر وہ باقی کے عوض مکاتب ہو گا۔ کیونکہ مطلق غلام بدل کتابت ہونے کے لائق ہوتا ہے اور اوسط درجہ کے غلام کی طرف ہوتا ہے تو ایسے ہی یہ غلام مشقتی بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ اور عقود کے معاوضات میں یہی اصل ہے طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اشرفیوں سے غلام کا استثناء نہیں ہوسکتا بلکہ اس قیمت کا استثناء ہو سکتا ہے اور قیمت عوض ہونے کے لائق نہیں تو وہ مستی بھی نہیں ہو سکتی۔
تشریح قوله وان كاتبه ... الخ - اگر آقا نے اپنے غلام کو سود دینار کے عوض اس شرط پر مکاتب کیا کہ آقا اس کو ایک غیر معین غلام - واپس کرے گا تو طرفین کے نزدیک نیہ بھی فاسد ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ عبد مطلق بدل کتابت ہونے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے تو یہاں درمیانی قسم کے غلام کی قیمت پر تقسیم کر دیں گے۔ پس اوسط درجہ کے غلام کی قیمت کا حصہ ساقط ہو جائیگا۔ اور باقی کے عوض وہ مکاتب ہو جائے گا۔ فرض کر دو کہ کاتب غلام کی قیمت چھ سو اور اوسط درجہ کے غلام کی قیمت چارسو ہے تو سوکو ان دونوں پر پھیلانے سے اوسط غلام کے مقابلہ میں چالیس پڑے تو یہ نکال کر باقی ساٹھ کے عوض غلام مکاتب ہوا۔
He said: 'And if he made a kitabah with him for one hundred dinars on condition that the master would return to him a non-specific slave, then the kitabah is fasid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: It is valid. The hundred dinars are to be divided between the value of the mukatab and the value of an average slave; then the slave's portion is deducted, and he becomes a mukatab for the remainder. Because an absolute slave is suitable as a substitute in kitabah, and it refers to the average; so likewise he is suitable as an exception, and this is the principle in exchanges of contracts. Their evidence (for invalidity) is that the slave cannot be excepted from the dinars; only his value can be excepted, and value is not suitable as a substitute, so likewise what is excepted.' Translation: If he made a mukatab for one hundred gold coins on the condition that the master would return to him a non-specific slave, then the kitabah is invalid according to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Imam Abu Yusuf said that this kitabah is valid, and the hundred gold coins will be divided over the value of the mukatab and the value of an average slave. So the share of the slave from the hundred is excluded, and he becomes a mukatab for the remainder. Because an absolute slave is capable of being a substitute in kitabah, and it refers to the average; so similarly this slave can be an exception. And this is the principle in contracts of exchange. The argument of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the slave cannot be excepted from the dinars; only its value can be excepted, and value is not suitable as a substitute, so the excluded (value) is also not suitable. Commentary: If the master made his slave a mukatab for one hundred dinars on condition that the master would return to him a non-specific slave, then according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) this is also invalid. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, it is valid. Because an absolute slave is capable of being a substitute in kitabah, so here it will be divided over the price of an average slave. So the share of the price of the average slave is dropped, and for the remainder he becomes a mukatab. For example, if the value of the slave (mukatab) is six hundred and the value of an average slave is four hundred, then spreading the hundred over both gives forty for the average slave; deducting that, the slave becomes a mukatab for the remaining sixty.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a kitabah contract where the master stipulates that he will return a non-specified slave to the mukatab as part of the arrangement. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad rule the contract invalid (fasid) because the condition introduces an exception of a slave from the dinars, but the slave is a specific property, and only its value can be excepted, yet value cannot serve as a substitute in kitabah. Imam Abu Yusuf, however, considers it valid by applying a division: the hundred dinars are allocated proportionally between the value of the mukatab and the value of an average slave. The share corresponding to the slave is deducted, and the mukatab remains bound to pay the remainder. This is based on the principle that an absolute slave is a valid substitute in kitabah and defaults to an average quality. The example given clarifies: if the mukatab's value is 600 and an average slave's value is 400, then 100 dinars are divided in the ratio 600:400 (3:2), so 40 dinars correspond to the slave's share, which is dropped, and the mukatab pays the remaining 60 dinars for freedom.

Key Terms
بدل کتابت (badal al-kitabah): The consideration for freedom; must be property. In this case, 100 dinars with a condition to return a slave.
استثناء (istithna'): Exception; here, the slave is meant to be excepted from the dinars, but the authors argue that only value can be excepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The contract is valid and the slave's value is deducted.
B) The contract is invalid (fasid).
C) The contract is valid only if the slave is specified.
D) The contract is suspended until the slave is identified.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school divides on whether a condition to return a non-specified slave in kitabah can be quantified; the majority view holds it invalid for uncertainty.

Kitaba for Wine with a Christian Master: Validity and Disputes
Explains the ruling when a Christian writes kitaba for wine and a party converts to Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the validity of kitaba with wine as a substitute when a party converts to Islam, state the conditions for validity, and compare the Hanafi view with the Shafi'i/Maliki position.

Core Idea
Kitaba for wine is valid for non-Muslims; conversion to Islam triggers a price substitution, not contract nullification.

In the Hanafi school, the legal status of wine differs between Muslims and non-Muslims: for Muslims, wine is not property; for non-Muslims, it is. This distinction shapes the ruling on kitaba contracts where wine is the substitute. When a Christian master enters a kitaba with his slave for wine, the contract is valid if certain conditions are met. But what happens if either party converts to Islam before payment? This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the Hanafi ruling and addresses the objections of other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Position
State the Hanafi ruling on kitaba for wine with a Christian master, including the conditions (wine known, slave disbeliever) and the effect of conversion to Islam (price substitutes).
The passage begins by stating the permissibility and conditions.
2
Understand the Opposing View
Identify the Shafi'i, Maliki, and (in one narration) Ahmad and Muhammad's position: kitaba becomes fasid upon conversion because Muslims cannot own or transfer wine.
The opposing school bases its argument on the general prohibition of wine.
3
Analyse the Hanafi Response
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal: the distinction between specified and unspecified wine. For unspecified wine, ownership transfers by delivery, not contract; thus delivering wine to a Muslim is prohibited, but the master still gets its price. For specified wine, ownership is established by contract, and delivery is merely transferring possession, which is not prohibited.
This is the key technical distinction (qiyas khafi).
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Hanafi says kitaba remains valid and slave must pay price; opposing says kitaba becomes fasid, requiring a new contract.
This affects whether the slave can still become free under the original contract.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Difference
Recognise the minority view (Sharh Tahawi) that the slave does not become free even if he pays the wine, versus the majority view (Qadi Zahir al-Din et al.) that he does.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قـولـه ومعناه اذا كان .... الخ - یہ دونوں شرطیں عبارت جامع صغیر میں مصرح موجود ہیں مگر صاحب ہدایہ نے یہاں جامع کی عبارت بعینہ ذکر نہیں کی۔ اس لئے دونوں شرطوں پر متنبہ کرنے کی ضرورت پیش آئی۔
قوله لانها مال .. الخ - مذکورہ کتابت کے جواز کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ شراب ان لوگوں کے حق میں ایسا مال ہے جیسے ہمارے حق میں سرکہ مال ہے۔ پھر آقا اور مکاتب میں سے جو کوئی مسلمان ہو جائے ۔ تو ہر حال میں آقا کو شراب کی قیمت ملے گی۔ (امام شافعی و مالک ، ایک روایت میں امام احمد ومحمد کے نزدیک کتابت فاسد ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ مسلمان کو شراب کی تملیک ( مالک بنانے اور مالک ہونے ) ہے منع کیا گیا ہے اور شراب سپرد کرنے میں یہی لازم آتا ہے۔ یعنی اگر مکاتب مسلمان ہوا تو تملیک اور آقا مسلمان ہوا تو تملک لازم آتا ہے کیونکہ مسئلہ میں مفروض یہی ہے کہ شراب غیر معین ہے تو اس میں ملک نفس عقد سے ثابت نہ ہوگی بلکہ سپرد کرنے سے ثابت ہوگی (برخلاف اس کے جب شراب معین ہو۔ کہ اس میں نفس عقد سے ملک ثابت ہو جائے گی اور اب شرب سپرد کرنا ایک قبضہ سے دوسرے قبضہ کی طرف منتقل کرنا ہوگا۔ اور مسلمان کے لئے نقل ید ممنوع نہیں ہے ) بہر کیف جب مسلمان کے لئے تسلیم خمرممنوع ہوا تو وہ بدل کتابت سپرد کرنے سے عاجز ہو گیا۔ لہذا اس کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔
He will become incapable. Therefore, its price becomes wajib upon him. And this is contrary to the case when the Zoroastrians [؟] bought and sold wine, then one of them became Muslim: according to some, the sale becomes fasid. Because in kitaba, price is possible in general. Thus, if a slave is made mukatib upon a service-maid and the mukatib brings its price, the master will be forced to accept it. So it is permissible that the contract remains upon the price. As for sale, it is not concluded at that time. So there is a difference between the two. And when the master takes possession of the wine, the slave becomes free. Because in kitaba, there is the meaning of exchange. So when one counter-value reaches the master, the other counter-value becomes secured for the slave, and this happens by him becoming free. Contrary to when the slave becomes Muslim, because the kitaba will not be valid, since a Muslim is not entitled to undertake wine. But if he pays the wine, he becomes free. Explanation of his saying 'and if a Christian writes kitaba...' - If a Christian writes kitaba with his slave for wine, it is permissible provided the quantity of wine is known, because ignorance of the substitute prevents permissibility. Also, the slave should be a disbeliever. If he is Muslim, the kitaba with the mentioned substitute includes the suspension of the contract upon payment, so it becomes like when a Muslim writes kitaba with his Muslim slave for wine and the mukatib pays the wine, then he becomes free. Qadi Zahir al-Din, Razi, Najm al-Din Afzali, and Nishapuri and other scholars have mentioned this. However, in Sharh Tahawi and Tamar Nash it is stated that he will not become free. His statement 'and its meaning when...' - These two conditions are explicitly present in the text of Jami' al-Saghir, but the author of Hidayah did not mention the exact wording of Jami' here. Therefore, it was necessary to alert to both conditions. His statement 'because it is property...' - The reason for the permissibility of the mentioned kitaba is that wine is property for those people just as vinegar is property for us. Then, if either the master or the mukatib becomes Muslim, in any case the master will receive the price of the wine. (Imam Shafi'i and Malik, and in one narration Imam Ahmad and Muhammad, hold that the kitaba becomes fasid because a Muslim is prohibited from being made the owner of wine (tamlik) and from owning it (tamalluk), and this necessarily follows in delivering wine. That is, if the mukatib becomes Muslim, tamlik is necessary, and if the master becomes Muslim, tamalluk is necessary. Because it is assumed in the issue that the wine is unspecified, so ownership is not established by the contract itself but by delivery. (Contrary to when the wine is specified, where ownership is established by the contract itself, and then delivering the wine is merely transferring from one possession to another, and for a Muslim transfer of possession is not prohibited.) In any case, since for a Muslim delivering wine is prohibited, he becomes incapable of delivering the substitute in kitaba. Therefore, its price becomes wajib.)
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute concerning kitaba (contract of manumission) where the substitute is wine and the master is a Christian. The Hanafi school rules that such a kitaba is valid provided the wine is known in quantity and the slave is a disbeliever. If the slave later becomes Muslim, the kitaba becomes invalid because a Muslim cannot contract for wine, but if he pays the wine, he becomes free. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the majority of scholars (Qadi Zahir al-Din, Razi, etc.) hold that he becomes free, but in Sharh Tahawi and Tamar Nash it is said he does not. The main inter-madhhab dispute arises when one party converts to Islam: Shafi'i, Maliki, and in one narration Ahmad and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) say the kitaba becomes fasid because giving wine to a Muslim involves tamlik (making him owner) or tamalluk (taking ownership), which is prohibited. The Hanafi response distinguishes between specified and unspecified wine: if unspecified, ownership transfers only by delivery, so the Muslim's inability to deliver wine renders the substitute impossible, but the master is still entitled to its price. The ruling is based on istihsan and qiyas, comparing wine to property for non-Muslims. The Hanafi position is that the kitaba remains valid and the master receives the price.

Key Terms
کتابت (kitābah): A contract between a master and his slave whereby the slave is to pay a sum and thereby become free.
خمر (khamr): Wine, a prohibited substance for Muslims but considered property for non-Muslims in Hanafi fiqh.
بدل (badal): The substitute (payment) in a kitaba contract, here wine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The kitaba becomes invalid and the slave remains a slave.
B) The kitaba is valid; the slave must pay the price of the wine to become free.
C) The kitaba is valid only if the wine is specified; otherwise invalid.
D) The kitaba becomes fasid and a new contract must be made.

Key Takeaway
Kitaba for wine is valid for non-Muslims; conversion of a party does not invalidate but converts the substitute to price.

Permissible Actions for a Mukatib: Buying, Selling, and Travel
Ruling on permissible actions for a mukatib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissible actions for a mukatib and explain the reasoning based on the purpose of kitaba.

Core Idea
A mukatib may buy, sell, and travel because these actions enable him to earn his freedom.

This lesson covers the first part of the passage, which clarifies that a mukatib (a slave under a kitaba contract) is permitted to engage in trade and travel. These actions are essential for him to accumulate the funds needed to pay his ransom. The ruling is based on the overarching purpose of the kitaba contract: to facilitate the slave's path to freedom through independent economic activity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions permitted
The passage explicitly states that the mukatib may buy, sell, and travel.
2
Understand the rationale
The reasoning is that the purpose of kitaba is freedom through payment, and these actions are means to that end.
3
Note the additional ruling on selling at a loss (muhabah)
The text permits selling below market value because it is a common trade practice.
4
Recognize the principle
The permissibility is based on the mukatib's independent control over his actions, as required by the contract.

باب ما يجوز للمكاتب ان يفعله
ترجمہ باب اس کے بیان میں جو م کا تب کو کرنا جائز ہے
مکاتب کے لئے بیع وشراء اور سفر کی اجازت ہے
قال ويجوز للمكاتب البيع والشراء والسفر لان موجب الكتابة ان يصير حرا وذلك بمالكية التصرف مستبدا به تصرفا يوصله الى مقصوده وهو نيل الحرية باداء البدل والبيع والشراء من هذا القبيل وكذا السفر لان التجارة ربما لا تتفق فى الحضر فيحتاج الى المسافرة ويملك البيع بالمحاباة لانه من صنيع التجار فان التاجر قد يحابى فى صفقة ليربح فى اخرى. قال فان شرط عليه ان لا يخرج من الكوفة فله ان يخرج استحسانا لان هذا الشرط مخالف لمقتضى العقد وهو مالكية اليد على جهة الاستبداد وثبوت الاختصاص فبطل الشرط وصح العقد لانه شرط لم يتمكن فى صلب العقد وبمثله لا تفسد الكتابة وهذا لان الكتابة تشبه البيع وتشبه النكاح فالحقناها بالبيع فى شرط تمكن فى صلب العقد كما اذا شرط خدمة مجهولة لانه فى البذل وبالنكاح فى شرط لم يتمكن فى صلبه هذا هو الاصل او نقول ان الكتابة في جانب العبد اعتاق لانه اسقاط الملك وهذا الشرط يخص العبد فاعتبر اعتاقا في حق هذا الشرط والاعتاق لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة
ترجمہ جائز ہے مکاتب کے لئے خرید و فروخت اور سفر، کیونکہ مقتضائے کتابت یہ ہے کہ وہ از راہ ید آزاد ہو اور یہ بات مستقلاً ہر ایسے تصرف کا مالک ہونے سے ہوگی جو اس کو اس کے مقصود تک پہنچائے اور وہ ادا ئیگی عوض کے ذریعہ سے آزادی حاصل کرنا ہے۔ اور خریدو فروخت اسی قبیل سے ہے اور ایسے ہی سفر بھی ۔ کیونکہ بسا اوقات دیس میں تجارت ممکن نہیں ہوتی ۔ پس سفر کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے۔ اور وہ گھٹی سے بیچنے کا بھی مالک ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ صنیع تجار سے ہے اس لئے کہ تاجر کبھی ایک بیع [گھاٹا] اٹھاتا ہے تا کہ دوسری میں نفع اٹھائے پھر اگر آقا نے اس پر شرط لگائی کہ کوفہ سے باہر نہ جائے تب بھی وہ استحسانا باہر جا سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ شرط مقتضائے عقد کے خلاف ہے۔ اور وہ بطریق استقلال قبضہ کا مالک ہونا اور اختصاص کا ثابت ہونا ہے پس شرط باطل ہوگی اور عقد صحیح ہو گا اس لئے کہ یہ ایسی شرط ہے جو صلب عقد میں ممکن نہیں ہوئی اور ایسی شرط سے کتابت فاسد نہیں ہوتی ۔ وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ کتابت مشابہ بیع بھی ہے اور مشابہ نکاح بھی ۔ پس ہم نے اس کو بیع کے ساتھ لاحق کیا ایسی شرط میں جو صلب عقد میں متمکن ہو جیسے خدمت مجہولہ کی شرط لگائی۔ کیونکہ یہ بدل کے اندر داخل ہے اور نکاح کے ساتھ لاحق کیا ایسی شرط میں جو صلب عقد میں ممکن نہ ہو۔ پس یہی اصل ہے۔ یا ہم کہتے ہیں کہ کتابت جانب عقد میں اعتاق ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ اسقاط ملک ہے اور یہ شرط غلام کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے تو اس شرط کے حق میں کتابت کو اعتاق اعتبار کیا گیا اور اعتاق شروط فاسدہ سے باطل نہیں ہوتا۔
تشریح قوله باب .. الخ - عنایہ و بنایہ میں ہے کہ کتابت صحیحہ و فاسدہ ہر دو کے احکام سے فراغت کے بعد ان امور کو بیان کر رہے ہیں جو مکاتب کے لئے جائزیا نا جائز ہیں۔ کیونکہ "جواز تصرف عقد صحیح پر موقوف ہے صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ یہ تعلیل اس کی منتفی نہیں
Chapter on what is permissible for the mukatib to do. Translation: Chapter on what is permissible for the mukatib to do. The mukatib is permitted sale, purchase, and travel. He said: It is permissible for the mukatib to buy, sell, and travel, because the requisite of kitaba is that he becomes free, and that is by having independent control over such dispositions that bring him to his goal, which is attaining freedom by paying the substitute. Sale and purchase are of this kind, and likewise travel, because trade may not be possible in the town, so he needs to travel. And he has the right to sell at a loss (muhabah), because it is the practice of merchants, for the merchant may suffer loss in one deal to profit in another. He said: Then if the master stipulates that he should not leave Kufa, then he may leave by istihsan, because this condition contradicts the requisite of the contract, which is independent possession and establishment of special right. So the condition is void and the contract is valid, because it is a condition that is not effective in the core of the contract, and such a condition does not invalidate the kitaba. This is because kitaba resembles sale and also resembles marriage. So we analogized it to sale in a condition that is effective in the core of the contract, such as stipulating unknown service, because it is part of the substitute, and to marriage in a condition that is not effective in its core. This is the principle. Or we say: kitaba from the slave's side is manumission (i'taq), because it is the relinquishment of ownership, and this condition pertains specifically to the slave, so kitaba is considered manumission in respect of this condition, and manumission is not invalidated by invalid conditions. Explanation of his saying 'Chapter...' - In 'Inayah and Binayah it is stated that after finishing the rulings of valid and invalid kitaba, he is now explaining those matters that are permissible or impermissible for the mukatib. Because 'the permissibility of disposition is dependent upon a valid contract'. The author of Nata'ij says that this explanation does not preclude...
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining what actions a mukatib (a slave under kitaba contract) may lawfully do. The matn states he may buy, sell, and travel, and even sell at a loss (muhabah). The reasoning is that the purpose of kitaba is to enable the slave to earn money to pay his ransom and become free; these actions are means to that end. The author then discusses a condition: if the master stipulates that the mukatib not leave a specific city (Kufa), this condition is void but the kitaba remains valid. The proof is by istihsan, based on analogy (qiyas): kitaba resembles both sale and marriage. For conditions that affect the core of the contract (like unknown service), it is analogized to sale, and such conditions would invalidate the kitaba if they are invalid. But for conditions that do not affect the core (like a travel restriction), it is analogized to marriage, where invalid conditions do not void the contract. Alternatively, the condition is void because kitaba from the slave's perspective is an act of manumission (i'taq), and manumission is not invalidated by invalid conditions. The commentary from 'Inayah and Binayah adds that this chapter is placed after the rulings on valid and invalid kitaba.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered into a kitaba contract to earn his freedom by paying a specified sum.
محاباة (muḥābāh): Selling at a price below market value; a form of charitable sale.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Equity-based juristic preference used to derive a ruling contrary to qiyas for a stronger reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary rationale for permitting a mukatib to buy, sell, and travel?
A) Because the master consents
B) To enable him to earn his ransom
C) Because it is required by law
D) To fulfill a religious obligation

Key Takeaway
A mukatib's independent economic activity is essential to the kitaba contract, so buying, selling, and traveling are permissible, including selling at a loss.

Invalid Conditions in Kitaba: Void Condition but Valid Contract
Ruling on the effect of a restrictive condition in a kitaba contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that an invalid condition that does not affect the core of the kitaba contract renders the condition void but the contract remains valid.

Core Idea
An invalid condition in kitaba does not void the contract if it does not affect the core; the condition is void by istihsan.

This lesson focuses on the second part of the passage, which addresses a scenario where the master imposes an invalid condition on the mukatib, such as not leaving a specific city. The Hanafi school rules that such a condition is void by istihsan, but the kitaba contract remains valid. This is based on the unique nature of kitaba, which resembles both sale and marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The master stipulates that the mukatib should not leave Kufa.
2
Apply the ruling
The condition is void, but the kitaba is valid.
3
Understand the proof
The reasoning uses istihsan, analogizing kitaba to marriage for non-core conditions and to sale for core conditions.
4
Distinguish core vs. non-core conditions
A condition that is effective in the core (like unknown service) would invalidate the kitaba because it affects the substitute; a condition that is not effective in the core does not.

Permissibility of Sale, Purchase, and Travel for a Mukatab
States the permissibility and rationale for a mukatab's commercial and travel activities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mukatab's capacity to sell, purchase, and travel, and explain the rational proof behind it.

Core Idea
A mukatab has independent trading rights because kitabah requires freedom through payment, which demands commercial activity.

In this passage from the Kitab al-Mukatab, the Hanafi school establishes that a slave under a contract of manumission (mukatab) has the capacity to engage in sale, purchase, and travel. The ruling is based on the nature of the kitabah contract: the mukatab needs to earn money to pay the consideration, so he must be allowed to trade and travel. Let's examine the proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Who is a mukatab? A slave who has a kitabah contract with his master, agreeing to pay a sum for freedom.
2
Identify the ruling
It is permissible for the mukatab to engage in sale, purchase, and travel. Note that this is mubah (permissible) as a means to fulfill the kitabah.
3
Understand the rational proof
The text provides a rational argument: the essence of kitabah is becoming free, which requires independent financial capacity. Sale, purchase, and travel are means to earn the consideration, thus they are allowed.
The proof is based on the purpose (maqsad) of the contract, not explicit text.
4
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i do not permit a mukatab to transact independently; they require master's permission. The Hanafi school differs due to the independent authority (maliyyat al-tasarruf) granted by the kitabah contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز للمكاتب البيع والشراء والسفر لان موجب الكتابة ان يصير حرا وذلك بمالكية التصرف مستبدا به تصرفا يوصله الى مقصوده وهو نيل الحرية باداء البدل والبيع والشراء من هذا القبيل وكذا السفر لان التجارة ربما لا تتفق فى الحضر فيحتاج الى المسافرة
It is permissible for the mukatab to engage in sale, purchase, and travel, because the requirement of kitabah is that he becomes free, and that is through having exclusive ownership of disposal, independently, by a disposal that leads him to his objective, which is attaining freedom by paying the consideration. Sale and purchase are of this category. Likewise travel, because trade perhaps does not happen in one's hometown, so travel is needed.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Kitab al-Mukatab. The passage establishes the general permissibility for a mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission) to engage in sale, purchase, and travel. The proof given is rational (dalil aqli): the essence of kitabah is that the slave gains freedom through paying the agreed consideration. This freedom is realized when the mukatab has independent control over his actions (maliyyat al-tasarruf). Sale, purchase, and travel are means to earn and pay the consideration, thus they are permissible. The text emphasizes that the mukatab acts independently (mustabiddan bihi). The commentary (tashrih) adds that Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i differed on this issue, but the Hanafi position is as stated.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract with his master, agreeing to pay a sum in exchange for freedom.
كتابة (kitabah): A contract between master and slave whereby the slave pays a specified consideration to become free.
مالكية التصرف (maliyyat al-tasarruf): Ownership of the right to dispose; the mukatab has independent authority over his actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is travel permissible for a mukatab according to this matn?
A) Because it is a way to increase the master's profit.
B) Because trade may not be possible in the hometown, so travel is needed to earn the consideration.
C) Because the Quran commands travel for slaves.
D) Because the kitabah contract requires travel.

Key Takeaway
The mukatab's capacity to sell, purchase, and travel is derived from the purpose of the kitabah contract, which requires independent means to earn freedom.

Condition Prohibiting Travel Is Void for a Mukatab
Ruling that a master's condition barring travel is void, with detailed legal reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a condition restricting travel in a kitabah contract and explain the istihsan-based reasoning involving salb al-aqd and the dual analogy.

Core Idea
A condition contradicting kitabah's purpose is void; the contract remains valid.

This passage addresses a common scenario: a master imposes a condition that the mukatab (contractually enslaved person working for freedom) cannot leave a certain city, such as Kufa. Does this condition invalidate the kitabah contract, or is it simply void? The Hanafi school, using istihsan (juristic preference), rules that the condition is void but the contract remains valid. The reasoning hinges on whether the condition is incorporated into the substance of the contract (salb al-aqd) and on the nature of kitabah as a form of manumission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its source
Read the opening sentence: the master imposes a condition, but the mukatab may still leave by istihsan. This tells us the condition is void and the contract valid. Note that istihsan is the evidence used.
This is a departure from strict qiyas, hence 'istihsan'.
2
Analyze why the condition is void
The condition contradicts the requirement (muqtada) of the contract: independent control (istibdad) over actions. The mukatab must be free to work and earn to pay installments. Restricting travel undermines that independence.
This contradiction makes the condition invalid.
3
Understand the concept of salb al-aqd
The condition is not 'incorporated into the substance' (lam yatamakkan fi salb al-aqd). Conditions that affect the core exchange (like an unknown service in a sale) are incorporated and can invalidate the contract. This condition does not.
Incorporated conditions typically relate to the price or subject matter.
4
Examine the dual analogy
Kitabah resembles sale (in conditions incorporated) and marriage (in conditions not incorporated). Here, the condition is like a marriage condition not incorporated, so it does not invalidate the contract. Alternatively, kitabah is manumission, and manumission is not vitiated by corrupt conditions.
The comparison to sale and marriage is a key Hanafi tahlil.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
According to the commentary, Imam Shafi'i's second view holds that travel is not permissible even without a condition. This ikhtilaf shows the importance of the underlying analogy.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions are based on different analogies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فان شرط عليه ان لا يخرج من الكوفة فله ان يخرج استحسانا لان هذا الشرط مخالف لمقتضى العقد وهو مالكية اليد على جهة الاستبداد وثبوت الاختصاص فبطل الشرط وصح العقد لانه شرط لم يتمكن فى صلب العقد وبمثله لا تفسد الكتابة وهذا لان الكتابة تشبه البيع وتشبه النكاح فالحقناها بالبيع فى شرط تمكن فى صلب العقد كما اذا شرط خدمة مجهولة لانه فى البذل وبالنكاح فى شرط لم يتمكن فى صلبه هذا هو الاصل او نقول ان الكتابة في جانب العبد اعتاق لانه اسقاط الملك وهذا الشرط يخص العبد فاعتبر اعتاقا في حق هذا الشرط والاعتاق لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة
He said: If the master imposed a condition that the mukatab should not leave Kufa, then he may leave by istihsan, because this condition contradicts the requirement of the contract, which is ownership of control in an independent manner and establishment of special right. So the condition is void and the contract is valid, because it is a condition that is not incorporated in the substance of the contract, and the like does not invalidate kitabah. This is because kitabah resembles sale and resembles marriage. So we analogize it to sale in a condition that is incorporated in the substance of the contract, as when an unspecified service is stipulated because it is part of the consideration; and to marriage in a condition that is not incorporated in its substance. This is the principle. Or we say: kitabah on the part of the slave is manumission because it is relinquishment of ownership, and this condition is specific to the slave, so it is considered manumission in respect of this condition, and manumission is not invalidated by corrupt conditions.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage deals with a condition imposed by the master that restricts the mukatab from traveling (e.g., leaving Kufa). The ruling: the condition is void (batil), but the kitabah contract remains valid. The proof uses istihsan: the condition contradicts the inherent purpose of kitabah, which is to give the mukatab independent control (istibdad) over his actions. Since the condition is not part of the substance of the contract (lam yatamakkan fi salb al-'aqd), it does not invalidate it. The text provides two analogical justifications: (1) Kitabah resembles sale in that conditions incorporated into the substance (like unknown service) affect validity; (2) It resembles marriage in conditions not incorporated. Alternatively, from the slave's perspective, kitabah is manumission ('itq), and manumission is not invalidated by invalid conditions. The commentary (tashrih) adds that Imam Shafi'i also holds this view in one of his positions, but his second position considers travel impermissible even without a condition. There is no intra-Hanafi dispute mentioned here, but the principle is clear.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that allows departure from strict analogy for a more equitable ruling.
صلب العقد (salb al-'aqd): The substance or core of the contract; conditions that are integral to the transaction.
اعتبار المعاوضة (i'tibar al-mu'awadah): Consideration of exchange; kitabah is treated as a contract of exchange resembling sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a condition in kitabah that prevents the mukatab from leaving the city?
A) Both the condition and the contract are void.
B) The condition is void but the contract remains valid.
C) The condition is valid and the contract is valid.
D) The contract is invalid regardless of the condition.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a condition in a kitabah contract that contradicts its purpose (like restricting travel) is void, but the contract itself remains valid, relying on istihsan and the distinction between incorporated and non-incorporated conditions.

Marriage of a Mukatab: Authority and Restrictions
Ruling on mukatab's marriage with rationale and dissenting view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mukatab marrying without his master's permission and explain the rationale and the differing view of Ibn Abi Layla.

Core Idea
A mukatab cannot marry without master's permission because marriage is a financial burden, not a means of earning.

This lesson examines a specific restriction on a mukatab: marriage. The Hanafi school considers marriage a voluntary act that could hinder the mukatab's ability to pay his kitaba installments. We will explore the ruling, the rationale, and a differing opinion from Ibn Abi Layla.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage and note that the mukatab does not have the authority to marry himself without his master's permission. This is the Hanafi position shared by the three Imams.
2
Understand the rationale
The text explains that kitaba is meant to break prohibitions on earning while ownership remains. Marriage is not a means to earning; it incurs dower and maintenance obligations, conflicting with the kitaba's purpose.
The master's permission allows marriage because the master's ownership remains and consent is given.
3
Note the alternative view
Ibn Abi Layla holds that if the master did not explicitly forbid marriage, the mukatab may marry without permission. If there is a condition, then no marriage.
This difference affects whether marriage is valid without explicit consent.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi fatwa position is that the mukatab cannot marry without master's permission regardless of whether a condition exists, as stated by the text.
This is the relied-upon view in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح قوله ولا يتزوج ... الخ - احناف وائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک مکاتب کو آقا کی اجازت کے بغیر اپنا نکاح کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے ( ابن ابی لیلی کہتے ہیں کہ اگر آقا کی طرف سے نکاح نہ کرنے کی شرط ہوتب تو اختیار نہیں ہے اور گر اس کی شرط نہ ہو تو آقا کی اجازت کے بغیر بھی کر سکتا ہے ) اس لئے کہ کتابت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ آقا کی ملک قائم ہوتے ہوئے ممانعت تصرف کو توڑ دیا جائے تا کہ وہ مقصود تک رسائی کا وسیلہ ہو۔ اور نکاح اس مقصد کا وسیلہ نہیں بلکہ اس میں اور محل ہے کیونکہ وہ نکاح کر کے ادائیگی مہر اور نان نفقہ کے چکر میں پڑ جائے گا۔ اور آقا کی اجازت سے نکاح کا اختیار اس لئے ہے کہ اس میں آقا کی ملک قائم ہے۔
قوله ولا يهب ... الخ - مکاتب کو ہبہ وصدقہ کرنے کا بھی اختیار نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ از قبیل تبرعات ہیں اور مکاتب تبرعات کا مجاز نہیں ہے البتہ شی بیر کے ہبہ کی اجازت ہے کیونکہ یہ ضروریات تجارت میں سے ہے اس لئے کہ کبھی اہل معاملہ کی ضیافت کرنی پڑتی ہے کبھی کسی کو سواری وغیرہ کوئی چیز عارت دینی پڑتی ہے تاکہ تجار کے ساتھ لین دین کے تعلقات استوارر ہیں ۔
قوله المجاهزون .. الخ - عوام کی زبان میں مجاہز مالدار تاجر کو کہتے ہیں یہاں اس سے مراد محجز ہے جو تجار کو متاع فاخرہ کے ساتھ روانہ کرے۔ پس اس کی تحریف کر کے مجاہز بنا دیا گیا (مغرب)۔
قوله ولا يتكفل ... الخ - مکاتب کو یہ بھی اختیار نہیں ہے کہ کفالت قبول کرے خواہ کفالت جان کی ہو یا مال کی۔ نیز مکفول عنہ کے حکم سے ہو یا بلا حکم ۔ اسی طرح مال نقد قرض دینے کا بھی اختیار نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ امور از قبیل تبرعات ہیں نہ ضروریات تجارت میں سے ہیں اور نہ توابع اکتساب ہیں۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر مکاتب نے کوئی چیز بشرط عوض ہبہ کی تو یہ بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ابتداء میں ہبہ بھی احسان ہوتا ہے اور عقد کتابت میں تبرع داخل نہیں ہے۔
Commentary on the saying: 'And he may not marry... etc.' - According to the Hanafis and the three Imams, the mukatab does not have the authority to marry himself without the permission of his master. (Ibn Abi Layla says: If there is a condition from the master not to marry, then he has no authority; but if there is no such condition, he may marry even without the master's permission.) This is because the meaning of kitaba is to break the prohibition of disposal while the master's ownership remains, so that it may be a means to reach the objective. Marriage is not a means to this objective; rather, it is another matter, because by marrying he will fall into the cycle of paying dower and maintenance. And the authority to marry with the master's permission is because in it the master's ownership remains.
The saying: 'And he may not give gifts... etc.' - The mukatab also does not have the authority to give gifts and charity. Because these are of the category of voluntary acts, and the mukatab is not authorized for voluntary acts. However, a gift of something trivial [slight?] is permitted because it is among the necessities of trade, as sometimes one has to host people of dealing, and sometimes one needs to lend a riding animal or something to someone to maintain business relations.
The saying: 'Al-Mujahizun... etc.' - In common language, Mujahiz is said for a wealthy merchant. Here, the intended meaning is Muhajiz, who dispatches merchants with expensive goods. So it was altered to Mujahiz (Mughrib).
The saying: 'And he may not undertake kafala... etc.' - The mukatab also does not have the authority to accept kafala, whether it is kafala for life or for property, nor whether it is by order of the principal or without order. Similarly, he does not have authority to lend cash money, because these matters are of the category of voluntary acts, neither from the necessities of trade nor from the accessories of earning. To the extent that if the mukatab gives a gift with consideration, that too is not permissible, because a gift is initially a favor, and voluntary giving is not included in the contract of kitaba.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an expansion of the matn from al-Hidayah, detailing the restrictions on a mukatab (a slave who has contracted with his master to earn his freedom by paying installments) regarding non-commercial voluntary acts. The passage explains that a mukatab is not permitted to marry, give gifts (except trivial hospitality gifts necessary for trade), accept kafala (suretyship), or lend money without his master's permission. The rationale is that these are tabarru' (voluntary acts) not part of kasb (earning) which is the focus of the kitaba contract. The text also notes that giving a gift with consideration is still invalid because it begins as a gift (a favor). The discussion includes a note on Ibn Abi Layla's alternative view on marriage conditional permission, and clarifies the word 'mujahiz' as a common term for a wealthy merchant, correcting it to 'muhajiz'. All rulings are consistent with the Hanafi school: the mukatab's authority is limited to acts that generate income or are necessary for trade, not voluntary benevolence.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitaba contract with his master, agreeing to pay a sum in installments in exchange for eventual freedom.
کتابت (kitaba): A contract of manumission by payment: the slave pays installments to the master to earn freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of a mukatab's marriage if contracted without his master's permission?
A) Valid, because he is partially free.
B) Invalid (batil), because he lacks authority.
C) Valid only if he promises to pay the dower from his earnings.
D) Permissible if the master does not object within a month.

Key Takeaway
A mukatab's marriage without his master's permission is invalid in the Hanafi school due to the non-earning nature of marriage.

A Mukatab's Prohibited Voluntary Acts: Gifts, Kafala, and Lending
Rules on a mukatab's voluntary non-commercial acts: gifts, kafala, lending

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which voluntary acts (hiba, sadaqa, kafala, qard) are prohibited for a mukatab and distinguish the exception for trivial business gifts.

Core Idea
A mukatab is barred from all tabarru' acts except trivial gifts necessary for trade.

This lesson dives into the general prohibition on a mukatab from engaging in acts of generosity and surety. The unifying principle is that these are voluntary transfers not aimed at earning, which contradicts the kitaba's purpose. However, small gifts essential for business relationships are allowed.

Guided Path
1
List the prohibited acts
From the text, identify the acts: giving gifts (hiba), charity (sadaqa), accepting kafala (suretyship) for life or property, and lending money (qard).
2
Identify the common element
All these acts are tabarru' (voluntary) and not part of the earning process (kasb).
3
Understand the exception
A gift of something trivial (shay' yasir) is allowed if it is a necessity of trade, e.g., hosting business partners or lending a riding animal.
This exception is based on urf (custom of merchants).
4
Note the ruling on gift with consideration
Even a gift with consideration (bishart 'iwad) is prohibited because it starts as a gift (tabarru') and is not covered by kitaba.
Thus, no disguise works to circumvent the prohibition.

Key Terms
تبرع (tabarru'): A voluntary act of giving or benefiting others without compensation, such as gifts, charity, loans, and suretyship.
کفالت (kafala): A contract of suretyship where one person guarantees the presence or debt of another.
شی بیر (shay' yasir): A trivial thing; in context, a gift of small value.

Mukatab's Authority Over His Slaves: Marriage and Kitaba
Inter-madhhab dispute on mukatab's commercial acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on a mukatab's authority to marry his slave woman and make his slave a mukatab, and evaluate the opposing qiyas-based argument using istihsan.

Core Idea
A mukatab can make his slave a mukatab because kitaba is an earning contract, not a grant of freedom.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a key dispute: can a mukatab (a slave under kitaba) exercise authority over his own slaves? The Hanafi school, using istihsan, permits marriage and kitaba of his slaves, while others (Zufar, Shafi'i, Ahmad) oppose by qiyas, arguing that the end result is freedom. Understanding this ruling reveals the Hanafi prioritization of commercial benefit over formal analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts
Note the two acts: a mukatab marrying his slave woman and making his slave a mukatab. Both are initially stated as permissible.
These are commercial acts, not pure manumission.
2
State the qiyas objection
The opposing view (Zufar, Shafi'i) uses qiyas: since kitaba leads to freedom, and the mukatab lacks authority over freedom, it should be invalid (like manumission for property).
The illa is the end result (freedom).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response via istihsan
The Hanafi school overrides qiyas with istihsan: kitaba is an earning contract (iktisab al-mal), like sale or marriage of a slave woman. Ownership only transfers after payment, so it does not grant freedom immediately.
Istihsan considers the immediate nature, not the ultimate outcome.
4
Apply the wala' rules
The passage then discusses wala' when the second slave pays before or after the first's freedom. This shows the practical implications of the ruling.
Wala' goes to the master if the second pays before the first is freed, otherwise to the first mukatab.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Compare the practical outcomes: under Hanafi law, a mukatab can expand his business by making his slaves mukatabs; under opposing schools, he cannot.
This is a genuine difference in Fiqh al-muamalat.

مکاتب نے اپنی باندی کا نکاح کر دیا تو یہ جائز ہے
فان زوج امته جاز لانه اكتساب للمال فإنه يتملك به المهر فدخل تحت العقد قال وكذا لك ان كاتب عبده والقياس ان لا يجوز وهو قول زفر والشافعى لان مآله العتق والمكاتب ليس من اهله كالاعتاق على مال وجه الاستحسان انه عقد اكتساب للمال فيملكه كتزويج الامة وكالبيع وقد يكون هو انفع له من البيع لانه لا يزيل الملك الا بعد وصول البدل اليه والبيع يزيله قبله ولهذا يملكه الاب والوصى ثم هو يوجب للمملوك مثل ما هو ثابت له بخلاف الاعتاق على مال لانه يوجب فوق ما هو ثابت له. قال فان ادى الثانى قبل ان يعتق الاول فولاءه للمولى لان له فيه نوع ملک ويصح اضافة الاعتاق اليه في الجملة فاذا تعذر اضافته الى مباشر العقد لعدم الاهلية اضيف اليه كما فى العبد اذا اشترى شيئا يثبت الملك للمولى. قال فلو ادى الأول بعد ذلك وعتق لا ينتقل الولاء اليه لان المولى جعل معتقا والولاء لا ينتقل من المعتق وان ادى الثانى بعد عتق الاول فولاؤه له لان العاقد من اهل ثبوت الولاء وهو الأصل فيثبت له

If the mukatab marries his slave woman, it is permissible.
For he married his slave woman, it is permissible because it is an acquisition of wealth, as he becomes the owner of the dower through it, so it falls under the contract [of kitaba]. He said: Likewise, if he makes his slave a mukatab, and by analogy it is not permissible, and it is the saying of Zufar and al-Shafi'i, because its end is freedom, and the mukatab is not of its people, like manumission for property. The basis of istihsan is that it is a contract of acquisition of wealth, so he owns it, like the marriage of a slave woman and like sale. And it may be more beneficial for him than sale, because it does not remove ownership except after the substitute reaches him, while sale removes it before. For this reason, the father and executor own it. Then it establishes for the slave the same as is established for him, unlike manumission for property because it establishes more than what is established for him. He said: If the second one pays before the first is freed, then his wala' is for the master, because the master has a kind of ownership over him, and attributing the manumission to him is valid in some respect. When attribution to the direct agent becomes impossible due to lack of eligibility, it is attributed to him, just as when a slave buys something, ownership is established for the master. He said: If the first one pays after that and becomes free, the wala' does not transfer to him, because the master is made the manumitter, and wala' does not transfer from the manumitter. And if the second pays after the freeing of the first, then his wala' is for him [the first], because the contracting party is eligible for establishing wala', and he is the principal, so it is established for him.

Commentary... The saying: 'And likewise if he makes a mukatab... etc.' - If the mukatab makes one of his trade slaves a mukatab, then according to us it is valid by istihsan. Imam Malik, Qadi Hanbali, and the Zahiris also hold this view. The requisite of analogy was that it should not be permissible. Consequently, the saying of Imam Zufar, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad is this. Because the end of the contract of kitaba is that he becomes free, while the mukatab does not have the authority over that, just as he does not have the authority to manumit for property. The basis of istihsan is that wealth is obtained through kitaba. So just as on the basis of earning wealth, the mukatab is authorized to marry his slave woman and to buy and sell, similarly he will be authorized to make a mukatab. Rather, sometimes kitaba is more beneficial than sale, because the contract of kitaba does not remove the ownership of the slave mukatab until the substitute reaches him, while in sale, ownership is removed before receipt of price. Despite this, when the mukatab is the owner of the sale, he is even more so the owner of kitaba. For this reason, the father and executor have the authority to make the slave of a minor child a mukatab.
The saying: 'Then it establishes... etc.' - Then the first mukatab can establish for the second mukatab, i.e., his slave, the same thing that is established for the first mukatab through the first kitaba. And that is ownership of possession and authority of disposal, which the first mukatab possesses through kitaba. And the rule is that whoever himself owns a thing can make another the owner of it, like the lender lends, the lessee leases. The powers that the first possesses, he can establish for his slave whom he made a mukatab. Contrary to manumission for property, because he cannot free his slave for property, because this manumission would establish for the slave powers that are not greater than the powers of the mukatab himself. The reason is that in the case of manumission for property, the slave of the first mukatab attains immediate freedom upon acceptance, not contingent on payment, whereas the first mukatab does not possess this. Because the mukatab only possesses the right to freedom, while the manumitter for property possesses actual freedom. Now if the mukatab's freeing his slave for property were permissible, it would necessitate that the mukatab gave a slave such powers...
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and expansion of a matn from al-Hidayah concerning a mukatab's actions regarding his own slaves. The text first states that if a mukatab marries his slave woman, it is valid (permissible). This is because it is a way of earning wealth (iktisab al-mal) through the dower, so it falls under the kitaba contract. The same applies if the mukatab makes his own slave a mukatab (contract of kitaba with the slave). By qiyas (analogy), this would be invalid because the end result is freedom, and the mukatab lacks the authority to grant freedom (like manumission for property). This is the view of Imam Zufar (a Hanafi) and Imam al-Shafi'i, and also Imam Ahmad. However, the Hanafi school, along with Imam Malik and others, accepts it based on istihsan (juristic preference). Istihsan sees it as a contract for earning money, akin to selling or marrying off a slave woman. In fact, it may be more beneficial than selling because ownership of the slave only transfers after payment, unlike sale where ownership transfers immediately. The commentary then details the rule of wala' (patronage) in cases where a mukatab makes his slave a mukatab and the second pays before or after the first's freedom. If the second pays before the first is freed, the wala' goes to the original master; if the second pays after the first's freedom, the wala' goes to the first mukatab (now free). The reasoning involves the capacity for manumission: the first mukatab cannot manumit his slave directly for property because that would grant full freedom immediately, while the slave's freedom is contingent on payment in kitaba. The passage exemplifies the Hanafi use of istihsan to override qiyas for the benefit of trade.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference over qiyas, used here to validate a mukatab's act of making his slave a mukatab despite apparent analogy.
ولاء (wala'): Patronage rights established between a manumitter and the freed slave, granting inheritance rights in certain cases.
مملوک (mamluk): A slave owned by another, specifically here the slave owned by the mukatab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the basis for allowing a mukatab to make his slave a mukatab?
A) It is based on qiyas to manumission for property
B) It is based on istihsan, treating it as an earning contract like sale
C) It is allowed because the mukatab is free in all transactions
D) It is allowed by ijma' of all scholars

Key Takeaway
A mukatab may make his slave a mukatab because the contract is an acquisition of wealth, not a direct manumission, as established by the Hanafi principle of istihsan.

Mukatab Making His Slave a Mukatab: Istihsan Ruling and Wala' Distribution
Explains ruling and wala' distribution for mukatab making his slave a mukatab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mukatab making his slave a mukatab, explain the istihsan reasoning, and apply the wala' distribution rules based on payment timing.

Core Idea
A mukatab may make his slave a mukatab by istihsan; wala' goes to the master until the first mukatab is free.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from the Book of Kitabah: whether a mukatab (a slave under a manumission contract) can, in turn, make his own slave a mukatab. The Hanafi school permits this by istihsan (juristic preference), diverging from strict qiyas. The passage also clarifies the distribution of wala' (patronage) based on the timing of payments. Understanding this ruling deepens your grasp of the interplay between earning capacity, limited slave status, and the transfer of wala'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
State the Hanafi position: a mukatab making his slave a mukatab is permissible (mubah) based on istihsan. Note that qiyas would render it impermissible, as held by Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i.
The text explicitly contrasts istihsan with qiyas.
2
Analyze the qiyas argument
Reconstruct the qiyas: the asl is that a mukatab cannot free his slave for money (itq 'ala mal) because freedom requires full ownership. The far' is making a kitabah. The illa is that both lead to freedom, which the mukatab cannot grant. Therefore kitabah is also impermissible.
This is the opposing view.
3
Understand the istihsan reasoning
Istihsan refutes the illa: kitabah is not a direct grant of freedom but a contract for earning. The mukatab is authorized to earn, and kitabah is a means of earning. Moreover, kitabah keeps ownership until payment, so it does not transfer freedom immediately. Hence istihsan overrides qiyas.
The text lists several supporting analogies: marriage of slave-girl, sale, and authority of father/executor.
4
Apply wala' distribution rules
Work through the three scenarios: (1) sub-mukatab pays before first mukatab → wala' goes to original master (first's master). (2) Sub-mukatab pays after first is free → wala' goes to first mukatab. (3) Simultaneous payment → wala' goes to master. Explain the principle: wala' is attributed to the nearest cause (manumittor) possible, and only shifts to the remote cause when the immediate cause is incapable.
The text uses the analogy of the authorized slave (abd ma'dhun).
