كتاب المكاتب
دے دیے جن کا وہ خود بھی مالک نہیں ہے یعنی خودا بھی غلام ہے اور اس نے دوسرے کو آزاد کر دیا ۔ حالانکہ یہ ناممکن ہے لہذا مال پر مکاتب کرنا جائز ہوگا لیکن مال پر آزاد کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ قوله فان ادى الثانى ... الخ - مکاتب کا اپنے مملوک کو مکاتب کرنا جائز ہے جیسا کہ اوپر معلوم ہو چکا۔ اب اس کی تین صورتیں ہیں۔ مکاتب ثانی (مکاتب المکاتب ) بدل کتابت کی ادائیگی مکاتب اول کی ادائیگی سے پہلے کرے گا۔
۲۔ یا اس کے بعد ۔ ۳۔ یا اس کے ساتھ ساتھ ۔
پہلی اور تیسری صورت میں مکاتب ثانی کی ولاء مکاتب کے آقا کو ملے گی۔ اس لئے کہ مکاتب ثانی میں آقا کی بھی ایک طرح کی ملکیت ہے۔ بایں معنی کہ مکاتب ثانی بواسطه مکاتب اول ، آقا کا مکاتب ہے تو اول کے لئے آقا کی کتابت بمنزلہ علیہ العلہ ہوئی (یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر مکاتب اول ادائیگی بدل سے عاجز ہو جائے تو اسکی طرح مکاتب ثانی بھی آقا کی ملک ہوگا ) نیز آقا کی طرف اعتناق کی نسبت فی الجملہ صحیح ہے۔ چنانچہ مجاز بولتے ہیں۔ مولی زید معتق زید۔ اگر چہ وہ معتق ہو یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے موالی فلاں کے لئے وصیت کی۔ حالانکہ زندوں میں فلاں کا کوئی معتق نہیں ہے البتہ معتق المعتق ہے تو وصیت کا مستحق وہی ہو گا۔
پھر مکاتب ثانی کو آزاد کرنے کی نسبت چونکہ مکاتب اول کی طرف اس وجہ سے متعذر ہے کہ وہ ابھی غلام ہے اس لئے اعتاق کی نسبت اس کے آقا کی طرف کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ حکم جیسے علت کی طرف مضاف ہوتا ہے۔ ایسے ہی علتہ العلہ کی طرف بھی مضاف ہوتا ہے
جب کہ علت کی طرف اس کی اضافت متعد ر ہو جائے۔ جیسے عبد ماذون اگر کوئی چیز خرید لے تو اسکے آقا کی ملکیت ثابت ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ عبد ماذون کو مالک ہونے کی لیاقت نہیں ہے اگر چہ اصلی خریدار وہی عبد ماذون ہے۔ بہر کیف مکاتب اول چونکہ ابھی غلام ہے اور اس کو ولاء کی لیاقت نہیں ہے اس لئے ولاء اس کے آقا کو ملے گی۔
قوله فلو ادى الاول ... الخ پھر اگر آقا کو مکاتب ثانی کی ولاء ملنے کے بعد مکاتب اول نے اپنا بدل کتابت ادا کیا اور آزاد ہو گیا تو اس کے مکاتب کی ولاء اس کی جانب منتقل نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ آقا معتق قرار پا چکا اور ولاء آزاد کنندہ سے منتقل نہیں ہوتی ۔ کیونکہ یہاں آقا ایک لحاظ سے مباشرة معتق ہے بخلاف جز ولاء کے کہ وہاں باندی کا آقا بچہ کو مباشرة آزاد کرنے والا نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اعتاق اُم کے اعتبار سے تسبیا معتق ہوتا ہے۔ اس بارے میں اصل کلیہ یہ ہے کہ سبب کی طرف حکم کی اضافت اسی وقت کی جاتی ہے جب علت کی طرف اضافت کرنا متعذر ہو۔ اور جر ولاء والے مسئلہ میں تعذر اس وقت تک ہے۔ جب تک باپ آزاد نہیں ہوا جب وہ آزاد ہو گیا تو ضرورت ختم ہوگئی۔ لہذا اولاء پوری قوم کی طرف منتقل ہو جائیگی۔ اور اگر مکاتب دوم نے اپنا بدل کتابت مکاتب اول کے ( بذریعہ اداء بدل کتابت ) آزاد ہو جانے کے بعد ادا کیا اور آزاد ہوا تو اس کی ولاء مکاتب اول کو ملے گی ۔ کیونکہ اب اس کو دلاء کی لیاقت حاصل ہے اور اصل مکاتب وہی ہے تو ولا بھی اسی کو حاصل ہوگی ۔
The Book of Kitabah. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya Volume 12: Translation: If a mukatab marries his female slave, it is permissible. Because it is earning wealth. Because he will own the dowry through it, so it falls under acquisition. Similarly, if he makes his slave a mukatab, and by qiyas it would not be permissible. This is the saying of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i. Because the end result of kitabah is freedom, and the mukatab is not eligible for it, just as he is not eligible to free for money. The reason of istihsan is that this is a contract of earning wealth, so he will own it. Like marrying a female slave and selling his own property. Rather, kitabah is sometimes more beneficial than sale, because it does not remove ownership except after the payment reaches him, whereas sale removes it before. That is why a father and executor own it. Then, the contract of kitabah will establish for the owned slave the same thing established for the mukatab. Then, if the second (sub-mukatab) pays before the first is freed, his wala' will be for the master. Because the master has a kind of ownership in him, and attribution of manumission to him is valid in some sense. When attribution to the direct contractor became impossible due to lack of eligibility, it was attributed to his master. Like an authorized slave (abd ma'dhun): if he buys something, ownership is established for the master. Then if the first (mukatab) pays after that and becomes free, the wala' will not transfer to him. Because the master has been deemed the manumittor, and wala' does not transfer from the manumittor. And if the second pays after the first's freedom, his wala' will be for him (the first mukatab), because now the contractor is qualified for wala', and he is the original, so wala' will be established for him. Commentary: 'And likewise if he makes a kitabah...' - If a mukatab makes a kitabah with one of his trade slaves, in our school by istihsan it is also valid. Imam Malik, Qadi Hanbali, and the Zahiris also hold it. The requirement of qiyas was that it be not permissible. Therefore Imam Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad's saying is this. Because the end result of the kitabah contract is that he becomes free. But the mukatab does not have that authority, just as he does not have authority to free in exchange for money. The reason of istihsan is that wealth is obtained through kitabah. So just as based on earning wealth the mukatab is authorized to marry his female slave and to buy and sell, similarly he will be permitted to make a kitabah. Rather, sometimes kitabah is more beneficial than sale, because the kitabah contract does not remove the ownership of the slave-mukatab until the kitabah payment reaches him, whereas in sale ownership is removed before receipt of price. Moreover, since a mukatab owns sale, he will own kitabah a fortiori. For this reason, a father and executor have authority to make a kitabah for the slave of their minor child. 'Then it establishes...' - Then the first mukatab can establish for the second mukatab, i.e., his slave, the same thing established for the first mukatab through the first kitabah. And that is possession (milk al-yad) and ownership of disposal, which the first mukatab has through kitabah. And it is a rule that whoever himself owns something can make another its owner, like the lender lends and the lessee leases. Whatever authorities the first has, he can establish for this slave he has made a mukatab. Unlike freeing for money, for he cannot free his slave for money, because this would establish for the owned slave authorities that exceed the mukatab's own authorities. The reason is that in freeing for money, the slave of the first mukatab would obtain immediate freedom by mere acceptance, not dependent on payment, while the first mukatab does not have that. Because a mukatab only has the right to freedom (haqq al-hurriyya), while a person who frees for money obtains actual freedom (haqiqat al-hurriyya). If a mukatab freeing his slave for money were permissible, it would necessitate that the mukatab gave to a slave authorities that he himself does not own, i.e., he is himself a slave and freed another. This is impossible. Therefore making a kitabah for money is permissible, but freeing for money is not permissible. 'If the second pays...' - It is established that a mukatab making his slave a mukatab is permissible. There are three scenarios: the second mukatab pays before the first mukatab pays; or after; or simultaneously. In the first and third scenarios, the wala' of the second mukatab goes to the first mukatab's master. Because the master has a kind of ownership in the second mukatab. That is, the second mukatab is, through the first, a mukatab of the master, so the master's kitabah for the first is like the cause of the cause. (Hence if the first becomes unable to pay, the second also becomes the master's property.) Also, attribution of manumission to the master is valid in some sense. Thus it is figuratively said: 'The master of Zaid is the manumittor of Zaid,' even if he is (only) the manumittor of the manumittor. This is why if someone makes a bequest to the patrons (mawali) of so-and-so, while none of so-and-so's manumittors are alive, but there is a manumittor of the manumittor, the bequest goes to him. Then, because attribution of freeing the second mukatab to the first mukatab is impossible since he is still a slave, the attribution is made to his master. For a ruling is attributed to the cause, and also to the cause of the cause when attribution to the cause becomes impossible. Like an authorized slave: if he buys something, ownership is established for his master, because an authorized slave is not capable of ownership, although the actual buyer is the authorized slave. In short, since the first mukatab is still a slave and not qualified for wala', the wala' goes to his master. 'If the first pays...' - Then if after the master receives the wala' of the second, the first mukatab pays his kitabah and becomes free, the wala' of his (the first's) mukatab does not transfer to him. Because the master has been established as the manumittor, and wala' does not transfer from the manumittor. For here the master is in a sense the direct manumittor, unlike the case of wala' of a child (jar), where the master of the mother is not the direct manumittor of the child, but becomes manumittor by causality through the mother's manumission. The principle in this regard is that attribution of a ruling to the cause is only done when attribution to the cause proper is impossible. In the issue of jar wala', the impossibility continues until the father is freed. When he becomes free, the need ends, so the wala' transfers to him fully. And if the second mukatab pays his kitabah after the first mukatab becomes free (by paying his kitabah), and becomes free, his wala' goes to the first mukatab. Because now he (the first) is qualified for wala', and he is the original, so wala' will accrue to him.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) from Ashraf al-Hidaya on the ruling of a mukatab making his own slave a mukatab. The author begins by stating a parallel ruling: if a mukatab marries his female slave, it is permissible because it is a means of earning (kasb). Similarly, making his slave a mukatab is also permissible by istihsan, even though qiyas (analogy) would render it impermissible. The qiyas argument, attributed to Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i, is that kitabah leads to freedom, and a mukatab lacks authority to free, just as he cannot free for a price. The istihsan counter-argument: kitabah is a contract for earning; the mukatab is empowered to earn through trade, marriage of his slave, etc. Moreover, kitabah is sometimes more beneficial than sale because ownership does not transfer until payment is completed. The authority of a father or executor to make kitabah for a minor's slave is cited as support. Then the text clarifies the legal effect: the first mukatab can confer onto his slave the same rights he himself has—possession (milk al-yad) and disposal (tasarruf)—but not the right to free for money (itq 'ala mal), because that would give the slave immediate freedom, which the mukatab himself does not have (he only has the right to eventual freedom). The passage then addresses three scenarios of payment timing for the two mukatabs and the distribution of wala' (patronage). If the sub-mukatab pays before or simultaneously with the first mukatab's payment, wala' goes to the original master because the first mukatab is not yet free and thus incapable of holding wala'; the master is considered the manumittor by attribution. If the sub-mukatab pays after the first mukatab becomes free, wala' goes to the first mukatab because he is now qualified. This is analogous to an authorized slave (abd ma'dhun) where purchase ownership goes to the master due to the slave's incapacity. The key principle: attribution of a ruling goes to the nearest cause, and only to the remote cause when attribution to the immediate cause is impossible.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract with his master, entitling him to earn and pay for his freedom in installments.
کتابت (kitābah): A contract between a master and slave whereby the slave agrees to pay a sum in installments in exchange for eventual freedom.
ولاء (walā’): The right of patronage (guardianship) that belongs to the manumittor over a freed slave, entitling him to inherit from the freed slave under certain conditions.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that allows departure from strict qiyas in favor of a more equitable result based on a stronger proof or custom.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical deduction; extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a shared effective cause ('illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a mukatab making his own slave a mukatab?
A) Permissible by qiyas
B) Not permissible by istihsan
C) Permissible by istihsan
D) Not permissible by qiyas but permissible by ijma'

Key Takeaway
A mukatab may make his slave a mukatab by istihsan, and wala' distribution depends on the payment order: first to the master, then to the free mukatab.

beginner
6 min
The Mukatab's Limited Authority over His Slave
States the ruling that a mukatab's freeing, selling, or marrying his slave is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three actions a mukatab cannot perform with his slave and explain why they are invalid.

Core Idea
A mukatab cannot grant immediate freedom because he himself does not possess it.

In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling from Al-Hidayah: a mukatab (a slave who has contracted to earn his freedom) cannot free his own slave for money, sell him to himself, or marry him. The reason is that these actions fall outside his authorized sphere of earning (kasb). Understanding this limitation is key to grasping the mukatab's legal capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited actions
The text lists itq 'ala mal (freeing for payment), bay' min nafsih (selling the slave to himself), and tazwij (marrying) his slave. Marrying means acting as guardian to marry off the slave.
These are the only explicit prohibitions; other transactions may be permissible.
2
Understand the reason given
The author says 'these things are not from earning' (laysa min al-kasb). The mukatab's authority is limited to activities that help him earn money to pay his kitabah.
The underlying principle is that the mukatab cannot confer immediate freedom as he himself is not yet free.
3
Contrast with permissible actions
The mukatab is allowed to make a kitabah contract with his slave (i.e., let the slave earn his freedom), which is a form of earning. Kitabah is permissible because it does not grant immediate freedom.
Selling the slave to a third party is also permissible as it is a normal trade.
4
State the hukm
All three actions are batil (invalid) and produce no legal effect. If performed, the slave remains enslaved to the mukatab and the kitabah contract continues unaffected.
No legal consequences flow from a batil act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و ان اعتق عبده على مال او باعه من نفسه او زوج عبده لم يجز لان هذه الاشياء ليست من الكسب ولا
مکاتب نے اپنے غلام کو مال پر آزاد کیا یا اس کو اسی کے ہاتھ بیچ دیا یا اپنے غلام کو بیاہ دیا تو یہ جائز نہیں
He (the author) said: And if he (the mukatab) frees his slave for money, or sells him to himself, or marries his slave, it is not permissible, because these things are not from earning nor... The mukatab freed his slave for money, or sold him to himself, or married his slave – this is not permissible.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement (matn) from Al-Hidayah. It lists three actions that a mukatab is not permitted to do with his slave: (1) freeing the slave in exchange for a payment (itq 'ala mal), (2) selling the slave back to the slave himself (i.e., the slave purchases himself from the mukatab), and (3) marrying his slave (to anyone). The reason given is that these actions are not part of earning (kasb). Unlike the permissibility of making a kitabah contract, which is a means of earning, these transactions either grant immediate freedom (freeing for money) or are not normally undertaken for trade purposes. The ruling is clear and without internal dispute.

Key Terms
اعتاق على مال (i‘tāq ‘alā māl): Freeing a slave in exchange for a payment, where the slave becomes immediately free upon accepting the contract.
بيع من نفسه (bay‘ min nafsih): Selling the slave to himself; effectively the slave purchases himself from the master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Can a mukatab free his slave in exchange for a payment?
A) Yes, because it is a form of earning
B) Yes, because he is authorized to trade
C) No, because it is not from the kasb and he does not have authority to grant immediate freedom
D) No, but he can do it through a third party

Key Takeaway
A mukatab's authority is limited to earning; he cannot grant immediate freedom, sell the slave to himself, or act as guardian for marriage.

Ruling on a Mukatab Making His Slave a Mukatab and Transfer of Wala'
Explains the ruling on mukatab al-mukatab and transfer of wala'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a mukatab making his slave a mukatab and explain when the wala' transfers to the master versus the first mukatab.

Core Idea
Wala' transfers to the master when the first mukatab is still a slave, but to the first mukatab if he becomes free before the second pays.

This lesson examines the permissibility and consequences of a mukatab (a slave under contract of manumission) making his own slave a mukatab. The key issue is who receives the wala' (patronage) of the second mukatab, which depends on the timing of payments and the capacity of the first mukatab to hold wala'.

Guided Path
1
Understand the permissibility
Identify that a mukatab making his slave a mukatab is permissible (ja'iz) in the Hanafi school, as stated in the text.
This is the starting point; the ruling is mubah.
2
Analyze the three timing scenarios
The second mukatab's payment can occur before, after, or simultaneously with the first mukatab's payment. Determine which scenarios result in wala' going to the master.
Scenarios 1 and 3 (before or simultaneous) → master; scenario 2 (after) → depends on first mukatab's status.
3
Apply the principle of causal attribution
The ruling attributes wala' to the master because the first mukatab lacks capacity. If attribution to the direct cause is impossible, the ruling goes to the cause of the cause.
Analogy to ma'dhun slave's purchase: ownership goes to the master.
4
Determine wala' transfer after first mukatab is freed
If the second pays after the first becomes free, the first mukatab now has capacity and receives wala'. If the first becomes free after the master already received wala', it does not transfer back.
Wala' once established with the master is immutable.

پہلے کرے گا۔ ۲۔ یا اس کے بعد ۔ ۳۔ یا اس کے ساتھ ساتھ ۔ پہلی اور تیسری صورت میں مکاتب ثانی کی ولاء مکاتب کے آقا کو ملے گی۔ اس لئے کہ مکاتب ثانی میں آقا کی بھی ایک طرح کی ملکیت ہے۔ بایں معنی کہ مکاتب اول کو ملے گی ۔ کیونکہ اب اس کو دلاء کی لیاقت حاصل ہے اور اصل مکاتب وہی ہے تو ولا بھی اسی کو حاصل ہوگی ۔
His saying: 'If the second pays... etc.' - A mukatab making his own slave a mukatab is permissible as has been known above. Now there are three scenarios: The second mukatab (mukatab al-mukatab) will pay his kitabah (a) before the first mukatab's payment, (b) after it, or (c) simultaneously. In the first and third scenarios, the wala' of the second mukatab goes to the master of the first mukatab. This is because the master has a kind of ownership in the second mukatab. Meaning: the second mukatab, through the first mukatab, is the master's mukatab, so for the first, the master's kitabah is like a cause of the cause. (This is the reason that if the first mukatab becomes unable to pay, the second mukatab also becomes the master's property.) Also, attribution of emancipation to the master is valid in a general sense. Thus they speak metaphorically: 'The master is the emancipator of Zayd' even though he is (only) the emancipator of his emancipator. This is the reason that if someone makes a will for the mawali of so-and-so, while among the living there is no emancipator of so-and-so, but there is an emancipator of his emancipator, then the will is owed to him. Then, because attribution of freeing the second mukatab to the first mukatab is impossible since he is still a slave, the attribution of emancipation is made to his master. Because just as a ruling is attributed to its cause, it is also attributed to the cause of the cause when attribution to the cause becomes impossible. Like when a ma'dhun slave buys something, ownership is established for his master, because the ma'dhun slave lacks capacity for ownership, even though the actual buyer is the ma'dhun slave. In any case, since the first mukatab is still a slave and lacks capacity for wala', the wala' goes to his master. His saying: 'If the first pays... etc.' - Then, after the master receives the wala' of the second mukatab, if the first mukatab pays his kitabah and becomes free, the wala' of his mukatab does not transfer to him. Because the master has become established as the emancipator, and wala' does not transfer from the emancipator. Because here the master is in one sense the direct emancipator, unlike the case of jar al-wala' where the master of the slave girl is not the direct emancipator of the child, but is indirectly an emancipator through the emancipation of the mother. The general principle in this matter is that attribution of a ruling to a cause is done only when attribution to the cause is impossible. And in the matter of jar al-wala', the impossibility remains until the father becomes free; when he becomes free, the need ends. Therefore, the wala' transfers to the father. And if the second mukatab pays his kitabah after the first mukatab becomes free (by paying his kitabah) and is freed, then his wala' goes to the first mukatab. Because now he has capacity for wala', and the original mukatab is he, so the wala' also goes to him.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on a mukatab (a slave who has contracted to earn his freedom) making his own slave a mukatab (mukatab al-mukatab). The commentator explains that this is permissible. He then discusses three possible timings for the second mukatab's payment relative to the first's. In the first and third scenarios (before or simultaneously), the wala' (patronage) of the second mukatab goes to the master of the first mukatab. The reason is that the master has an indirect ownership interest in the second mukatab through the first. The commentator draws an analogy to a ma'dhun slave (authorized to trade): when he buys something, ownership goes to his master. Similarly, since the first mukatab is still a slave, he cannot hold wala', so it goes to the master. If the first mukatab later becomes free, the wala' does not transfer to him because the master is already established as the direct emancipator. However, if the second mukatab pays his kitabah after the first becomes free, then the wala' goes to the first mukatab because he now has the capacity to hold wala'. A key principle is that a ruling is attributed to the cause, or to the cause of the cause when direct attribution is impossible.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitabah contract with his master, agreeing to pay a sum in installments in exchange for eventual freedom.
ولاء (wala'): The right of patronage or legal bond that attaches to the emancipator after freeing a slave, giving inheritance rights and other ties.
عبد ماذون (abd ma'dhun): A slave authorized by his master to engage in trade and commercial transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mukatab makes his own slave a mukatab (mukatab al-mukatab) and the second mukatab pays his kitabah before the first mukatab finishes paying, who receives the wala' of the second mukatab?
A) The first mukatab (the direct emancipator)
B) The master of the first mukatab
C) The second mukatab himself
D) No one receives wala'

Key Takeaway
A mukatab can make his slave a mukatab, but the wala' of that slave belongs to the original master until the first mukatab becomes free and gains capacity.

Prohibited Actions for a Mukatab Regarding His Slave and Father/Guardian Authority
Lists and explains three invalid actions by a mukatab regarding his slave, then analogizes father/guardian.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited actions for a mukatab regarding his slave, explain the reasoning based on kasb, and apply the same rule to the father/guardian of a minor.

Core Idea
A mukatab cannot free, sell, or marry his slave because these are not earnings; he can marry the slave-girl because mahr is earning.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the limits of a mukatab's authority over his own slave. While the mukatab is required to earn to pay for his freedom, certain actions are prohibited because they are not forms of earning and harm his financial capacity. The same reasoning extends to a father or guardian over a minor's property, highlighting the Islamic principle of wilayat nazari (guardianship based on benefit).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited actions
List the three actions declared 'ghayr ja'iz': itaq 'ala mal (freeing for money), bai' min nafsih (selling to self), and tazwij al-'abd (marrying the male slave).
2
Understand the reasoning for each prohibition
For each action, note why it is not kasb: freeing for money is like loss without compensation; selling to self is disguised freeing; marrying the male slave burdens him and reduces earnings.
The key concept is 'kasb' (earnings) and its accessories.
3
Distinguish the permissible action
Marrying off a female slave (umm al-walad or purchased) is permissible because mahr is a form of earning for the mukatab.
The mahr becomes part of the mukatab's earnings used to pay kitabah.
4
Extend the ruling to father/guardian
The father and guardian have the same authority over the minor's slaves as the mukatab over his own, because they own the power of earning (kasb) and their guardianship is based on benefit (wilayat nazari).
Thus they can make the slave a mukatab and marry the slave-girl, but not the three prohibited actions.

Source Text

مکاتب نے اپنے غلام کو مال پر آزاد کیا یا اس کو اسی کے ہاتھ بیچ دیا یا اپنے غلام کو بیاہ دیا تو یہ جائز نہیں
قال و ان اعتق عبده على مال او باعه من نفسه او زوج عبده لم يجز لان هذه الاشياء ليست من الكسب ولا من توابعه اما الاول فلانه اسقاط الملك عن رقبته واثبات الدين في ذمة المفلس فاشبه الزوال بغير عوض وكذا الثاني لانه اعتاق على مال فى الحقيقة واما الثالث فلانه تنقيص للعبد وتعييب له وشغل رقبته بالمهر والنفقة بخلاف تزويج الامة لانه اكتساب لاستفادته المهر على مامر قال وكذلك الاب والوصى في رقيق لة المكاتب لانهما يملكان الاكتساب كالمكاتب ولان فى تزويج الامة والكتابة نظرا له ولا النظر فيما سواهما والولاية نظرية
ترجمہ اگر مکاتب نے اپنے غلام کو مال پر آزاد کیا یا اس کو اسی کے ہاتھ بیچ ڈالا یا اپنے غلام کو بیاہ دیا تو یہ جائز نہیں ۔ کیونکہ یہ چیزیں نہ کمائی سے ہیں نہ اس کے توابع میں سے ہیں۔ بہر حال اول سو اس لئے کہ یہ اس کی گردن سے ملک زائل کرنا اور مفلس کے ذمہ قرضہ ثابت کرنا ہے تو یہ بلاعوض زائل کرنے کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ اسی طرح ثانی ہے کیونکہ یہ در حقیقت مال پر آزاد کرنا ہے۔ رہا ثالث سو اس لئے کہ یہ غلام کو ناقص و عیب دار کرنا اور اس کی گردن کو مہر ونفقہ میں پھنسانا ہے بخلاف تزویج امتہ کے کہ یہ اکتساب ہے اسکے ذریعہ مہر حاصل کرنے کی وجہ سے جیسا کہ گذر چکا۔ اسی طرح باپ اور وصی صغیر کے مملوک میں بمنزلہ مکاتب کے ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ دونوں اکتساب کے مالک ہیں مکاتب کی طرح اور اس لئے کہ باندی کی تزویج اور مکاتب کرنے میں صغیر کے لئے بہتری ہے اور اس کے ماسوا میں کوئی بہتری نہیں حالانکہ باپ اور وصی کی ولایت نظری ہے۔ تشریح قوله وان اعتق الخ - اگر مکاتب نے اپنے نظام کو مال پر آزاد کہا اسکے ربہ کاری کے ہاتھ فروخت کیا کسی عورت کے ساتھ اس کا نکاح کر دیا تو یہ امور چونکہ نہ کسب و کمائی ہیں نہ توابع کسب اس لئے جائز نہ ہوں گے۔ ۔تو اس لئے جائز نہیں کہ یہ اس غلام کے رقبہ سے اپنی ملک زائل کرنا اور ایک مفلس و نادار کے ذمہ اپنا قرض ثابت کرنا ہے تو گویا اس نے مفت آزاد کر دیا۔ -۲- اس لئے جائز نہیں کہ یہ بظاہر گویج ہے لیکن در حقیقت اعتاق بر مال ہے اور مکاتب کے لئے اعتاق کی اجازت نہیں۔ -۳۔ اس لئے جائز نہیں کہ اس صورت میں غلام کو ناقص و عیب دار کرنا اور اس کو عورت کے مہر اور نان نفقہ میں پھانس کر اپنی مالیست خراب کرنا ہے۔ ہاں اگر اپنی کمائی کی باندی کا نکاح کیا تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ بھی کمائی کا ایک طریقہ ہے کہ اس کے ذریعہ سے اس کو مہر حاصل ہوگا۔ قوله و کذالک الاب.... الخ - احناف اور امام مالک واحمد کے نزدیک باپ اور وصی کو صبی صغیر کے مملوک کے حق میں وہی اختیارات حاصل ہیں جو مکاتب کو اپنی کمائی کے غلام میں حاصل ہیں اور جن امور کا اختیار مکاتب کو اپنے غلام کے بارے میں نہیں ہے ان کا اختیار باپ اور وحی کو بھی نہیں ہے۔ پس باپ اور وصی صغیر کے غلام کو مکاتب اور اس کی باندی کا نکاح کر سکتے ہیں ۔ لیکن اس کے غلام کا نکاح یا خود اس کے ہاتھ فروخت یا مال کے عوض آزاد نہیں کر سکتے ۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ مکاتب کی طرح باپ اور وھی بھی اکتساب کے مالک ہیں ۔ نیز اس لئے بھی کہ باندی کا نکاح کرنے اور اس کے مملوک کو مکاتب کرنے میں صغیر کی بہتری ہے اور اس کے ماسوا میں کوئی بہتری نہیں ہے اور باپ اور وصی کی ولایت چونکہ نظری ہے اس لئے جو کام بچہ کے حق میں بہتر ہو وہی جائز ہوگا۔
If a mukatab frees his slave for money, or sells him to himself, or marries off his slave, then this is not permissible. He said: And if he frees his slave for money, or sells him to himself, or marries his slave, it is not permissible, because these things are not from earning nor from its accessories. As for the first, because it is removing ownership from his person and establishing a debt on the person of an insolvent, so it resembles loss without compensation. Similarly the second, because it is in reality freeing for money. As for the third, because it is diminishing the slave, causing a defect in him, and burdening his person with mahr and maintenance, unlike marrying off a slave-girl, because it is earning since he obtains the mahr by it, as has passed. He said: Similarly the father and the guardian over the minor's property are like the mukatab, because they both own the power of earning like the mukatab, and because in marrying off the slave-girl and making a mukatab there is benefit for him, and there is no benefit in other than these, and the guardianship is based on consideration. Translation: If a mukatab frees his slave for money, or sells him to himself, or marries his slave, then this is not permissible. Because these things are not from earning nor from its accessories. In any case, the first is because it is removing ownership from his person and establishing a debt on the person of an insolvent, so it resembles loss without compensation. Similarly the second, because it is in reality freeing for money. As for the third, because it is diminishing the slave, causing a defect in him, and burdening his person with mahr and maintenance, unlike marrying off a slave-girl, because it is earning since he obtains the mahr by it, as has passed. Similarly the father and the guardian over the minor's property are like the mukatab, because they both own the power of earning like the mukatab, and because in marrying off the slave-girl and making a mukatab there is benefit for him, and there is no benefit in other than these, and the guardianship is based on consideration. Elaboration of his saying: If he frees, etc. - If a mukatab frees his slave for money, or sells him to himself, or marries him to a woman, then these matters are not permissible because they are neither earning nor accessories of earning. The first is not permissible because it is removing ownership from the slave and establishing a debt on the person of an insolvent, so it is as if he freed him for free. The second is not permissible because it is outwardly a sale but in reality freeing for money, and a mukatab is not permitted to free. The third is not permissible because in that situation he is diminishing the slave and causing a defect, and trapping him in the woman's mahr and maintenance, thereby ruining his own financial strength. Yes, if he marries off his own earned slave-girl, it is permissible because this is also a way of earning through which he will obtain mahr. His saying: Similarly the father, etc. - According to the Hanafis and Imam Malik and Ahmad, the father and guardian have the same powers over the property of a minor as the mukatab has over his earned slave. And those matters over which the mukatab has no authority over his slave, the father and guardian also have no authority. So the father and guardian can make the minor's slave a mukatab and marry off his slave-girl. But they cannot marry off his male slave, nor sell him to himself, nor free him for money. The reason is that the father and guardian, like the mukatab, own the power of earning. Also because marrying off the slave-girl and making the slave a mukatab is beneficial for the minor, and there is no benefit in other than these, and the guardianship of the father and guardian is based on consideration, so only what is beneficial for the child is permissible.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, stating three actions a mukatab (a slave contracted for freedom) cannot perform regarding his own slave: (1) freeing him for money, (2) selling him to himself, and (3) marrying him off. These are invalid because they are not forms of earning (kasb) nor its accessories. The first is like giving away property without compensation, as the slave cannot pay. The second is actually a disguised freeing for money, which a mukatab cannot do. The third harms the slave by burdening him with mahr and maintenance. However, marrying off a female slave (umm al-walad or a purchased slave-girl) is permissible because it brings mahr, which is a form of earning. The text then extends the same ruling to a father or guardian of a minor: they have the same authority over the minor's slaves as a mukatab over his own earned slaves. They can make the slave a mukatab and marry off the slave-girl, but cannot do the three prohibited actions. This is because both have the capacity for earning, and their guardianship is based on the minor's benefit (wilayat nazari).

Key Terms
اعتاق على مال (itaq 'ala mal): Freeing a slave in exchange for a payment, effectively a sale of freedom.
تزویج (tazwij): Marriage contract; here refers to the mukatab arranging the marriage of his slave or slave-girl.
ولایت نظری (wilayat nazari): Guardianship based on consideration of benefit (maslahah), as opposed to absolute authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following actions by a mukatab regarding his slave is permissible according to the text?
A) Freeing the slave in exchange for a payment
B) Selling the slave to the slave himself
C) Marrying off his female slave
D) Marrying off his male slave

Key Takeaway
A mukatab's authority over his slave is limited to earning actions; the father/guardian has the same limitation due to wilayat nazari.

intermediate

Mukatab's Limited Authority Over His Slave
States three prohibited acts for a mukatab and extends the ruling to father/guardian.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited acts for a mukatab and explain why they are invalid based on the principle of kasb, and apply the same reasoning to the father/guardian.

Core Idea
A mukatab's authority is limited to his kasb; acts beyond it are invalid.

A mukatab is a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom. He owns his earnings (kasb) and can trade, but his ownership is not absolute. This lesson examines three acts he cannot perform regarding his own slave: freeing him for payment, selling him to himself, and marrying him off. The same restrictions apply to a father or guardian acting for a minor, based on the principle of welfare-based guardianship (wilayah nazariyyah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited acts
From the passage, list the acts a mukatab cannot do: (1) freeing his slave for a payment, (2) selling the slave to himself, (3) marrying his male slave to a woman.
Note that marrying his female slave is allowed because it is a means of earning.
2
Understand the unifying principle: not from kasb
All three acts are invalid because they are not from the mukatab's kasb (earnings) nor its appendages. The mukatab only owns what he acquires through trade or labor; these acts remove value or create obligations without commensurate benefit in his earning framework.
3
Analyze each act's specific reasoning
For freeing for payment: it removes ownership and puts a debt on an insolvent person, resembling gratuitous manumission. For selling to himself: it is effectively manumission for consideration, which is not permitted. For marrying a male slave: it reduces the slave's value and encumbers him with mahr and maintenance, harming the mukatab's wealth.
The reasoning is talil (cause-based) and each act is measured against the concept of kasb.
4
Extend the ruling to father and guardian
The same three acts are prohibited for a father or guardian (wasi) regarding the minor's slave. They have authority similar to the mukatab's: they own acquisition like the mukatab (they can manage the minor's property for benefit), but their guardianship is based on consideration (wilayah nazariyyah). Only acts beneficial to the minor are allowed: marrying the female slave and making the slave a mukatab. The three prohibited acts are not beneficial and thus invalid.
Imam Malik and Ahmad agree on this extension.
5
Apply the principle to new scenarios
If a mukatab or guardian attempts any act that is not clearly part of the earning stream and not beneficial, it is invalid. For example, a guardian cannot free the minor's slave for payment or sell the slave to himself.

Source Text

Book of the Mukatab. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidaya, Vol 12. From its appendages: As for the first, because it is removal of ownership from his person and establishing a debt in the liability of the insolvent, so it resembles removal without compensation. Similarly the second, because it is really manumission for consideration. As for the third, because it is a reduction and defect of the slave and occupying his person with mahr and maintenance, unlike marrying the female slave because it is acquisition to obtain the mahr as previously mentioned. He said: Similarly the father and guardian regarding the minor's slave like the mukatab, because they own acquisition like the mukatab, and because in marrying the female slave and kitabah there is benefit for him, and there is no benefit in other than these, and their guardianship is based on consideration. Translation: If a mukatab frees his slave for consideration, or sells him to himself, or marries his slave, it is not permissible. Because these things are not from his earning nor from its appendages. In any case, the first is because it removes ownership from his person and establishes a debt on the insolvent, so it resembles removal without compensation. Similarly the second, because it is in reality manumission for consideration. As for the third, because it is making the slave deficient and defective and entangling his person with mahr and maintenance, unlike marrying his female slave because it is acquisition through which he obtains mahr as passed. Similarly, the father and guardian in the minor's property are like the mukatab. Because both own acquisition like the mukatab, and because in marrying the female slave and making the mukatab there is benefit for the minor, and in other than these there is no benefit, while the father and guardian's guardianship is based on consideration. Explanation: His statement 'And if he frees...' - If a mukatab frees his slave for consideration, sells him to his master, or marries him to a woman, these acts are not permissible because they are not from his earning nor from its appendages. It is not permissible because it is removing ownership from the slave's person and establishing his debt on an insolvent person, so he has freed him for free. -2 It is not permissible because it is outwardly a sale but in reality manumission for consideration, and the mukatab is not permitted manumission. -3 It is not permissible because in this case he makes the slave deficient and defective and entangles him in the woman's mahr and maintenance, ruining his own wealth. Yes, if he marries his female slave from his earning, it is permissible because it is also a means of earning through which he obtains mahr. His statement: 'Similarly the father...' - According to the Hanafis and Imam Malik and Ahmad, the father and guardian have the same powers over the minor's property as the mukatab has over his own earning slave, and the acts which the mukatab does not have authority over, the father and guardian also do not have authority. So the father and guardian can make the minor's slave a mukatab and marry his female slave. But they cannot marry his male slave, or sell him to himself, or free him for consideration. The reason is that like the mukatab, the father and guardian own acquisition. Also, because marrying the female slave and making the mukatab brings benefit to the minor, and there is no benefit in other than these, and the father and guardian's guardianship is based on consideration, so only what is beneficial for the child is permissible.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on the mukatab. It first states three acts that are not permissible for a mukatab regarding his own slave: freeing the slave in exchange for payment, selling the slave to himself, and marrying the slave (male) to a woman. The text provides the reasoning: these acts are not part of the mukatab's 'kasb' (earning) nor its appendages. Freeing the slave removes ownership and creates a debt on an insolvent person, resembling gratuitous manumission which a mukatab cannot do. Selling to oneself is effectively manumission for consideration, also prohibited. Marrying a slave diminishes his value and encumbers him with obligations. However, marrying off his female slave is allowed because it is a means of earning through the mahr. The text then extends the same ruling to a father or guardian (wasi) acting for a minor. They have the same limited authority as a mukatab over the minor's slaves: they can make the slave a mukatab and marry the minor's amah (female slave) because these are beneficial, but they cannot perform the three prohibited acts since those are not beneficial. The basis is that both the father and guardian have 'wilayah nazariyyah' (guardianship based on consideration), so they may only do what is in the minor's interest. The commentary elaborates on each point, emphasizing that the mukatab's ownership is restricted to what is acquired through his earning, and any act outside that scope is invalid.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has made a contract of manumission (kitabah) with his master, agreeing to pay a sum in exchange for freedom; he retains limited ownership over his earnings.
كسب (kasb): Earning or acquisition through trade, labor, or similar efforts; the source of the mukatab's permissible wealth.
ولاية نظرية (wilāyah naẓariyyah): Guardianship based on consideration of benefit (maslahah); the guardian (father/wasi) may only act in the minor's best interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a mukatab not allowed to sell his slave to the slave himself?
A) Because the sale is invalid without witnesses
B) Because it is essentially manumission for consideration, which is not from his kasb
C) Because the slave cannot own property
D) Because the mukatab lacks the legal capacity to sell

Key Takeaway
A mukatab's authority over his slave is limited to acts that fall within his kasb; any act that diminishes value or encumbers without kasb benefit is invalid, and the same limitation applies to a father/guardian based on welfare.

Ma'dhun Cannot Marry His Amah: The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the limits of a ma'dhun's authority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa and Muhammad forbid a ma'dhun from marrying his amah, and evaluate Abu Yusuf's counter-argument via analogical reasoning.

Core Idea
A ma'dhun's authority is limited to trade; marriage is not trade, so he cannot marry his amah.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about the limits of a ma'dhun's (slave permitted to trade) authority. While Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the ma'dhun cannot marry his own female slave, Abu Yusuf dissents, drawing analogies to the mukatab and ijarah. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply the principle that permission is restricted to its explicit scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed act
The disagreement is over whether a ma'dhun (slave granted permission to trade) can marry his own female slave (amah).
The same dispute extends to mudarib, mufawid, and sharik 'inan.
2
State the majority position
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the ma'dhun cannot marry his amah. The act is invalid (batil).
The ma'dhun's permission is limited to trade only.
3
Identify Abu Yusuf's exception
Abu Yusuf holds that the ma'dhun may marry his amah. He uses qiyas: ma'dhun is like mukatab (who can marry), and marriage is like ijarah.
4
Analyze the majority rebuttal
The majority distinguishes: the mukatab owns kasb (earning), and marriage is kasb; the ma'dhun owns trade, and marriage is not trade. Also, marriage is mubadala bil-mal bi-ghayr al-mal (exchange of property for non-property), akin to kitabah, not ijarah.
This rebuttal refines the illa of the qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If a ma'dhun marries his amah, the marriage is valid according to Abu Yusuf but invalid according to the majority, affecting the status of the marriage and children.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فاما الماذون له فلا يجوز له شيء من ذلك عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابو يوسف له ان يزوج امته وعلى هذا الخلاف المضارب والمفاوض والشريك شركة عنان هو قاسه على المكاتب واعتبره بالاجارة ولهما ان الماذون له يملك التجارة وهذا ليس بتجارة فاما المكاتب يملك الاكتساب وهذا اكتساب ولانه مبادلة المال بغير المال فيعتبر بالكتابة دون الاجارة اذ هى مبادلة المال بالمال ولهذا لا يملك هؤلاء كلهم تزويج العبد
ترجمہ رہاوہ غلام جس کو تجارت کی اجازت دی گئی ہو تو اس کو جائز نہیں کوئی چیز ان میں سے طرفین کے نزدیک اور امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کو باندی کے نکاح کرنے کا اختیار ہے اور اسی اختلاف پر ہے۔ مضارب مفاوض اور شرکت عنان کا شریک انہوں نے مازون کو مکاتب پر اور تزویج کو اجارہ پر قیاس کیا ہے۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عبد ماذون تجارت کا مالک ہوتا ہے۔اور یہ تجارت نہیں ہے رہا مکاتب سودہ اکتساب کا مالک ہوتا ہے اور یہ کتاب ہے اور اس لئے کہ نکاح مبادلہ مال بلا مال ہے تو اس کو کتابت پر قیاس کیا جائے گا نہ کہ اجارہ پر کیونکہ اجارہ مبادلہ مال بالمال ہے۔ اسی لئے یہ سب لوگ غلام کا نکاح کرنے کے مجاز نہیں ہیں۔ تشریح قوله فاما الماذون .. الخ - طرفین کے نزدیک عہد ماذون امور مذکورہ میں سے کسی امر کا مجاز نہیں ہے۔ یعنی نہ وہ تجارت کے غلام کو مال پر آزاد کر سکتا ہے نہ اس کا نکاح کر سکتا ہے نہ غلام کو اسی کے ہاتھ فروخت کر سکتا ہے نہ تجارتی باندی کی شادی کر سکتا ہے البتہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ترویج امنہ کا اختیار ہے۔
صاحب نہا یہ نے لکھا ہے کہ اس باب میں اصل یہ ہے کہ ہر وہ شخص جس کا تصرف تجارت وغیرہ سب میں عام ہو وہ باندی کا نکاح کر سکتا ہے۔ جیسے باپ، دادا، وصی شریک مفاوض مکاتب ، قاضی اور اس کا امین اور ہر وہ شخص جس کا تصرف تجارت میں خاص ہو وہ طرفین کے نزدیک باندی کا نکاح نہیں کر سکتا۔ جسے مضارب، شریک عنان ، عبد مازون، قاضی خاں اور شیخ محبوبی نے ایسا ہی ذکر کیا ہے۔ قوله شئ من ذلك ... الخ ۔ اس پر یہ اشکال ہوتا ہے کہ ذالک کا مشار الیہ اگر نخاص طور سے اعتناق : مال، غلام کو اسکے ہاتھ فروخت کرنا یا اس کی شادی کرنا ہو جو اس مسئلہ سے پیشتر مذکور ہے۔ وان اعتق عبده على مال او باعه من نفسه اوزوج عبده لم يجز" تب تو وقال ابو يوسف له ان يزوج امة “ کہنا اس کے منافی ہے۔ کیونکہ اشیاء ثلاثہ مذکورہ میں ترویج امتر داخل ہی نہیں۔ پس امام ابو یوسف کا اختلاف ذکر کرنا بے معنی ہوا۔ اور اگر ذلک کا مشار الیہ تمام امور ہوں جو اس باب میں مذکور ہیں تو اس پر یہ اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ خرید و فروخت جیسے مکاتب کے لئے جائز ہے۔ ایسے ہی عبد ماذون کے لئے بھی قطعا جائز ہے۔ پس فلا یجوز لہ شی من ذلک ساب کلی بے معنی ہوا۔ قوله و المفاوض .. الخ - بقول شیخ کا کی یہاں لفظ مفاوض سہوا کا تب سے لکھا گیا ہے کیونکہ مفاوض تو بمنزلہ مکاتب ہے۔ علامہ انزاری کہتے ہیں کہ مفاوض کو بالاتفاق تزویج امتہ کا اختیار ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ امام کرخی نے اپنی مختصر کے باب المفاوضہ میں تصریح کی ہے: ويجوز لا حد المفا وضين ان يكاتب عبيد التجارة ويأذن لهم فى التجارة ولا يجوزان يعتق شيئا
He said: As for the ma'dhun (slave permitted to trade), nothing of that is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He may marry his female slave. The same difference applies to the mudarib, mufawid, and partner in 'inan company. He (Abu Yusuf) analogized him to the mukatab and considered marriage to ijarah. The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) said: The ma'dhun owns trade, and this is not trade. As for the mukatab, he owns earning (kasb), and this is earning. And because marriage is an exchange of property for non-property, so it is considered by kitabah (manumission contract) not ijarah, since ijarah is an exchange of property for property. Therefore, all of these do not have the authority to marry a male slave. Translation: As for the slave who has been permitted to trade, nothing of these things is permissible according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Imam Abu Yusuf says he has the authority to marry his female slave. The same difference applies to the mudarib, mufawid, and partner in 'inan company. He (Abu Yusuf) analogized the ma'dhun to the mukatab and considered marriage to ijarah. The proof of the two is that the ma'dhun owns trade, and this is not trade. As for the mukatab, he owns earning, and this (marriage) is earning. And because marriage is an exchange of property for non-property, so it is analogized to kitabah not ijarah, because ijarah is exchange of property for property. Therefore, all of these are not authorized to marry a male slave. Explanation: According to the two, the ma'dhun is not authorized in any of the mentioned matters. That is, he cannot free his commercial slave for consideration, marry him, sell him to himself, or marry his commercial female slave. However, according to Abu Yusuf, he has the authority to marry the female slave. The author of al-Nihayah wrote that the principle in this chapter is that anyone whose disposition is general in trade and other things can marry the female slave, like father, grandfather, wasi, mufawid partner, mukatab, qadi and his amin. And anyone whose disposition is specific to trade cannot marry the female slave according to the two, such as mudarib, 'inan partner, and ma'dhun slave. Qadi Khan and Shaikh Mahbubi mentioned likewise. As for his statement 'shay'un min dhalik', there is a problem: if the referent of 'dhalik' specifically refers to the three acts mentioned before this issue (freeing for consideration, selling to himself, marrying his slave) then saying 'Abu Yusuf said he may marry his female slave' contradicts because marrying the female slave is not among those three. So mentioning Abu Yusuf's difference becomes meaningless. And if the referent is all matters mentioned in this chapter, then it is objected that buying and selling, which are permissible for the mukatab, are definitely permissible for the ma'dhun. So saying 'he may not do anything from that' as a general statement becomes meaningless. As for his statement 'and the mufawid' – by the words of the Shaykh, the word 'mufawid' here was written erroneously from the copy, because the mufawid is like a mukatab. Allamah al-Ansari says that the mufawid has, by consensus, the authority to marry his female slave. Thus Imam al-Karkhi stated in his Mukhtasar in the chapter of mufawadah: 'It is permissible for one of the mufawidayn to make commercial slaves mukatab and to permit them to trade, but it is not permissible for him to free anything...'
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ma'dhun (a slave granted permission to trade). According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, a ma'dhun cannot perform any of the three acts (freeing for consideration, selling to himself, or marrying his slave), nor can he marry his female slave. Abu Yusuf disagrees: he holds that the ma'dhun may marry his female slave. The disagreement extends to the mudarib (trading partner), the mufawid (unrestricted partner), and the sharik 'inan (limited partner). Abu Yusuf draws an analogy between the ma'dhun and the mukatab, and considers marriage analogous to ijarah (lease). The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) reject this: the ma'dhun's authority is limited to trade (tijarah), and marriage is not trade. In contrast, the mukatab's authority is kasb (earning), and marriage is a form of earning. Moreover, marriage is an exchange of property (mahr) for non-property (the woman's right to intimacy), so it is more like kitabah (a contract of manumission involving payment) than ijarah (which exchanges property for property). The commentary from Nihayah states a general principle: anyone whose disposition is general (e.g., father, mukatab) can marry the amah; anyone whose disposition is restricted to trade (e.g., ma'dhun) cannot, according to the majority. The text also notes a potential textual contradiction regarding the phrase 'shay'un min dhalik' and corrects that the word 'mufawid' may be a scribal error, as the mufawid by consensus can marry the amah.

Key Terms
مأذون (ma'dhūn): A slave who has been granted permission by his master to engage in trade; his authority is limited to commercial transactions.
مضارب (muḍārib): A person who enters into a mudarabah partnership, where one provides capital and the other labor; subject to the same difference.
مفاوض (mufāwiḍ): A partner in a mufawadah company, which is an unrestricted partnership; by consensus can marry his amah.
شريك عنان (sharīk 'inān): A partner in a limited partnership ('inan), where each partner contributes capital but the partnership is restricted; follows the ruling of ma'dhun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, why can't a ma'dhun marry his amah?
A) Because the amah is not his property
B) Because marriage is not considered trade, and the ma'dhun only owns trade
C) Because the ma'dhun needs his master's permission for marriage
D) Because marriage is akin to ijarah, which the ma'dhun cannot do

Key Takeaway
A ma'dhun's permission to trade does not extend to marrying his female slave; this ruling hinges on the distinction between trade (tijarah) and earning (kasb).

Abu Yusuf's Qiyas on the Ma'dhun's Marriage Authority and the Pair's Rebuttal
Presents Abu Yusuf's analogy, an objection, and the pair's counter-argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Abu Yusuf's qiyas for the ma'dhun's marriage authority, identify the objections, and state the mufta bihi Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Marriage is not trade; the ma'dhun's permission for trade does not extend to marriage.

Imam Abu Yusuf analogized the ma'dhun slave to a mukatab and marriage to ijarah to permit marrying off a female slave. But the pair (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rejected this, arguing that marriage is not an exchange of property – the vulva is not property – and the ma'dhun is only authorized for trade. This lesson unpacks the analogies, the objections, and the reliance on the pair's view as the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling under dispute
Determine the precise act: a ma'dhun slave marrying off his master's female slave. Abu Yusuf says it is permissible; Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it is not.
2
Analyze Abu Yusuf's first analogy (mukatab)
Abu Yusuf argues: just as a mukatab can marry off his own female slave, so can a ma'dhun, because both have removal of restriction (raf' al-hajr) and general discretion (itlaq al-tasarruf).
The 'illa (effective cause) is the removal of restriction.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's second analogy (ijarah)
He also analogizes marriage to ijarah: both transfer a benefit for a consideration. Since the ma'dhun can hire out slaves, he should be able to marry them off.
This analogy treats marriage as a financial exchange.
4
Examine the objections to the qiyas
The author of Nata'ij objects that the qiyas leads to contradictions (e.g., writing kitabah for his own slave, which is invalid). The pair object on the basis that marriage is not trade and the vulva is not property.
The pair's objection rests on the definition of trade (mubadala mal bil mal).
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The pair's view is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school: a ma'dhun slave cannot marry off his master's female slave, because marriage is not considered a financial transaction within his permission.
This is an example of preferring a broader principle (marriage ≠ trade) over a narrow qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تنبیہ امام ابویوسف کی مذکورہ قیاسی دلیل پر صاحب نتائج نے یہ اعتراض کیا ہے کہ یہ دونوں قیاس محل نظر ہیں۔ قیاس اول تو اسلئے کہ اگر تزویج امتہ میں مازون لہ کو مکاتب پر قیاس کرنا صحیح ہو تو اپنے غلام کو مکاتب کرنے میں بھی ماذون لہ کا قیاس مکاتب پر صحیح ہونا چاہئے کہ مکاتب کیلئے اپنے غلام کو مکاتب کرنا جائز ہے تو بطریق قیاس مازون لہ کیلئے بھی مکاتب کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ حالانکہ ماذون لہ کیلئے اپنے غلام کو مکاتب کرنا بالاتفاق نا جائز ہے۔ قیاس ثانی اسلئے محل نظر ہے کہ اگر تزویج کو اجارہ پر قیاس کرنا تام ہو جائیں معنی کہ ماذون لہ کیلئے اپنے غلام اور باندی کو اجارہ پر دینا جائز ہے۔ پس تزویج بھی جائز ہو گی تو اس قیاس کی رو سے لازم آئے گا کہ ماذون کیلئے اپنے غلام کی ترویج بھی جائز ہو ۔ حالانکہ ماذون کیلئے یہ بالا جماع نا جائز ہے۔
فائدہ صاحب ہدایہ نے عینین یعنی مازون و مکاتب کی جانب میں لفظ قیاس استعمال کیا ہے اور فعلین یعنی ترویج و اجارہ کی جانب میں لفظ اعتبار استعمال کیا ہے۔ صاحب نہایہ نے اس کا نکتہ یہ بیان کیا جسے بین العینین مماثلت چونکہ بالکل ظاہر ہے۔ بایں معنی کہ ان دونوں میں فتِ حجر ( رکاوٹ اٹھا دینا ) اور اطلاق تصرف ہے تو شرط قیاس پائی گئی اس لئے ان میں لفظ قیاس استعمال کیا ہے۔ بخلاف مذکورہ فعلین کے کہ ان میں مماثلت صرف فعلیت کے لحاظ سے ہے۔ کیونکہ اجارہ جانبہین سے معاوضات مالیہ میں سے ہے تو یہاں لفظ اعتبار کا استعمال ہی لائق تر ہے۔ رہا صاحب عنایہ کا قیاس و اعتبار کے درمیان ترادف کا دعوئی سو یہ غیر ظاہر او محتاج برہان ہے۔
قوله ولهمان ان الماذون .. الخ - طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عبد مازون کو تجارت کا اختیار ہے اور ترویج امتہ تجارت میں سے نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ تزویج مبادلہ مال بالمال نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ بضع حقیقت میں مال نہیں ہے۔ حالانکہ تجارت مبادلہ مال بالمال کو کہتے ہیں۔ رہا مکاتب سو وہ اکتساب کا مالک ہوتا ہے اور تزویج متر بھی اکتساب کا ایک طریقہ ہے اس لئے کہ اکتساب اس کو کہتے ہیں جس کے ذریعہ سے مال تک رسائی ہو اور یہ بات تزویج امتہ میں موجود ہے کہ اس کے ذریعہ سے مہر تک رسائی ہوتی ہے۔
قوله ولا نه مبادلة المال .... الخ ۔ یہ طرفین کی دوسری دلیل ہے کہ تزویج تو مبادلہ بلا مال ہے تو اس کو کتابت پر قیاس کرنا چاہیے ( کہ کتابت بھی ابتداء میں مبادلہ مال بلا مال ہوتی ہے ) نہ کہ اجارہ پر کیونکہ اجارہ مبادلہ مال بالمال ہوتا ہے اس لئے کہ اس میں منفعت عین شی کے قائم مقام ہوتی ہے تو وہ مال کے حکم میں ہوئی ۔ اسی لئے وہ باب نکاح میں مہر ہونے کے قابل ہے۔
His saying: 'He analogized it...' etc. - This is Imam Abu Yusuf's proof. Its explanation is that Imam Abu Yusuf analogized the ma'dhun slave's marriage of a female slave to the mukatab: just as it is permissible for a mukatab to marry off his own female slave, similarly it will be permissible for a ma'dhun slave. Also, he analogized marriage to a hire contract (ijarah): just as it is permissible for the ma'dhun principal to let out his male and female slaves on hire, so too will marrying off a female slave be permissible, because each of them is a transfer of ownership or a transfer of benefit for a consideration. Caution (Tanbih): The author of Nata'ij objected to this qiyas of Imam Abu Yusuf, saying that both analogies are questionable. The first analogy: if it were correct to analogize the ma'dhun slave to a mukatab in marrying off a female slave, then it should also be correct to analogize him to a mukatab in writing a kitabah for his own male slave, because it is permissible for a mukatab to write kitabah for his own male slave, so by analogy it should be permissible for a ma'dhun slave as well. But writing kitabah for his own male slave by a ma'dhun slave is unanimously impermissible. The second analogy is questionable because if marriage is completely analogized to hire, then it would be permissible for a ma'dhun slave to marry off his own male slave as well, but that is unanimously impermissible. Benefit (Fa'idah): The author of Hidayah used the word 'qiyas' for two entities (the ma'dhun and the mukatab), and used the word 'i'tibar' for two actions (tazwij and ijarah). The author of Nihayah explained that the similarity between the two entities is completely apparent, because both involve removal of restriction (hajr) and general discretion, so the condition for qiyas is met, hence 'qiyas' was used. In contrast, for the two actions, the similarity is only in terms of being actions, because ijarah is a financial exchange on both sides, so the use of 'i'tibar' is more appropriate. As for the claim of the author of 'Inayah that qiyas and i'tibar are synonymous, that is not apparent and requires proof. His saying: 'And for them (the two) that the ma'dhun...' - This is the proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): the ma'dhun slave has permission for trade, but marrying off a female slave is not part of trade, because marriage is not an exchange of property for property, since the vulva is not actually property. Trade is an exchange of property for property. As for the mukatab, he is owner of acquisition, and marriage is also a means of acquisition, because acquisition is that by which wealth is accessed, and this is present in marrying off a female slave since through it access to dower (mahr) is achieved. His saying: 'And because it is an exchange of property...' etc. This is the second proof of the two: marriage is an exchange without property, so it should be analogized to kitabah (which is initially an exchange without property), not to ijarah, because ijarah is an exchange of property for property, since benefit stands in place of the thing itself, so it is treated as property. That is why it is fit to be a dower in the chapter of marriage.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This is an expansion of the intra-Hanafi dispute. It presents Abu Yusuf's proof using qiyas: he analogizes the ma'dhun slave to a mukatab (both have permission to acquire) and marriage to ijarah (both involve transfer for a consideration). The author of Nata'ij objects that this leads to inconsistencies: if the analogy stands, the ma'dhun should also be able to write kitabah for his own slave, which is unanimously invalid. Also, the analogy to ijarah would permit marrying off a male slave, also invalid. A fa'idah discusses the author's choice of words. Then the pair (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) respond: marriage is not trade, because the vulva is not property; the ma'dhun is only permitted for trade, not marriage. The mukatab is different because marriage is a form of acquisition (kasb) for him. Also, marriage should be analogized to kitabah (both exchange of non-property for property), not ijarah. This is a classic fit of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Key Terms
مأذون (ma'dhun): A slave who is given permission by his master to engage in trade.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has contracted with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
اجارہ (ijarah): A contract of hire or lease where the owner transfers the benefit (manfa'ah) of an asset for a payment (ujrah).
بضع (bud' / vulva): The female genitalia; legally treated as not being property in the context of trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because tazwij is an exchange of property for property, which is outside his permission
C) Because tazwij is not trade (mubadala mal bil mal) as the vulva is not property
D) Because the ma'dhun slave is owned by another

Key Takeaway
The ma'dhun slave's permission for trade does not include the authority to marry off his master's female slave, because marriage is not a financial transaction.

Mukatab Purchases Father or Son: Subsidiary Entry into Kitabah
Ruling: a mukatab's purchase of father/son includes them in kitabah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a mukatab purchases a direct ancestor or descendant and explain the qiyas (analogy) used to derive it.

Core Idea
A mukatab's purchase of a father or son includes them in his kitabah via taba'iyyah to preserve family ties (silat al-rahim).

This lesson deals with a special scenario in the law of kitabah: what happens when a mukatab (a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom) buys his own father or son? Intuitively, one might think the purchase is invalid because the mukatab cannot directly free a relative. However, Hanafi law uses a qiyas to allow the relative to enter the kitabah as a subsidiary. We will unpack the reasoning and the legal effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
State the act: a mukatab purchases his father or son. The ruling: the relative enters the mukatab's kitabah (becomes a party to the contract as a subsidiary).
The relative is not freed immediately but is included in the kitabah contract.
2
Determine the proof type
The proof is qiyas (analogy). Identify the asl (original case): a free person who owns a relative—they become free upon him. The far' (new case): a mukatab who buys a relative.
The qiyas is jaliy (evident) because the illa is shared.
3
Extract the illa (effective cause)
The illa is the ability to achieve freedom for the relative, even if partially. For the free person, it's full freedom; for the mukatab, it is inclusion in the kitabah, which is a step toward freedom.
The principle of silat al-rahim (maintaining family ties) supports this extension.
4
Apply the ruling to the far'
Since the mukatab cannot fully free, he can still make the relative a mukatab, which is the closest approximation. Thus, the relative enters the kitabah as a subsidiary.
If the mukatab later becomes free, the relative also becomes free.
5
State the practical outcome
The purchase is valid (sahih). The relative is included in the kitabah. If the mukatab frees himself, the relative is also freed. If not, they remain with the master as part of the mukatab's debt.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل قال واذا اشترى المكاتب اباه او ابنه دخل فى كتابته لانه من اهل ان يكاتب وان لم يكن من اهل الاعتاق فيجعل مكاتباً تحقيقاً للصلة بقدر الامكان الاترى ان الحر متى كان يملك الاعتاق يعتق عليه ترجمہ فصل کو اگر خرید لیا مکاتب نے اپنے باپ یا بیٹے کو تو وہ اس کی کتابت میں داخل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ مکاتب کرنے کا اہل ہے۔ اگر چہ آزاد کرنے کا اہل نہیں ہے۔ پس اس کو مکاتب ٹھہرایا جائے گا بقدر امکان صلہ رحمی محقق کرنے کے لئے کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ آزاد آدمی جب اعتناق کا مالک ہو تو وہ اس پر آزاد ہو جاتے ہیں۔ تشریح قوله فصل الخ - جو لوگ کتابت میں بطریق اصالت داخل ہوتے ہیں ان کے مسائل ذکر کرنے کے بعد ان لوگوں کے مسائل ذکر کر رہے ہیں جو کتابت میں بطریق تبعیت داخل ہوتے ہیں۔ لان التبع يتلو الاصل قوله و اذا اشترى .. الخ - اگر مکاتب نے اپنے اصول و فروغ (باپ بیٹے وغیرہ ) کو خرید لیا تو تبعا وہ بھی کتابت میں داخل ہ: جائیں گے۔ پس مکاتب آزاد ہوگا تو وہ بھی آزاد ہو جائیں گے ورنہ مکاتب کے ساتھ آقا کے نام رہیں گے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ مکاتب اگر
A chapter: He said: If a mukatab buys his father or his son, he enters his kitabah, because he (the father/son) is one who can be made a mukatab, even if he is not one who can be freed, so he is made a mukatab to achieve family connection (silah) to the extent possible. Do you not see that when a free person has the right to free, they become free upon him? Commentary: This is a section on those who enter kitabah as subsidiary. He mentioned rulings on those who enter kitabah as principal. Now he mentions those who enter as subsidiary, because the subsidiary follows the principal. His saying: 'If he buys his father or son...' - If a mukatab buys his ascendants or descendants (father, son, etc.), they enter his kitabah as subsidiary. So if the mukatab becomes free, they will also become free; otherwise they will remain with the master along with the mukatab. The reason: If a mukatab... (text cut off).
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from analogy. The mukatab can include his father or son in his kitabah. The proof is that the father/son is eligible to be made a mukatab (he can be a party to a kitabah contract), even though the mukatab cannot directly free him (since he is a relative?). The ruling is based on achieving family ties (silah al-rahim) to the extent possible. The proof is an analogy: just as a free person, if he owns a relative, causes them to be freed automatically (because he can free them), similarly, the mukatab, even though he cannot free, can include them in his kitabah as a subsidiary. This is from the chapter on those who enter kitabah by subsidiary (taba'iyyah). The commentary explains that if the mukatab later becomes free, they become free as well; otherwise they remain as part of the mukatab's debt.

Key Terms
تبعیت (taba'iyyah): Subsidiary inclusion; a person enters a contract not as principal but as a dependent of another.
صلہ رحمی (silat al-rahimi): Maintaining family ties; here used as the reason for allowing the inclusion of relatives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mukatab buys his son, what is the legal effect according to Hanafi law?
A) The son becomes free immediately.
B) The sale is void because the son cannot be a mukatab.
C) The son enters the mukatab's kitabah as a subsidiary.
D) The son remains a slave of the original owner and the purchase is ineffective.

Key Takeaway
A mukatab can include his direct ancestors or descendants in his kitabah as subsidiaries via qiyas, preserving family ties (silat al-rahim) to the extent possible.
